Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
6 min
Evaluating Charges of Heresy: The Case of Taftazani's Imamah
Biographical refutation of sectarian charges against Taftazani

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate accusations of sectarian deviation by analyzing textual evidence and authorial context using Hanafi usul principles.

Core Idea
A single ambiguous term does not prove sectarian allegiance; context and authorial corpus must be examined.

This passage defends Allamah al-Taftazani against allegations of Shi'i leanings. It demonstrates a sound method: when a term like 'imamah' is used, check the author's own clarification and broader works. This lesson walks through the refutation and its methodological principles, showing how to avoid superficial interpretations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the accusation
State the specific textual evidence used to allege Taftazani's Shi'ism. In the first doubt, critics pointed to his inclusion of 'imamah' in the definition of kalam.
The accusation is based on a single term.
2
Examine the refutation
The author argues that 'imamah' in Sunni usage includes khilafah and imarah, not the Shi'i concept of a specific infallible imam. Determine how the refutation reinterprets the term.
The refutation relies on mainstream Sunni definition.
3
Analyze supporting evidence
The author cites Taftazani's own commentary on al-Nasafi's 'Aqa'id, where he explicitly rejects the Shi'i view of imamate. Explain how this internal evidence strengthens the refutation.
Context from author's corpus is key.
4
Evaluate the second doubt
The second doubt concerns a grammatical example using 'Ali and Mu'awiya. The accusation is that this shows sectarian bias. The refutation explains it is purely linguistic. Identify the logical flaw.
Assuming linguistic illustration implies doctrinal stance is flawed.
5
Summarize the methodological lesson
What interpretive principles does this refutation illustrate? Consider Hanafi usul principles such as 'al-ibra bi umum al-lafz la bi khusus al-sabab' and the need to consider authorial context.
Sound scholarship requires holistic evidence.

الترويح لِحَلَّ التَّوْضِيعِ وَالتَّلُويْحِ
علامہ تفتازانی سے متعلق چند شبہات کا ازالہ
55
بعض حضرات نے علامہ تفتازانی کی طرف شیعیت کی نسبت کی ہے اور چند وجوہ سے اس کو ثابت کرنے کی کوشش کی ہے لیکن یہ بات دامن تحقیق سے خالی اور سطحی ذہن کی عکاس ہے ہم ان شاء اللہ ان وجوہ کو ذکر کرنے کے بعد ان کا ازالہ کریں گے
شبہ اولی: یہ ہے کہ علامہ تفتازانی علیہ الرحمۃ نے حاشیہ تکویح میں علم کلام کے بارہ میں گفتگو کرتے ہوئے لکھا ہے کہ مما يشتمل عليه علم الكلام عن احوال الصانع والنبوة والامامة والمعاد ومايتصل بذلك على قانون الاسلام تو لفظ امامہ کو دیکھ کر بعض حضرات نے اعتراض کر دیا کہ شاید علامہ صاحب بھی شیعوں کا عقیدہ امامتہ رکھتے ہیں اور یہاں وہی عقیدہ مراد لے رہے ہیں یہ ان کے شیعہ ہونے کی دلیل ہے۔ الجواب:۔یہ ہے کہ یہ شبہ واعتراض انتہائی سطحی ہے اس کے تو جواب دینے کی ضرورت بھی محسوس نہیں ہوتی اس لئے کہ اہل سنت و الجماعت کے نزدیک امامت کا ایک جنگ مفہوم ہے اور یہ خلافت اور امارت دونوں کو شامل ہے اور ظاہر ہے کہ علامہ نے یہاں امامت سے وہ مفہوم مراد لیا ہے جو اہل سنت و الجماعت کے ہاں معتبر ہے نہ کہ شیعوں کا عقیدہ امامت اور اس کی تائید اس سے بھی ہوتی ہے کہ علامہ نسفی نے اپنی کتاب عقائد نسفیہ میں جب یہ فرمایا کہ ثم ينبغي ان يكون الامام ظاهرا لا مختفيا و لا منتظرا (امام کیلئے مناسب ہے کہ ظاہر ہو چھپا ہوا نہ ہو اور نہ ہی منتظر ہو تو اس کے تحت علامہ تفتازانی فرماتے ہیں کہ لا كنا زعمت الشيعة خصوصاً الأمامية منهم ان الامام الحق بعد رسول الله على ثم ابنه الحسين ثم اخوه الحسن ثم ابنه على زين العابدين رضی اللہ عنہم یعنی امام سے مراد وہ امام نہیں جس کا شیعہ خصوصاً ان میں سے جو فرقہ امامیہ سے تعلق رکھنے والے ہیں گمان رکھتے ہیں خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ علامہ نے یہاں لفظ امامت کو ذکر کر کے اس سے وہ مفہوم مراد نہیں لیا جو معتبر عند الشیعہ ہے بلکہ وہ مفہوم مرادلیا ہے جو معتبر عند اہل السنتہ ہے اس پر قرینہ خود علامہ محمدوح کا شرح عقائد میں اس عقیدہ کی تردید کرنا ہے واللہ اعلم بالصواب
شبہ ثانیہ:۔ دوسرا شبہ یہ ہے کہ علامہ تفتازانی علیہ الرحمہ نے مختصر المعانی میں مندالیہ کو بصورت علم ولقب ذکر کرنے کی وجوہات میں سے تعظیم اور اہانت کی مثال دیتے ہوئے فرما یار کسب على وهرب معاویہ کہ لفظ علی چونکہ علو سے مشتق ہے اس کے لفظوں سے ہی تعظیم معلوم ہو رہی ہے اس لئے مسند الیہ تعظیماً بطور علم و لقب کے ذکر کیا اور معاویہ عوی سے مشتق ہے جس کا معنی ہے بھیڑیئے کی آواز تو اس کے لفظوں سے ہی اہانت کبھی جارہی ہے اس کو دیکھتے ہوئے بعض حضرات نے اعتراض
besturdubooks.wordps.com
Al-Tarwih li Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih
Refutation of some doubts about Allamah Taftazani
55
Some people have attributed Shi'ism to Allamah Taftazani and have tried to prove it with several reasons, but this is devoid of research and reflects a superficial mind. We will, God willing, mention these reasons and then refute them.
First doubt: That Allamah Taftazani wrote in Hashiya al-Talwih while discussing the science of kalam: 'What is included in the science of kalam concerning the states of the Creator, prophethood, imamah, resurrection, and what is connected to that according to the law of Islam.' Seeing the word 'imamah', some objected, thinking that perhaps the Allamah also held the Shi'i belief of imamate and intended that meaning here; this is evidence of his being Shi'a. The answer: This doubt and objection are extremely superficial, and there is no need to even respond, because in the view of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, imamah has a broad meaning that includes both khilafah and amarah. And it is clear that the Allamah intended here the meaning that is valid in the view of Ahl al-Sunnah, not the Shi'i belief of imamate. This is supported by the fact that when Allamah Nasafi said in his book 'Aqa'id al-Nasafiyyah: 'Then the imam should be apparent, not hidden, and not awaited,' under that Allamah Taftazani says: 'Not as the Shi'a, especially the Imamiyyah among them, claim that the true imam after the Messenger of God is 'Ali, then his son al-Husayn, then his brother al-Hasan, then his son 'Ali Zayn al-'Abidin (may God be pleased with them).' That is, the intended imam is not the one that the Shi'a, especially the Imami sect, imagine. The summary is that the Allamah, by mentioning the word 'imamah' here, did not intend the meaning that is valid among the Shi'a, but rather the meaning that is valid among Ahl al-Sunnah. This is further evidenced by the fact that the Allamah himself refuted this belief in his commentary on 'Aqa'id. And God knows best.
Second doubt: The second doubt is that Allamah Taftazani, in Mukhtasar al-Ma'ani, when discussing the reasons for mentioning something 'pertaining to' as a proper name and epithet, gave an example of glorification and insult by saying: 'Kasaba 'Ali wa haraba Mu'awiya' (Ali earned and Mu'awiya fled). The word 'Ali is derived from 'uluww (highness), so from its letters glorification is evident; therefore, the predicate (musnad ilayh) was mentioned as a proper name and epithet for glorification. And 'Mu'awiya' is derived from 'awwa' (the howling of a wolf), so from its letters insult is apparent. Seeing this, some people objected...
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a defense of Allamah al-Taftazani against allegations of Shi'i leanings. The author identifies two specific doubts. The first doubt concerns Taftazani's inclusion of 'imamah' in the definition of 'ilm al-kalam in his Hashiya al-Talwih. The refutation argues that Ahl al-Sunnah use 'imamah' in a broad sense meaning leadership (khilafah and imarah), not the Shi'i concept of a specific infallible imam. To prove this, the author cites Taftazani's own commentary on al-Nasafi's 'Aqa'id, where he explicitly rejects the Shi'i view that the imam after the Prophet is 'Ali and his descendants. This demonstrates Taftazani's Sunni orthodoxy. The second doubt arises from Taftazani's example in Mukhtasar al-Ma'ani using 'Ali and Mu'awiya to illustrate linguistic glorification and insult. The author explains that this is purely a grammatical illustration, not a sectarian statement. The refutation aims to clear Taftazani of any suspicion of Shi'ism and confirm his adherence to Ahl al-Sunnah.

Key Terms
إمامة (imamah): In this passage, imamah is defined in the Sunni sense as comprehensive leadership including khilafah and imarah, as opposed to the Shi'i specific belief in an infallible imam.
شیعیت (Shi'ism): The attribution of being a Shi'a, which the refutation denies for Taftazani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did Allamah Taftazani use as an example to illustrate glorification and insult in Mukhtasar al-Ma'ani?
A) Ali and Muawiya
B) Muhammad and Abu Jahl
C) Umar and Abu Sufyan
D) Hassan and Hussain

Key Takeaway
A single ambiguous term does not prove sectarian deviation; authorial corpus and mainstream usage must be consulted.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
15 min
Defending Taftazani: Methodological Responses to an Objection
Defense against claim that Taftazani disrespects Muawiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Hanafi textual and historical analysis to defend a scholar from accusations of disrespecting Sahaba.

Core Idea
Taftazani did not disrespect Muawiyah; the example was either for a non-Sahabi or later interpolated.

Scholars sometimes face objections that their words imply disrespect to the Sahaba. This lesson examines how Shaykh al-Hind and later Hanafi scholars defended Allamah Taftazani from such a claim. By analyzing two responses—one based on Taftazani's own stance and another on interpolation (idraj)—we learn the Hanafi method of defending scholarly integrity while maintaining respect for the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
State clearly what the objectors claimed: that Taftazani's example in Mukhtasar al-Ma'ani disrespected Sayyidina Muawiyah (RA).
The objection implies that Taftazani engaged in sabb or ta'n, which is prohibited.
2
Analyze the first answer
Understand the argument that the example was not intended for a Sahabi. Note the evidence: Taftazani's own prohibition of defaming Sahaba in Sharh al-Aqa'id and the hadiths he cites.
This answer uses Taftazani's own words as proof of his respect.
3
Analyze the second answer
Examine the claim that the example is mudraj (interpolated). Identify the evidence: its absence in al-Mutawwal and parallels with interpolation in other works.
This answer relies on textual criticism and historical precedent.
4
Reflect on Hanafi methodology
Consider how the defender uses dalil naqli (hadith), qawl of the scholar, and the concept of idraj to build a multi-layered defense. Notice the balance between textual proof and contextual reasoning.
The method shows that respect for Sahaba is a settled principle that cannot be overturned by a single ambiguous example.

Source Text

کیا کہ اس میں حضرت امیر معاویہ رضی اللہ عنہ کی بے ادبی ہے اور ان کے خلاف جرات بے جا ہے اور یہ رفض کے
الجواب الاول:۔ حضرت شیخ الہند رحمہ اللہ فرماتے ہیں علامہ تفتازانی علیہ الرحمہ نے یہ مثال صحابی رسول کیلئے نہیں دی بلکہ اگر غیر صحابی ان ناموں یا القاب کے ساتھ موسوم تو اس کیلئے یہ مثال پیش کی ہے اس کی تائید اس سے ہوتی ہے کہ اگر اس سے فراد صحابی رسول ہوں تو ظاہر ہے کہ یہ ان کی بے ادبی ہے اور ایک قسم کا طعن ہے جبکہ علامہ صحابی کے طعن کو فسق و بدعت اور کفر سے تعبیر کرتے ہیں چنانچہ شرح عقائد میں تحریر فرماتے ہیں کہ والسب والطعن فيهم ان كان مما يخالف الادلة القطعية فكفر كقذف عائشة رضى الله عنها والا فبدعة وفسق یعنی صحابہ کرام کے خلاف ایسی تنقیص اور ایسا طعن جس سے نصوص قطعیہ کی مخالفت لازم آئے تو یہ کفر ہے وگرنہ بدعت و فسق ہے اور علامہ منفی علیہ الرحمہ نے جب یہ فر ا کہ و یکف عن ذكر الصحابة الا بخیر تو اس کے تحت علامہ نے اس قول کی دلیل بیان کرتے ہوئے متعدد احادیث سے استدلال کیا ہے مثلا قال النبي علیه السلام لا تسبوا اصحاب الحدیث اور ظاہر ہے کہ سب تنقیص کو کہتے ہیں حدیث نمبر۲ اکــر مـوا اصحابی فانهم خياركم حدیث نمبر ۳: الله الله فی اصحابى لا تتخذوهم غرضا من بعدى فمن احبهم فبحبى احبهم ومن ابغضهم فببغضى ابغضهم من آذاهم فقد آذاني و من آذاني فقد آذى الله (الحدیث ) اور جب یہ اعتراض ہوا کہ صحابہ کرام کے آپس میں منازعات و محاربات بھی تو ہوئے ہیں تو سب کو خیر کے ساتھ کیسے ذکر کیا جاسکتا ہے تو علامہ نے جواب دیا کہ و ماوقع بينهم من المنازعات والمحاربات فله محامل و تاویلات اور وہ حمل اور تاویل یہ ہے کہ ہر ایک نے اپنے اجتہاد پر عمل کیا دین سمجھ کر ذاتی عناد و عداوت کو دخل نہ تھا اور اجتہاد صواب بھی ہو سکتا ہے اور خطاء بھی اور اجتہاد خطاء پر بھی ایک ثواب کی بشارت آنحضرت علیہ السلام نے دی ہے خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ جب علامہ کسی صحابی کی طرف طعن یا تنقیص کی نسبت کو نا جائز سمجھتے ہیں بھلا یہ کیسے ہو سکتا ہے کہ وہ اس مثال میں صحابی رسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم حضرت امیر معاویہ کو مرا دلیں لیکن اس مثال سے ظاہراً ذہن چونکہ صحابی رسول کی طرف جا سکتا ہے اس لئے اس کا ترک اولی تھا اور یہ بھی کچھ سوء ادبی سے خالی نہیں اور علامہ کے منصب کے خلاف ہے۔
الجواب الثانی: بعض محققین فرماتے نہیں یہ مثال مدرج ہے یعنی اصل کتاب میں موجود نہ تھی بعد میں کسی رافضی نے اپنی فطری شرارت سے علامہ کے منصب کو مکدر کر دینے کیلئے یہ اضافہ کر دیا اور اس پر قرینہ یہ ہے کہ مطول میں یہ مثال موجود نہیں جبکہ اکثر ایسا ہے کہ جو کچھ مختصر المعانی میں موجود ہے وہ مطول میں بھی بمع اضافہ موجود ہے لیکن جو کچھ مطول میں ہے ضروری نہیں کہ وہ مختصر المعانی میں بھی ہو بخلا اس مقام کے یہاں معاملہ برعکس ہے مطول میں تو یہ مثال موجود نہیں مختصر میں موجود ہے معلوم ہوا کہ یہ مثال مدرج ہے۔ باقی رہا یہ سوال کہ اوراج کیسے ہو گیا تو اس کی کئی نظائر اور مثالیں موجود ہیں جب کتب احادیث محفوظ نہ رہیں پیران پیر شیخ عبد القادر جیلانی کی کتب میں ادراج والحاق ہوا قریب زمانہ میں شاہ اسماعیل شہید رحمہ اللہ کی کتاب صراط مستقیم میں غالیوں کی طرف سے عبارتوں کے اضافے کئے گئے تو مختصر المعانی میں ادراج کیوں نہیں ہو سکتا۔
What that there is disrespect of Amir Muawiyah, may Allah be pleased with him, and undue boldness against him, and this is Rafd. The first answer: Shaykh al-Hind, may Allah have mercy on him, says that Allamah Taftazani, may Allah have mercy on him, did not give this example for a Companion of the Messenger, but rather if a non-Companion is named or titled with these, then he presented the example for that. It is supported by this: if the intended were Companions of the Messenger, then it is clear that this is disrespect of them and a kind of defamation, whereas Allamah considers defamation of a Companion to be transgression, innovation, and disbelief. Thus in Sharh al-Aqa'id he writes: 'And cursing and defaming them, if it contradicts definitive proofs, is disbelief, like accusing Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, otherwise it is innovation and transgression.' That is, such disparagement and defamation against the noble Companions that necessitates contradiction of definitive texts is disbelief; otherwise it is innovation and transgression. And when Allamah [said]: 'And he refrains from mentioning the Companions except with good,' he then cited the proof of this statement with multiple hadiths, e.g., the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Do not revile my Companions.' It is clear that reviling means disparagement. Hadith no. 2: 'Honor my Companions, for they are the best of you.' Hadith no. 3: 'Allah, Allah regarding my Companions; do not make them targets after me. Whoever loves them, loves them out of love for me; whoever hates them, hates them out of hatred for me. Whoever harms them harms me, and whoever harms me harms Allah.' (The hadith) And when the objection came that there were conflicts and battles among the Companions, how can they all be mentioned with good? Allamah answered: 'And what occurred between them of conflicts and battles has interpretations and explanations.' That interpretation is that each one acted according to his ijtihad, considering it religion; there was no personal enmity or hostility. And ijtihad may be correct or erroneous, and for erroneous ijtihad the Prophet gave good news of one reward. In summary, since Allamah considers attribution of defamation or disparagement to any Companion as impermissible, how can it be that he intends the Messenger's Companion Amir Muawiyah in this example? But because this example ostensibly could direct the mind to a Companion, it was a better to avoid it, and it is not entirely free from some lack of propriety, and contrary to Allamah's rank. The second answer: Some scholars say that this example is interpolated, i.e., it was not present in the original book; later some Rafidi added it with his natural mischief to tarnish Allamah's rank. Evidence for this is that this example is not present in al-Mutawwal, whereas often whatever is in Mukhtasar al-Ma'ani is also in al-Mutawwal with additional content, but what is in al-Mutawwal is not necessarily also in Mukhtasar al-Ma'ani. Contrary to this case, the situation is reversed: the example is not in al-Mutawwal but is in Mukhtasar. Thus it is known that this example is interpolated. As for the question of how interpolation occurred, there are many similar instances when hadith books were not preserved; interpolation and addition occurred in the books of Pir Pir Shaykh Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani. Recently in Shah Ismail Shaheed's book Sirat-i-Mustaqim, additions were made by extremists. So why could interpolation not occur in Mukhtasar al-Ma'ani?
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is a defense of Allamah Taftazani against the objection that he used an example disrespectful to Sayyidina Muawiyah (RA). The defender gives two answers. The first answer, from Shaykh al-Hind, argues that Taftazani's example was not meant for a Companion but for a non-Companion with similar names/titles. It cites Taftazani's own words from Sharh al-Aqa'id, where he states that defaming Companions is disbelief or transgression depending on the severity, and he brings hadiths prohibiting their defamation. Therefore, he could not have intended disrespect to Muawiyah. However, the defender concedes that the example may appear to refer to a Companion, so avoiding it would have been better. The second answer claims that the example was later interpolated by a Rafidi, citing its absence in al-Mutawwal and giving examples of interpolation in other works. The defender uses both textual and historical evidence to absolve Taftazani of any intentional disrespect.

Key Terms
السب (al-sabb): Cursing or reviling, which includes any form of verbal abuse or disparagement
الطعن (al-ta'n): Defamation or impugning the character of someone
مدرج (mudraj): Interpolated; text inserted into a book that was not originally part of it

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main argument of the second answer to the objection?
A) The example was not meant for a Sahabi
B) The example was interpolated later by a Rafidi
C) Taftazani apologized for the example
D) The example is actually a quote from another scholar

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi defense of Taftazani shows that a scholar's respect for Sahaba must be proven through his own statements and the integrity of textual transmission, not by isolated examples.

Defending Taftazani: The Method of Citing Only Explicit Bisharat
Defense against claim of deliberate omission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of textual limitation to defend a scholar's selective citation of hadith, identifying when a Companion's virtue is omitted due to lack of explicit bisharat.

Core Idea
Taftazani's omission is methodological: he only cites hadiths of explicit glad tidings, not bias.

In this passage, Taftazani's Sharh al-Aqa'id is defended against the accusation that he deliberately omitted the virtues of Muawiyah out of bias. The defense provides two clear reasons rooted in the author's method of citing only those Companions with explicit prophetic glad tidings of Paradise, and including Muawiyah in the general statement about all great Companions. By understanding this, we see how a scholar's method—not personal sentiment—governs textual citation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Read the objection: Taftazani is accused of omitting Muawiyah's virtues while mentioning others, implying bias. Note the specific hadith from Tirmidhi they cite.
2
Analyze the first answer
Taftazani only lists those with explicit bisharat (glad tidings) of Paradise. Muawiyah is not among the ten, nor has an explicit bisharat hadith. Thus his omission is consistent with the author's stated method.
This is a textual category argument: only those with explicit nass (clear text) are included.
3
Analyze the second answer
Taftazani includes Muawiyah in the general phrase 'others among the great Companions' and cites a hadith against hating any Sahabi. This shows he did not omit Muawiyah but included him in a broader category.
This uses the principle of 'amm (general) to cover Muawiyah.
4
Evaluate the defense
The defense relies on the consistency of Taftazani's method. The objector's claim of bias is refuted because Taftazani treats all similar Companions the same way. Thus the charge is unfounded.
The evaluation uses usul al-hadith principles: explicit vs. general reports.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبہ ثالثہ : بعض حضرات نے علامہ پر یہ بھی اعتراض کیا ہے کہ انہوں نے شرح عقائد میں خلفاء اربعہ عشرہ مبشرہ اور حضرات حسنین کریمین اور سیدہ فاطمہ کی فضیلت پر احادیث ذکر کی ہیں جبکہ سیدنا امیر معاویہ رضی اللہ عنہ کی فضیلت پر کوئی حدیث ذکر نہیں کی بلکہ ان کے بارہ میں صرف اتنا کہا کہ ان پر لعن جائز نہیں حالانکہ ان کی فضیلت میں ترمذی شریف میں حدیث صحیح موجود ہے چنانچہ فرمایا اللهم اجعله ها دیا مھدیا تو حضرت امیر معاویہ کی فضیلت میں حدیث ذکر نہ کر کے انہوں نے دل کی بھر اس نکالی ہے (جبکہ یہ جملہ لکھتے ہوئے قلم لرز رہا ہے) الجواب (۱):۔ پہلی بات تو یہ ہے کہ علامہ نے ان حضرات کے فضائل پر جواحادیث ذکر کی ہیں وہ متن کے مندرجہ ذیل جملہ کے تحت ذکر کی ہیں ونشهد بالجنة للعشرة الذين بشرهم النبي علیه السلام یعنی ہم ان کے جنتی ہونے کی گواہی دیتے ہیں جن صحابہ کرام کیلئے حضور نے جنتی ہونے کی بشارت دی ہے پھر اسی کی مناسبت سے حسنین کریمین اور سیدہ فاطمہ رضی اللہ عنہم کی بشارت والی احادیث بھی ذکر کر دیں اور ظاہر ہے کہ سیدنا امیر معاویہ رضی اللہ عنہ عشرہ مبشرہ میں داخل نہیں اور نہ ان کے حق میں بشارت کی کوئی حدیث صراحہ واقع ہے اس لئے علامہ نے ان کے بارہ میں حدیث ذکر نہیں کی الجواب (۲): علامہ نے اشارہ سیدنا امیر معاویہ بلکہ تمام اکابر صحابہ کرام کے حق میں فضیلت پر وارد ہونے والی صحیح احادیث کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے چنانچہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ثم فی مناقب كل من ابي بكر و عمر و عثمان وعلى والحسن والحسين وغيرهم من اكــابــر الصحابة احاديث صحيحة اور ظاہر ہے کہ اکابر صحابہ کرام میں سیدنا امیر معاویہ بھی داخل ہیں تو معترض کا کیا خیال ہے کہ جن دوسرے اکابر صحابہ کرام کی فضیلت میں احادیث کی صراحت نہیں کی تو کیا یہ بھی دل کی بھڑاس نکالنے کیلئے اور بغض کی وجہ سے ہے ہر گز ایسا نہیں خصوص علامہ نے فمن ابغضهم فببغضى ابغضهم والی حدیث ذکر کر کے تمام صحابہ کرام سے بغض رکھنے کی نفی کر دی ہے تو صرف امیر معاویہ رضی اللہ عنہ کی فضیلت میں حدیث کی صراحت نہ کرنے کی وجہ سے اس کو دل کی بھڑاس نکالنے اور بغض پر کیسےمحمول کیا جا سکتا ہے زیادہ سے زیادہ یہ کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ اس طرز سے علامہ مدروح کے ہاں سید نا امیر معاویہ رضی اللہ عنہ کا حضرات خلفاء اربعہ اور حضرات
Third doubt: Some people also objected to Allamah that in Sharh al-Aqa'id he mentioned hadiths on the virtues of the Four Caliphs, the ten promised Paradise, and of Hasan, Husayn, and Fatima, but he did not mention any hadith on the virtue of Sayyidina Amir Muawiyah, rather he only said about him that cursing him is not permissible, whereas there is a sound hadith in Tirmidhi about his virtue: 'O Allah, make him a guide, guided.' So by not mentioning a hadith on Muawiyah's virtue, he vented his heart's spite (and this sentence makes the pen tremble). The answer (1): The first point is that Allamah mentioned the hadiths on the virtues of those persons under the following sentence in the text: 'And we testify to Paradise for the ten whom the Prophet gave glad tidings of Paradise.' That is, we bear witness to their being in Paradise for those Companions for whom the Prophet gave glad tidings. Then accordingly, he also mentioned the hadiths of glad tidings for Hasan, Husayn, and Fatima. It is clear that Sayyidina Amir Muawiyah is not included among the ten given glad tidings, nor is there any hadith explicitly giving glad tidings for him. Therefore, Allamah did not mention a hadith about him. The answer (2): Allamah pointed to the authentic hadiths that have come regarding the virtues of Sayyidina Amir Muawiyah and indeed all the great Companions. For he says: 'Then concerning the virtues of each of Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, Ali, Hasan, Husayn, and others among the great Companions, there are authentic hadiths.' It is clear that Sayyidina Amir Muawiyah is included among the great Companions. So what does the objector think? If he did not explicitly mention hadiths on the virtues of other great Companions, is that also for venting spite and due to hatred? Absolutely not. In particular, Allamah mentioned the hadith 'Whoever hates them, hates them out of hatred for me,' thus negating hatred of all Companions. So how can the mere failure to explicitly mention a hadith on the virtue of Muawiyah alone be attributed to venting spite and hatred? At most it can be said that in this style, according to the honored Allamah, Sayyidina Amir Muawiyah's [status] with respect to the Four Caliphs and [others]...
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage defends Taftazani against the objection that he deliberately omitted the virtues of Muawiyah in Sharh al-Aqa'id while mentioning others. The defender gives two answers. First, Taftazani only listed virtues of those with explicit prophetic glad tidings of Paradise (the ten, plus Hasan, Husayn, and Fatima who also received glad tidings). Muawiyah is not among that group, so there was no need to mention him. Second, Taftazani explicitly stated that there are authentic hadiths on the virtues of each of the great Companions, including Muawiyah, by saying 'and others among the great Companions.' Thus he did not omit him but included him in the general statement. The defender also argues that Taftazani's citation of the hadith 'Whoever hates them...' proves his love for all Sahaba, so singling out Muawiyah for omission cannot be due to hatred.

Key Terms
عشرہ مبشرہ (ashara mubashshara): The ten Companions given explicit glad tidings of Paradise by the Prophet
بشارت (bisharat): Glad tiding, specifically prophetic guarantee of Paradise

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first answer, why did Taftazani not mention a hadith specifically about Muawiyah's virtue?
A) He considered Muawiyah less virtuous
B) Muawiyah is not among the ten promised Paradise and there is no explicit bisharat hadith for him
C) He forgot to include it
D) He only mentioned virtues of the Four Caliphs

Key Takeaway
Taftazani's omission of Muawiyah's specific virtues is due to his method of citing only those with explicit prophetic glad tidings, and Muawiyah is included in the general category of great Companions, so the charge of bias is unfounded.

Defending Taftazani on Muawiyah's Hadith Omission
Addressing objection that Taftazani omitted Muawiyah's virtue hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the scholarly defense of Taftazani's omission of a specific hadith by identifying the contextual and methodological reasoning behind the selection of hadiths in a theological text.

Core Idea
Omission of a hadith does not imply bias; it reflects the scope of discussion and inclusive citation.

This passage addresses an objection that Taftazani deliberately omitted a hadith on Muawiyah's virtue due to personal bias. The responder provides two clear answers: first, the discussion was limited to the ten promised Paradise and their families; second, Taftazani included all major Companions in a general statement, thereby covering Muawiyah. Understanding this defense requires us to analyze textual context, authorial intent, and the difference between specific and inclusive citation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
What is the exact criticism against Taftazani? Note the hadith cited by the objector and the charge of bias.
The objector claims omission implies personal animosity.
2
Analyze Taftazani's textual context
Read the passage Taftazani wrote. He explicitly limits his discussion to the ten promised Paradise and then adds their family members. Muawiyah is not in these categories.
Know the scope of the original text.
3
Examine the inclusive citation
Taftazani later mentions 'others among the major Companions' and cites a hadith on love for all Companions. This implicitly includes Muawiyah.
General statements can cover specific cases.
4
Assess the counter-argument
The objector's argument is methodologically weak because it ignores the contextual boundary and the inclusive principle. The responder shows that the omission is not bias but adherence to the text's framework.
Methodological flaw in the objection.
5
Conclude the rational basis
At most, the omission suggests Muawiyah is less virtuous than the ten and the family members, which is standard Sunni doctrine. The charge of bias is unfounded.
The conclusion aligns with Ahl al-Sunna position.

Third doubt: Some people have objected to the author [Taftazani] that in his commentary on al-ʿAqāʾid, he mentioned hadiths on the virtues of the four Caliphs, the ten promised Paradise, al-Ḥasan, al-Ḥusayn, and Sayyida Fāṭima, but he did not mention any hadith on the virtue of Sayyidunā Muʿāwiya—rather, regarding him he only said that cursing him is not permissible—when in fact there is a ṣaḥīḥ hadith in Tirmidhī on his virtue, wherein [the Prophet] said: 'O Allah, make him a guide, rightly-guided.' So by not mentioning the hadith on Muʿāwiya's virtue, he vented his spleen (this sentence written while the pen trembles). Answer (1): The first point is that the author [Taftazani] mentioned the hadiths on the virtues of those persons under the following statement in the text: 'We testify to Paradise for the ten whom the Prophet (peace be upon him) gave glad tidings.' Then, in that context, he also mentioned the hadiths of glad tidings for al-Ḥasan, al-Ḥusayn, and Sayyida Fāṭima. It is obvious that Sayyidunā Muʿāwiya is not among the ten, nor is there any explicit hadith of glad tidings for him, so the author did not mention a hadith regarding him. Answer (2): The author hinted at the authentic hadiths regarding virtue for Sayyidunā Muʿāwiya—indeed for all the major Companions—when he said: 'Then there are authentic hadiths on the merits of Abū Bakr, ʿUmar, ʿUthmān, ʿAlī, al-Ḥasan, al-Ḥusayn, and others among the major Companions.' It is clear that Muʿāwiya is included among the major Companions. So what does the objector think: that he did not specify hadiths for other major Companions—does that also stem from spleen and hatred? Never. In particular, the author cited the hadith: 'Whoever hates them hates me, and whoever hates me, Allah hates him,' thereby negating hatred towards all Companions. So how can the mere lack of explicit mention of a hadith for Muʿāwiya be construed as venting spleen and hatred? At most, it can be said that in this style, from the author's perspective, Muʿāwiya is considered less virtuous than the four Caliphs and al-Ḥasan and al-Ḥusayn—and that is exactly the doctrine of Ahl al-Sunna.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes an objection that the author Taftazani intentionally omitted a hadith on Muʿāwiya's virtue, allegedly due to bias. The objector cites a hadith from Tirmidhī. The response provides two answers: First, Taftazani's discussion was limited to the ten promised Paradise and their families, among whom Muʿāwiya is not included. Second, Taftazani did mention authentic hadiths on the merits of major Companions collectively, which includes Muʿāwiya. Additionally, he cited a hadith condemning hatred of any Companion, proving his impartiality. The passage concludes that any perceived inferiority of Muʿāwiya in virtue relative to the first four Caliphs and the two grandsons is actually the standard Sunni position.

Key Terms
عشرہ مبشرہ (al-ʿashara al-mubashshara): The ten Companions to whom the Prophet gave glad tidings of Paradise during their lifetime.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He considered Muawiyah not among the Companions.

C) He believed the hadith was inauthentic.
D) He intentionally hid it due to sectarian bias.

Key Takeaway
A scholar's omission of a specific hadith must be understood in light of the textual scope and inclusive principles, not assumed as bias.

Defending Taftazani's Cursing of Yazid: A Sunni Ijtihad
Defending Taftazani by specifying the referent of 'supporters' and legitimizing the cursing of Yazid as an ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between legitimate ikhtilaf and heresy by analyzing the evidence for and against cursing Yazid, and apply the method of takhsis to similar historical evaluations.

Core Idea
Cursing Yazid is a legitimate difference of opinion within Ahl al-Sunna, not a sign of Shia affiliation.

The objection that Taftazani's curse on Yazid and his supporters falsely implicates the Companions is based on a superficial reading. The response clarifies that 'supporters' refers specifically to those who participated in the killing of al-Husayn, excluding the Companions. The lesson then explores the two Sunni positions on cursing Yazid, demonstrating that the permissibility view is well-supported by early scholars and textual proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection and its key premise
Read the fourth objection: it claims that Taftazani's curse on Yazid's 'supporters and helpers' necessarily includes the Companions, which would align him with the Shia. Note the premise: that 'supporters and helpers' means anyone who gave allegiance.
This premise is the point of attack.
2
Analyze the refutation: takhsis of 'supporters'
The answer restricts the meaning of 'supporters and helpers' to those who fought against al-Husayn. Identify the evidence for this restriction (the quote from ʿAllāma ʿAbd al-ʿAzīz al-Pānī Patī). Understand that this is a case of takhsis (specification) of a general term.
Takhsis is a key usul concept used here to rebut the objection.
3
Examine the two Sunni positions on cursing Yazid
The text states that there are two groups among Ahl al-Sunna: one permits cursing Yazid, the other forbids it. List the scholars cited for permissibility (Ibn al-Jawzī, Aḥmad ibn Ḥanbal, etc.) and note that Taftazani is part of this group.
This demonstrates that the issue is one of ijtihad, not deviance.
4
Evaluate the proofs for permissibility
Two proofs are given: Quran 47:22-23 (curse on those who sever kinship ties) and the hadith on frightening the people of Madinah. Determine how each proof applies to Yazid's actions (killing al-Husayn and al-Ḥarra).
Consider the thubut and dalala of each proof; both are zanni in dalala, allowing ikhtilaf.
5
Conclude: legitimacy of Taftazani's position
Synthesize: the objection is invalid due to takhsis, and even if it were not, cursing Yazid is a legitimate Sunni view. Taftazani remains within Ahl al-Sunna.
The key takeaway: ikhtilaf on historical figures does not necessarily indicate heresy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبہ رابعہ : یہ ہے کہ علامہ تفتازانی علیہ الرحمہ نے یزید اور اس کے اعوان و انصار پر لعنت کی ہے چنانچہ لکھتے ہیں کہ فنحن لا نتوقف في شانه بل في ايمانه لعنة الله عليه و علی انصاره و اعوانه اور یزید کے اعوان و انصار میں حضرات صحابہ کرام بھی داخل ہیں کیونکہ بعض صحابہ کرام نے بھی اس کے ہاتھ پر بیعت کی تھی تو یزید کے اعوان و انصار پر لعنت کر نام با صحابہ کرام پر لعنت کرنا ہے اور صحابہ کرام پر لعنت کرنا یہ اہل تشیع کا شیوہ ہے تو یہ بھی ان کے شیعہ ہونے کی دلیل ہے۔ الجواب:۔ یہ اعتراض تب درست ہو سکتا ہے جبکہ انصارہ و اعوانہ سے مراد وہ تمام لوگ ہوں جنہوں نے یزید کی بیعت کی تھی حالانکہ یہ قول سطحی ذہن کی عکاس ہے بلکہ انصارہ واعوانہ سے مراد خاص طور پر وہ لوگ ہیں جنہوں نے حضرت حسین کو قتل کیا یا قاتلین کی مدد کی تھی اور ظاہر ہے کہ قاتلین اور ان کی مدد کرنے والوں میں حضرات صحابہ کرام شامل نہ تھے چنانچہ علی انصاره و اعوانه تحت علامہ عبد العزیز پر ہاروی رقم طراز ہیں کہ ای جنوده الذين حاربوا الحسين رضي الله عنه لہذا جب انصارہ واعوا نہ میں حضرات صحابہ کرام شامل نہیں تو ان پر لعنت کی وجہ سے علامہ کو شیعہ کہنا یہ قول بلا زیل ہے یزید پر لعنت کے بارہ میں محققین کی رائے باقی علامہ تفتازانی علیہ الرحمہ نے یزید پر لعنت کی ہے اس کی وجہ سے وہ اہل سنت سے خارج نہیں ہوتے کیونکہ یزید پر لعنت کے جواز اور عدم جواز پر اہل سنت کے دو گروہ ہیں۔ اس گروہ لعنت کو جائز سمجھتا ہے اور دوسرا گروہ اس کو نا جائز سمجھتا ہے جو لعنت کو جائز سمجھتے ہیں وہ مندرجہ ذیل ہیں ۔ علامہ ابن جوزی ۲۔ امام احمد بن حنبل ۳۔ قاضی ابو یعلی ۴۔ قاضی ثناء اللہ پانی پتی وغیرہ اور علامہ تفتازانی بھی اسی گروہ میں شامل ہیں اور ان حضرات نے مندرجہ ذیل دلائل سے استدلال کیا ہے ولیل (۱): قال الله عز و جل فهل عسيتم ان توليتم أن تفسدوا فی الارض وتقطعوا ارحامکم اولئک الذين لعنهم الله یعنی جو قطع رحمی کا سبب بنے اس پر اللہ نے لعنت کی ہے تو امام احمد اس سے استدلال کرتے ہوئے کہتے ہیں کہ یزید بھی قطع رحمی کا سبب بنا ہے اس لئے اس پر لعنت جائز ہے ولیل (۲) قال عليه السلام من اخاف اهل المدينة ظلماً أخافه الله تعالى شانه وعليه لعنة الله والملائكة والناس اجمعین کہ جس نے اہل مدینہ کو ظلماً خوفزدہ کیا تو اللہ اس کو خوفزدہ کرے اس پر اللہ اور ملائکہ اور تمام لوگوں کی لعنت تو قاضی ابو یعلی فرماتے ہیں کہ واقعہ حرہ میں یزید نے مدینہ کی طرف لشکر بھیجا تھا اور اہل مدینہ کوقتل کیا اور ان پر ظلم
Fourth doubt: That the author Taftazani (may Allah have mercy on him) cursed Yazid and his supporters and helpers; thus he wrote: 'We do not hesitate regarding his matter, rather regarding his faith: the curse of Allah be upon him and upon his helpers and supporters.' And among Yazid's supporters and helpers are included the noble Companions, because some Companions pledged allegiance to him. So cursing Yazid's supporters and helpers becomes cursing the Companions, and cursing the Companions is the way of the Shia; so this too is evidence that he is Shia. Answer: This objection would be valid only if by 'ansārihī wa aʿwānihī' (his helpers and supporters) is meant all those who pledged allegiance to Yazid. However, this statement reflects a superficial mind. Rather, by 'ansārihī wa aʿwānihī' is meant specifically those who killed al-Ḥusayn or aided the killers. And it is obvious that among the killers and those who aided them, no Companions were included. Thus, under the phrase 'upon his helpers and supporters' in the text, ʿAllāma ʿAbd al-ʿAzīz al-Pāni Patī writes: 'i.e., his troops who fought against al-Ḥusayn (may Allah be pleased with him).' Therefore, when the supporters and helpers do not include the Companions, then calling the author Shia due to cursing them is an invalid statement. The opinion of the investigators regarding cursing Yazid: As for Taftazani cursing Yazid, he is not thereby excluded from Ahl al-Sunna, because there are two groups of Ahl al-Sunna regarding the permissibility and impermissibility of cursing Yazid. One group considers it permissible, the other considers it impermissible. Those who consider it permissible include: 1. ʿAllāma Ibn al-Jawzī; 2. Imam Aḥmad ibn Ḥanbal; 3. Qāḍī Abū Yaʿlā; 4. Qāḍī Thanaʾ Allāh al-Pānī Patī, etc. Taftazani is also included in this group. These individuals have argued with the following proofs: Proof (1): Allah says: 'Would you then, if you were given the authority, cause corruption in the land and sever your ties of kinship? Those are the ones whom Allah has cursed.' So whoever causes severing of ties, Allah curses him. Imam Aḥmad deduces from this that Yazid caused severing of ties, so cursing him is permissible. Proof (2): The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever frightens the people of Madinah unjustly, Allah will frighten him, and upon him is the curse of Allah, the angels, and all people.' Qāḍī Abū Yaʿlā says that in the incident of al-Ḥarra, Yazid sent an army to Madinah and killed the people of Madinah and oppressed them.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage deals with the objection that Taftazani's curse on Yazid and his supporters necessarily includes the Companions who pledged allegiance, thus equating him with the Shia. The response distinguishes between general supporters and those specifically involved in the killing of al-Ḥusayn, citing the interpretation of ʿAllāma ʿAbd al-ʿAzīz al-Pānī Patī that 'supporters' refers to those who fought against al-Ḥusayn. Since no Companions participated in that, the objection is invalid. The passage then addresses the broader issue of cursing Yazid, noting that it is a matter of legitimate ijtihad among Ahl al-Sunna. It lists scholars like Ibn al-Jawzī, Aḥmad ibn Ḥanbal, and Abū Yaʿlā who permitted it, and provides two proofs: Quranic verse on severing ties of kinship (which Yazid instigated via the killing of al-Ḥusayn) and the hadith on frightening the people of Madinah (applied to the Tragedy of al-Ḥarra). This shows that Taftazani's position is within mainstream Sunni orthodoxy.

Key Terms
اعوان و انصار (aʿwān wa anṣār): Supporters and helpers; in context, specified to those who fought against al-Husayn.
واقعہ حرہ (waqiʿat al-ḥarra): The battle in 63 AH where Yazid's army attacked Madinah, causing many casualties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which interpretation does the author give for Taftazani's phrase 'upon his helpers and supporters' to avoid including Companions?
A) All who pledged allegiance to Yazid
B) Only those who killed or aided in killing al-Husayn
C) All residents of Syria
D) The army that attacked Madinah

Key Takeaway
Cursing Yazid is a matter of legitimate scholarly difference (ikhtilaf) within Ahl al-Sunna, and Taftazani's stance does not exclude him from Sunni orthodoxy.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Interpreting 'Ansarihi wa A'wanihi': A Defense of Taftazani's Curse on Yazid
Defending Taftazani against the accusation of cursing the Sahaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of contextual specificity (takhsis bi al-qarina) to interpret a disputed phrase and defend a Hanafi scholar against accusations of cursing the Companions.

Core Idea
The phrase 'his helpers and supporters' is contextually restricted to those who fought Husayn, excluding all Companions.

This passage presents the fourth doubt raised against Allamah Taftazani: that his curse on Yazid and his supporters necessarily includes the Companions who pledged allegiance to Yazid. The response demonstrates that such a reading is superficial; rather, the phrase is contextually restricted to those who directly participated in the killing of Imam Husayn. This lesson will guide you through the interpretive reasoning and its justification, showing how precise textual analysis refutes unfounded accusations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the accusation
Read the doubt carefully: it claims that Taftazani's curse on Yazid's helpers and supporters includes the Companions because some Companions pledged allegiance. This is the core claim that must be refuted.
2
Isolate the disputed phrase
The phrase in question is 'ansarihi wa a'wanihi' (his helpers and supporters). The opponent interprets it broadly to mean all who supported Yazid in any way.
The term 'anasar' and 'a'wan' can be general in Arabic.
3
Recognize the opponent's interpretive method
The opponent takes the phrase at its broadest literal meaning, ignoring any contextual narrowing. This is a form of flawed interpretation that disregards qarina (contextual indicators).
In Hanafi usul, a general text (amm) can be restricted by context (qarina).
4
Apply the Hanafi response: contextual restriction
The response argues that the phrase is specifically restricted to those who fought against and killed Husayn. This is supported by the commentary of Allamah Abdul Aziz Parharwi who interprets 'his helpers' as 'his soldiers who fought against Husayn.' The presence of this specific context excludes the Companions.
This is a form of takhsis bi al-qarina – restriction by contextual evidence.
5
Evaluate the strength of the response
The response relies on a scholarly commentary that provides the intended meaning. The reasoning is sound because historically, no Companion participated in the army that killed Husayn. Thus, the restriction is factually and linguistically justified.
This also aligns with Sunni reverence for the Companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبہ رابعہ : یہ ہے کہ علامہ تفتازانی علیہ الرحمہ نے یزید اور اس کے اعوان و انصار پر لعنت کی ہے چنانچہ لکھتے ہیں کہ فنحن لا نتوقف في شانه بل في ايمانه لعنة الله عليه و علی انصاره و اعوانه اور یزید کے اعوان و انصار میں حضرات صحابہ کرام بھی داخل ہیں کیونکہ بعض صحابہ کرام نے بھی اس کے ہاتھ پر بیعت کی تھی تو یزید کے اعوان و انصار پر لعنت کر نام با صحابہ کرام پر لعنت کرنا ہے اور صحابہ کرام پر لعنت کرنا یہ اہل تشیع کا شیوہ ہے تو یہ بھی ان کے شیعہ ہونے کی دلیل ہے۔ الجواب:۔ یہ اعتراض تب درست ہو سکتا ہے جبکہ انصارہ و اعوانہ سے مراد وہ تمام لوگ ہوں جنہوں نے یزید کی بیعت کی تھی حالانکہ یہ قول سطحی ذہن کی عکاس ہے بلکہ انصارہ واعوانہ سے مراد خاص طور پر وہ لوگ ہیں جنہوں نے حضرت حسین کو قتل کیا یا قاتلین کی مدد کی تھی اور ظاہر ہے کہ قاتلین اور ان کی مدد کرنے والوں میں حضرات صحابہ کرام شامل نہ تھے چنانچہ علی انصاره و اعوانه تحت علامہ عبد العزیز پر ہاروی رقم طراز ہیں کہ ای جنوده الذين حاربوا الحسين رضي الله عنه لہذا جب انصارہ واعوا نہ میں حضرات صحابہ کرام شامل نہیں تو ان پر لعنت کی وجہ سے علامہ کو شیعہ کہنا یہ قول بلا زیل ہے
Fourth Doubt: That Allamah Taftazani, may Allah have mercy on him, cursed Yazid and his supporters and helpers. Thus he writes: 'So we do not hesitate concerning his state, but rather concerning his faith — the curse of Allah be upon him and upon his helpers and supporters.' And among Yazid's helpers and supporters are the noble Companions, because some Companions pledged allegiance to him. So cursing Yazid's helpers and supporters is cursing the noble Companions, and cursing the Companions is the practice of the Shia. So this too is evidence of his being Shia. The answer: This objection would be correct if by 'his helpers and supporters' were meant all those who pledged allegiance to Yazid; but this statement reflects a superficial mind. Rather, by 'his helpers and supporters' are meant specifically those who killed Sayyiduna Husayn or assisted the killers. And it is obvious that the killers and their helpers did not include the noble Companions. Thus, under 'upon his helpers and supporters,' Allamah Abdul Aziz Parharwi writes: 'That is, his soldiers who fought against Husayn, may Allah be pleased with him.' Therefore, when the noble Companions are not included in 'his helpers and supporters,' then calling the Allamah a Shia because of cursing them is an unfounded statement.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage addresses a fourth doubt (shubha rabi'a) raised against Allamah Mas'ud ibn Umar al-Taftazani (d. 792/1389), the author of al-Talwih. The accuser claims that Taftazani's curse on Yazid and his supporters (ansarihi wa a'wanihi) necessarily includes the Companions because some Companions had pledged allegiance to Yazid. This, they argue, proves Taftazani is Shia. The response clarifies that the phrase 'helper and supporters' refers specifically to the army that fought against and killed Imam Husayn — those who were directly involved in the tragedy of Karbala. Since no Companion participated in that, the curse does not fall on any Companion. The author supports this by citing Allamah Abdul Aziz Parharwi, who interprets 'his helpers' as 'his soldiers who fought against Husayn.' Thus, the accusation is baseless. This is a typical Hanafi defense of Taftazani, affirming that Taftazani adhered to Sunni orthodoxy while allowing curse on Yazid based on specific textual proofs.

Key Terms
شبہ رابعہ (shubha rabi'a): The fourth doubt or objection raised against Allamah Taftazani's cursing of Yazid.
انصارہ و اعوانہ (ansarihi wa a'wanihi): His helpers and supporters; in context, those who fought against Imam Husayn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the answer to the fourth doubt, who are meant by 'Yazid's helpers and supporters'?
A) All Muslims who pledged allegiance to Yazid
B) The Companions who pledged allegiance
C) Specific individuals who killed or assisted in killing Imam Husayn
D) All the Umayyad rulers

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'helpers and supporters' is contextually restricted to those who fought Husayn, excluding all Companions, so cursing them does not constitute cursing the Sahaba.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate

Two Sunni Views on Cursing Yazid: Textual Proofs and the Classification of La'nat
Presenting two Sunni positions on cursing Yazid with textual proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two Sunni positions on cursing Yazid, identify the textual proofs cited by each side, and apply the threefold classification of la'nat to evaluate a specific case.

Core Idea
Cursing a specific Muslim requires explicit textual warrant; absence of certainty about one's end leaves the matter in ikhtilaf.

This lesson examines a well-known ikhtilaf within Ahl al-Sunnah: the permissibility of cursing Yazid ibn Muawiyah. The passage presents both sides with their textual proofs and then offers a three-category framework for understanding the ruling on la'nat. As a usul al-fiqh lesson, we focus not on taking sides but on analyzing how each scholar derives his ruling from the primary sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two camps and their scholars
List the scholars who permit cursing Yazid and those who forbid it, as named in the text. Note that both groups are considered within Ahl al-Sunnah.
The permissibility camp includes Ibn Jawzi, Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Qadi Abu Ya'la, Thana'ullah Pani Pati, and Taftazani. The prohibition camp includes al-Ghazali, Hasan al-Basri, al-Razi, and al-Bukhari.
2
Examine the proofs of the permissibility camp
Locate each proof mentioned: Quran 47:22-23 (severing family ties), hadith on terrifying Madinah, Quran 4:93 (intentional killing), Quran 33:57 (annoying Allah and His Messenger), and Quran 7: (curse on wrongdoers). For each, identify the operative word or phrase that yields the ruling.
The permissibility camp uses these texts as general curses that apply to anyone fulfilling the condition, thus not requiring a specific revelation about Yazid.
3
Analyze the classification of la'nat by the prohibition camp
The text divides cursing into three types: (1) general curses on attributes, (2) curses on known eternal disbelievers, and (3) curses on specific persons whose end is unknown. Determine which type applies to Yazid according to the prohibition camp and why.
Type 3 is impermissible because the final state of the person is unknown. Since Yazid died outwardly Muslim, his ultimate fate is uncertain, so cursing him falls into this forbidden category.
4
Apply the usul principle of certainty vs. doubt
The disagreement hinges on whether the textual proofs provide certainty (qat') about Yazid's deserving curse or only probability (zann). The permissibility camp argues that his actions are so egregious that the texts definitively apply; the prohibition camp says the texts are general and cannot be applied to a specific individual without certainty of his end.
This is a classic usul issue: can a general text (amm) be applied to a specific person without additional evidence of inclusion? Both sides use valid usul methods.

دوسرا گروہ اس کو نا جائز سمجھتا ہے جو لعنت کو جائز سمجھتے ہیں وہ مندرجہ ذیل ہیں ۔ علامہ ابن جوزی ۲۔ امام احمد بن حنبل ۳۔ قاضی ابو یعلی ۴۔ قاضی ثناء اللہ پانی پتی وغیرہ اور علامہ تفتازانی بھی اسی گروہ پر اللہ نے لعنت کی ہے تو امام احمد اس سے استدلال کرتے ہوئے کہتے ہیں کہ یزید بھی قطع رحمی کا سبب بنا ہے اس لئے اس پر لعنت جائز ہے ولیل (۲) قال عليه السلام من اخاف اهل المدينة ظلماً أخافه الله تعالى شانه وعليه لعنة الله والملائكة والناس اجمعین کہ جس نے اہل مدینہ کو ظلماً خوفزدہ کیا تو اللہ اس کو خوفزدہ کرے اس پر اللہ اور ملائکہ اور تمام لوگوں کی لعنت تو قاضی ابو یعلی فرماتے ہیں کہ واقعہ حرہ میں یزید نے مدینہ کی طرف لشکر بھیجا تھا اور اہل مدینہ کوقتل کیا اور ان پر ظلم عظیم ڈھایاحتی کہ سینکڑوں صحابہ کرام کوقتل کیا تو اس لئے اس پر لعنت جائز ہے دلیل (۳): الله عز وجل ارشاد فرماتے ہیں و من يقتل مؤمنا متعمدا فجزاء ٥ جهنم خالدافيها وغضب الله عليه ولعنه الخ یعنی جس نے جان بوجھ کر کسی کوقتل کیا تو اس کا بدلہ جہنم ہے اور اس پر اللہ کا غضب اور اس کی لعنت ہے علامہ تفتازانی نے اس سے استدلال کیا ہے کہ یزید نے چونکہ حضرت حسین کے قتل کا حکم دیا ہے تو گویا یہ قاتل ہے اور چونکہ وہ اس پر خوش تھا اور رضاء بالمعصیت کفر ہے اور اسی طرح حق جل مجدہ ارشاد فرماتے ہیں ان الذین یو ذون اللہ ورسولہ علہم اللہ فی الدنیا والآخرة اسی طرح اللہ جل شانہ فرماتے ہیں کہ لعنة الله علی الظالمین اس میں کوئی شک نہیں کہ حضرت حسین کے قاتل اور قتل کے آمر اور اس پر راضی ہونے والے اللہ اور رسول اللہ اللہ کو ایذاء دینے والے ظالم ہیں لہذا ان پر لعنت جائز ہے۔ گروه ثانی دوسرا گر وہ جو لعنت کو جائز نہیں سمجھتا ہے وہ محققین اہل سنت و الجماعت ہیں وہ مندرجہ ذیل ہیں ا۔ امام غزالی ۲۔ حسن بصری ۳- امام رازی ۴۔ امام بخاری اور دیگر متقین او قواعد شرع سے ان حضرات کی تائید ہوتی ہے۔ عند امحققین لعنت کی تین اقسام ہیں۔ قسم اول : مطلقا صفت عامہ کے ساتھ لعنت کرنا جیسے کفارو یہود پرلعنت کرنا اور یہ جائز ہے اور اس طرح کی لعنت بعض صغیرہ گناہوں کے بارہ میں بھی وارد ہوئی ہے مثلاً آپ نے فرما یا لعن الله الواشمات والمستوشمات رواه شیخان اسی طرح آپ علیہ السلام نے فرما یا لعن الله المتشبهين من الرجال بالنساء والمتشبهات من النساء بالرجال رواه البخاری بلکہ بعض مکروہ امور پر بھی لعنت وارد ہوئی ہے کما قال علیہ السلام لعن الله المحلل والمحلل له قسم ثانی : کسی متعین کا فر پر لعنت کرنا جس کے کفر کی خبر شریعت نے دی ہو جیسے فرعون ابوجہل و ابلیس پر لعنت کرنا اس طرح کی لعنت بھی جائز ہے۔ قسم ثالث : کسی ایسے شخص پر لعنت کرنا جس کی موت علی الکٹر معلوم نہ ہو اس طرح کی لعنت نا جائز ہے آگے عام ہے کہ جس پر لعنت کی جارہی ہے وہ زندہ ہو یا مردہ بظاہر کا فرکیوں نہ ہو کیونکہ ممکن ہے اللہ اس کو اسلام کی توفیق دیدے اور اس کا خاتمہ اسلام پر ہو چنانچہ عبد اللہ بن عمر رضی اللہ عنہ سے حدیث ثابت ہے کہ قال قال رسول الله يوم احد اللهم العن ابا سفيان اللهم العن الحارث بن هشام اللهم العن سهيل بن عمر اللهم العن صفوان بن امية فنزلت
As for Allamah Taftazani cursing Yazid, he does not thereby leave Ahl al-Sunnah, because regarding the permissibility or impermissibility of cursing Yazid, Ahl al-Sunnah have two groups. One group considers cursing permissible, and the other considers it impermissible. Those who consider it permissible include: Allamah Ibn Jawzi, Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Qadi Abu Ya'la, Qadi Thana'ullah Pani Pati, and others. Allamah Taftazani is also among this group. These scholars have adduced the following proofs: Proof (1): Allah says, 'Would you perhaps, if you turn away, cause corruption in the land and sever your family ties? Those are the ones whom Allah has cursed.' That is, whoever causes severance of family ties, Allah has cursed him. Imam Ahmad deduces from this that Yazid also caused severance of family ties, so cursing him is permissible. Proof (2): The Prophet said, 'Whoever frightens the people of Madinah unjustly, Allah will frighten him, and upon him is the curse of Allah, the angels, and all people.' Qadi Abu Ya'la says that in the incident of Harrah, Yazid sent an army to Madinah, killed the people of Madinah, and inflicted immense oppression, killing hundreds of Companions. Therefore cursing him is permissible. Proof (3): Allah Almighty says, 'Whoever kills a believer intentionally, his recompense is Hell, abiding therein, and Allah's wrath and curse are upon him.' Allamah Taftazani deduces from this that since Yazid ordered the killing of Husayn, he is effectively a killer, and since he was pleased with it, and satisfaction with sin is disbelief. Similarly, Allah says, 'Indeed, those who annoy Allah and His Messenger, Allah has cursed them in this world and the Hereafter.' And Allah says, 'The curse of Allah is upon the wrongdoers.' There is no doubt that the killers of Husayn, those who ordered the killing, and those who were pleased with it, are annoyers of Allah and His Messenger and wrongdoers. Therefore cursing them is permissible. The second group, which does not consider cursing permissible, are the scholars of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah. They include: Imam al-Ghazali, Hasan al-Basri, Imam al-Razi, Imam al-Bukhari, and other pious ones. Their view is supported by the rules of Shariah. According to the scholars, cursing is of three types: The first type: Cursing absolutely with a general attribute, such as cursing disbelievers and Jews; this is permissible. Such cursing is even narrated for some minor sins, e.g., the Prophet said, 'May Allah curse the tattooers and those who are tattooed' (agreed upon). Similarly, the Prophet said, 'May Allah curse men who imitate women and women who imitate men' (Bukhari). Even for some disliked acts, cursing is narrated, as the Prophet said, 'May Allah curse the one who performs tahlil and the one for whom tahlil is performed.' The second type: Cursing a specific disbeliever whose unbelief has been reported by Shariah, such as cursing Pharaoh, Abu Jahl, and Iblis; this type is also permissible. The third type: Cursing a person whose death upon unbelief is not known; this type is impermissible, regardless of whether the person cursed is alive or dead, even if apparently a disbeliever, because it is possible that Allah grants him success in Islam and his end is upon Islam. Thus, it is authentically reported from Abdullah ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah said on the day of Uhud: 'O Allah, curse Abu Sufyan; O Allah, curse al-Harith ibn Hisham; O Allah, curse Suhayl ibn Amr; O Allah, curse Safwan ibn Umayyah.' Then the verse was revealed...
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage presents the complete discussion on the ruling of cursing Yazid ibn Muawiyah within Ahl al-Sunnah. The author asserts that Taftazani's curse does not expel him from Sunni orthodoxy, as there are two established Sunni positions. The first group, which includes major scholars like Ibn Jawzi, Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Abu Ya'la, and Ibn al-Humam (represented here by Thana'ullah Pani Pati), permits cursing Yazid based on clear textual proofs: (1) the Quranic curse on those who sever family ties (Q. 47:22-23) — Yazid severed ties by killing the Prophet's grandson; (2) the hadith threatening with curse those who terrorize the people of Madinah — Yazid's attack on Madinah (the Harrah incident) involved killing Companions; (3) the Quranic curse on intentional killers of believers (Q. 4:93) and those who annoy Allah and His Messenger (Q. 33:57) — Yazid ordered Husayn's killing and was pleased with it. The Hanafi school does not have a single position; many Hanafi scholars like Taftazani and Ibn al-Humam permit cursing Yazid, while others like al-Ghazali and al-Bukhari forbid it. The second group, which includes Ghazali, Hasan al-Basri, Fakhr al-Razi, and Bukhari, prohibits cursing a specific person whose final state (death upon faith or disbelief) is unknown. They categorize cursing into three: (1) general curses on attributes (like cursing disbelievers in general) — permissible; (2) cursing known eternal disbelievers (Pharaoh, Iblis) — permissible; (3) cursing a specific individual whose end is unknown — impermissible. Since Yazid's final state is unknown (he died outwardly Muslim), cursing him falls under the third category. The passage ends with a hadith example where the Prophet cursed specific polytheists at Uhud, but then a verse prohibited such cursing (probably Q. 3:128 or similar), implying abrogation. The Hanafi usul perspective on this issue is that cursing a specific person who is outwardly Muslim but known for major sins is a matter of ijtihad, and both positions are valid within the school.

Key Terms
لعنت (la'nat): Curse; being expelled from Allah's mercy. The text discusses its permissibility on specific individuals.
قطع رحمی (qat' al-rahmi): Severing family ties; used as a proof that Yazid merited curse due to killing Husayn.
واقعہ حرہ (waqi'at al-harrah): The battle of Harrah (63 AH) where Yazid's forces attacked Madinah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the threefold classification in the passage, which type of cursing is impermissible?
A) Cursing with a general attribute like 'cursed be the disbelievers'
B) Cursing a known eternal disbeliever like Pharaoh
C) Cursing a specific person whose death upon disbelief is not known
D) Cursing someone for a minor sin like tattooing

Key Takeaway
Cursing a specific historical figure like Yazid is a matter of ijtihad; the difference arises from how one applies general textual curses to specific persons and the epistemological caution required for such severe pronouncements.

The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute on Mutashabihat: Waw Isti'nafiyya vs 'Atfiyya
Explaining wisdom and resolving the waw dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the waw in Quran 3:7 and explain the wisdom of mutashabihat as a test for scholars.

Core Idea
The waw in 'wa al-rasikhun' determines whether scholars know the interpretation of mutashabihat—a test of submission.

This passage addresses a classic usul dispute: does Quran 3:7 exclude scholars from knowing the interpretation of ambiguous verses (mutashabihat) or include them? The answer hinges on whether the waw before 'al-rasikhun' is inceptive (isti'nafiyya) or conjunctive ('atfiyya). The Hanafi position, which we will follow, treats it as inceptive, making the knowledge exclusive to Allah and turning the verse into a test for scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ayah and the point of ikhtilaf
Locate Quran 3:7 and note the phrase 'wa ma ya'lamu ta'wilahū illa Allahu wa al-rasikhun fi al-'ilm'. The dispute is whether the waw before 'al-rasikhun' joins them to Allah (so they know) or starts a new sentence (so they do not know).
The ayah is the foundational proof for both schools.
2
State the Hanafi position and its linguistic dalil
The Hanafis hold that the waw is isti'nafiyya (inceptive). Therefore, the first sentence ends at 'illa Allah', meaning only Allah knows the interpretation. The second sentence begins: 'And those firmly grounded in knowledge say...' The evidence is the required stop after 'illa Allah' for proper recitation.
This position respects the apparent syntactic break.
3
State the Shafi'i position and its linguistic dalil
The Shafi'is consider the waw as 'atfiyya (conjunctive), linking 'al-rasikhun' to 'Allah'. Thus, 'Allah and the rasikhun know its interpretation.' Their evidence is that the waw normally joins, and the rasikhun are capable of knowledge.
This view includes scholars in the knowledge of ta'wil.
4
Explain the wisdom (hikmah) as a test
The passage argues that the revelation of mutashabihat is a test for the rasikhun. They desire complete knowledge, but being prevented from interpreting mutashabihat tests their obedience. Those who stop (submit) succeed; those who insist on knowing fail.
This aligns with the Hanafi view: the test proves their inability to know.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference: Hanafis refrain from interpreting mutashabihat (tafwid), while Shafi'is engage in interpretation (ta'wil) within scholarly bounds. The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position of tafwid.
This affects how scholars approach ambiguous verses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نزول متشابہات میں حکمت متشابہات کے نزول میں حکمت یہ ہے کہ اس کے ذریعے راسخین فی العلم کو امتحان میں مبتلا کیا گیا ہے۔ قوله فان انزال المتشابھات :۔ اور اس عبارت میں صاحب توضیح اس بات کی دلیل بیان فرمارہے ہیں کہ راسخین فی العلم کے لیے متشابھات کس طرح امتحان ہیں۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ہمارے یعنی احناف کے نزدیک و یا علم تاویلہ الا اللہ پر وقف لازم ہے۔ اور والراسخون میں واؤ ابتدائیہ ہے۔ یعنی متشابھات کی مراد صرف اللہ تعالیٰ جانتے ہیں کسی اور کو اس کا علم نہیں۔ اور شوافع کے نزدیک والراسخون میں واو عاطفہ ہے۔ اور اس کا الا اللہ پر عطف ہے۔ یعنی متشابھات کی مراد اللہ بھی جانتے ہیں اور راسخین فی العلم بھی جانتے ہیں تو گویا متشابھات کا اتارنا ہمارے مذہب پر ہے۔ اور امتحان اس طرح ہے کہ دراصل ہر آدمی کی خواہش کی مخالفت میں امتحان ہوتا ہے۔ مثلاً جاہل کی خواہش ہے کہ علم حاصل نہ کریں اور ان کے لیے علم حاصل کرنے کا حکم دینا امتحان ہے اور راسخین فی العلم کی خواہش ہے کہ ہر بات کا علم حاصل ہو جائے ۔ تو ان کے لئے متشابھات میں غور و فکر کرنے سے روکنے میں امتحان ہے۔ پس جو رک گیا ۔ وہ کامیاب جو نہ رکا وہ نا کام ۔
Wisdom in the revelation of mutashabihat: The wisdom in revealing mutashabihat is that through it, the firmly grounded in knowledge (al-rasikhun fi al-'ilm) are subjected to a test. His statement 'fa-inna inzal al-mutashabihat': In this phrase, the author of al-Tawdih is providing evidence for how mutashabihat are a test for the rasikhun. The summary is that according to us, the Hanafis, the proper stop is after 'illa Allah' and the waw in 'wa al-rasikhun' is isti'nafiyya (inceptive), meaning only Allah knows the interpretation of mutashabihat, no one else. According to the Shafi'is, the waw is 'atfiyya (conjunctive) and it is conjoined to 'illa Allah', meaning Allah and the rasikhun know the interpretation. Thus, the revelation of mutashabihat is consistent with our madhhab. The test is that truly every person is tested by opposing their desires. For example, the ignorant person desires not to acquire knowledge, and commanding them to acquire knowledge is a test. The rasikhun desire to know everything, so preventing them from delving into mutashabihat is a test. So whoever stops is successful; whoever does not stop is unsuccessful.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage presents a usul dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the interpretation of Quranic verse 3:7 about mutashabihat (ambiguous verses) and the phrase 'wa al-rasikhun fi al-'ilm' (and those firmly grounded in knowledge). The Hanafi position is that the waw is inceptive (isti'nafiyya), so the sentence means 'No one knows its interpretation except Allah. And those firmly grounded in knowledge say...' Thus, only Allah knows the true interpretation. The Shafi'i position is that the waw is conjunctive, so the phrase means 'Allah and those firmly grounded in knowledge know its interpretation.' The text then explains the wisdom behind this: the revelation of mutashabihat serves as a test for the rasikhun by preventing them from pursuing what they desire (complete knowledge). The test is successful for those who stop researching into mutashabihat, while those who continue are unsuccessful. This highlights an important usul principle: that some matters are beyond human comprehension, and the scholars are tested by their submission to this limitation.

Key Terms
متشابہات (mutashabihat): Quranic verses that are ambiguous or allegorical, whose interpretation is not definitively known.
راسخون فی العلم (al-rasikhun fi al-'ilm): Those firmly grounded in knowledge, i.e., deeply learned scholars.
واو ابتدائیہ (waw isti'nafiyya): The 'waw' that begins a new independent sentence, not connecting to the previous clause.
واو عاطفہ (waw 'atfiyya): The conjunctive 'waw' that joins words or phrases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the wisdom (hikmah) behind revealing mutashabihat?
A) To increase the reward of scholars who struggle to understand them.
B) To test the rasikhun by preventing them from pursuing their desire to know everything.
C) To allow scholars to display their interpretive skills.
D) To make the Quran difficult for the ignorant.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi interpretation of the waw as inceptive in Quran 3:7 establishes that the interpretation of mutashabihat is known only to Allah, and the scholars' submission to this limitation is a divinely ordained test.

Resolving the Objection of Tarjih Bila Murajjih Between Basmalah and Tahmid
Resolving an objection about preference between basmalah and tahmid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Hanafi usul principle of tarjīḥ bilā murajjiḥ is avoided when two things have different aspects of preference, and apply this reasoning to similar cases of conflicting preferences.

Core Idea
Equality can coexist with different preferences when each is superior in a distinct aspect.

In this passage, an objection is raised: if tahmid is part of the book but tasmiyah is not, then there is an unjustified preference (tarjih bila murajjih) and equality is lost. The commentator resolves this by showing that tasmiyah is preferred in mention and recitation, while tahmid is preferred in being part of the book. Thus, each has a distinct advantage, and overall equality is maintained. This illustrates a key principle in Hanafi usul: preference must be examined across all relevant aspects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objector claims that if tahmid is part of the book and tasmiyah is not, then there is an imbalance leading to tarjih bila murajjih (preference without a preponderant factor), which is rationally invalid. Additionally, the intended equality between them would be lost.
2
Recognize the two aspects of preference
The commentator points out that preference can be viewed from multiple angles. Here, two aspects are considered: (1) precedence in mention and recitation, (2) being made part of the book. Each phrase has an advantage in one aspect.
This shows that 'preference' is not monolithic.
3
Analyze the resolution
Tasmiyah is preponderant (raajih) in being mentioned first, while tahmid is preponderant in being included as part of the book. Therefore, neither is absolutely superior; they are equal in overall merit when considering both aspects together.
4
Conclude the principle
Thus, equality is achieved without violating the prohibition of tarjih bila murajjih, because each preference is justified by a valid preponderant factor (murajjih) in its respective aspect.
This principle is used in Hanafi usul to reconcile conflicting evidences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سوال:۔ اس صورت میں جب تحمید کتاب کا جز ہولیکن تسمیہ کتاب کا جز نہ ہوتو تسمیہ اور حمی میں ترجیح بلا مربح لا زم آئے گی۔ نیز دونوں میں تسویہ اور برابری پیدا نہیں ہوگی۔ حالانکہ ماقبل میں گزر چکا ہے کہ دونوں میں تسویہ مقصود ہے۔ جواب :۔ اس لحاظ سے کہ بسم اللہ کو ذکر اور پڑھنے میں مقدم کیا ہے۔ تو تسمیہ رائج اور تحمید مرجوح ہے۔ اور اس لحاظ سے کہ تحمید کو کتاب کا جز بنایا ہے۔ تسمیہ کو کتاب کا جز نہیں بنایا۔ تو تحمید راج اور تسمیہ مرجوح ہے۔ خلاصہ یہ ہے ایک اعتبار سے تسمیہ رائج ہے اور ایک صورت میں تحمید راجح ہے لہذا دونوں میں تسویہ اور برابری پائی گئی ۔ فلا اعتراض علیہ۔
Question: In this case, when tahmid is part of the book but tasmiyah is not part of the book, then preference without a preponderant factor (tarjih bila murajjih) would be necessary between tasmiyah and tahmid, and also equality between them would not be achieved, whereas it has passed before that equality is intended. Answer: From the aspect that bismillah is given precedence in mention and recitation, tasmiyah is preponderant and tahmid is outweighed. And from the aspect that tahmid is made part of the book while tasmiyah is not made part, tahmid is preponderant and tasmiyah is outweighed. The conclusion is that in one respect tasmiyah is preponderant, and in one aspect tahmid is preponderant, so equality between them is achieved. Thus no objection.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage addresses a follow-up objection to the previous discussion. If tahmid (alhamdulillah) is part of the book but tasmiyah (bismillah) is not, then there would be an unjustified preference (tarjih bila murajjih) unless they are equal. The commentator resolves this by showing that preference is relative: tasmiyah is preferred in being mentioned first (in recitation), while tahmid is preferred in being included as part of the book. Thus, each has an advantage in a different aspect, so they are equal overall. This preserves the intended equality between the two phrases.

Key Terms
ترجیح بلا مربح (tarjīḥ bilā murajjiḥ): Giving preference to one thing over another without a valid preponderant factor, which is rationally impermissible.
تسویہ (taswiyah): Equality or making equal between two things.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) By making both part of the book
B) By reciting both equally often
C) Tasmiyah is preferred in mention and recitation, tahmid is preferred in being part of the book
D) By omitting both from the book

Key Takeaway
Equality can be achieved when two items have different types of preference, each justified by a valid preponderant factor, avoiding the fallacy of tarjih bila murajjih.

Resolving Equality Between Tashmiya and Tahmid
Answering an objection about equality between tashmiya and tahmid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of tarjih to resolve apparent conflicts by identifying valid murajjih from different perspectives.

Core Idea
A preference without a preponderator is invalid, but when each element is preponderant in different respects, balance is achieved.

This passage tackles a subtle objection: if tahmid is part of the Quranic text but tashmiya is not, why are they considered equal? The answer reveals a key usul technique: preference can be based on multiple aspects, so both can be preponderant simultaneously—each from a different angle. This demonstrates how Hanafi usul resolves apparent contradictions by examining the underlying preponderating factors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
The objection states that if one element (tahmid) is part of the book while another (tashmiya) is not, then preference without a clear preponderator (tarjih bila murajjih) would arise, violating the earlier claim of equality.
The key term is 'tarjih bila murajjih'—an invalid preference in usul.
2
Locate the Murajjih for Each Element
The answer provides two different aspects: tashmiya is given precedence in recitation (qira'ah), so it is preponderant in that respect. Tahmid is part of the Quranic text, so it is preponderant in terms of being a component of the book.
Each aspect is a valid murajjih (preponderating factor).
3
Analyze How Multiple Aspects Resolve the Conflict
Since each element is preponderant from a different perspective, there is no single preference that would create inequality. Instead, the overall equality is preserved because the preponderances are balanced across different dimensions.
This avoids the fallacy of tarjih bila murajjih.
4
Conclude Why Equality Is Achieved
Thus, the objection is resolved: tashmiya and tahmid are equal in the sense that each has its own valid basis for preponderance, fulfilling the intended balance.
The Hanafi principle here is that multiplicity of aspects allows coexistence of preferences.

سوال:۔ اس صورت میں جب تحمید کتاب کا جز ہو لیکن تسمیہ کتاب کا جز نہ ہو تو تسمیہ اور تحمید میں ترجیح بلا مرجح لازم آئے گی۔ نیز دونوں میں تسویہ اور برابری پیدا نہیں ہوگی۔ حالانکہ ماقبل میں گزر چکا ہے کہ دونوں میں تسویہ مقصود ہے۔ جواب:۔ اس لحاظ سے کہ بسم اللہ کو ذکر اور پڑھنے میں مقدم کیا ہے۔ تو تسمیہ راجح اور تحمید مرجوح ہے۔ اور اس لحاظ سے کہ تحمید کو کتاب کا جز بنایا ہے۔ تسمیہ کو کتاب کا جز نہیں بنایا۔ تو تحمید راجح اور تسمیہ مرجوح ہے۔ خلاصہ یہ ہے ایک اعتبار سے تسمیہ راجح ہے اور ایک صورت میں تحمید راجح ہے لہذا دونوں میں تسویہ اور برابری پائی گئی ۔ فلا اعتراض علیہ۔
Question: In this case, when tahmid is part of the book but tashmiya is not part of the book, then a preference without a preponderator would become necessary. Also, equality and balance between the two would not be achieved, while it has passed earlier that equality between the two is intended. Answer: From the aspect that 'Bismillah' is given precedence in mention and recitation, tashmiya is preponderant and tahmid is preponderated. And from the aspect that tahmid is made part of the book while tashmiya is not made part of the book, tahmid is preponderant and tashmiya is preponderated. The summary is that in one respect tashmiya is preponderant and in one respect tahmid is preponderant, so equality and balance between the two is achieved. Thus no objection arises.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis resolving an objection regarding the relative preference of tashmiya (saying 'Bismillah') and tahmid (saying 'Alhamdulillah') in the Quranic context. The objection states that if tahmid is part of the book (i.e., Surah al-Fatihah) but tashmiya is not, then one should be preferred over the other without a clear preponderator, contradicting the earlier claim that both are equal. The answer explains that preference is relative: tashmiya is preponderant in terms of being recited first, while tahmid is preponderant in terms of being an integral part of the Surah. Thus, from different viewpoints, each is preponderant, achieving equality overall. This reasoning follows the Hanafi usul principle of considering multiple aspects to resolve apparent conflicts.

Key Terms
تسمیہ (tashmiya): Uttering 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim'
تحمید (tahmid): Uttering 'Alhamdulillah' as part of Surah al-Fatihah
ترجیح بلا مرجح (tarjih bila murajjih): Preference without a preponderating factor, which is considered invalid in usul

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is there no objection to the equality between tashmiya and tahmid?
A) Because both are part of the book equally
B) Because tashmiya is preponderant in recitation and tahmid in being part of the book
C) Because tahmid is always preponderant over tashmiya
D) Because the objection is invalid

Key Takeaway
Multi-aspect tarjih resolves apparent conflicts: each element can be preponderant in a different respect, preserving balance without invalid preference.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
