Is 'Al-Kalim' a Plural or a Genus? The Hanafi Analysis
Presenting and analyzing the dispute about the word 'الكلم'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two positions in the dispute over 'الكلم', state the five proofs for the majority (genus) view, and evaluate the significance of the alternative classification (collective noun).

Core Idea
Linguistic classification of a word affects how general rulings are derived from it in usul al-fiqh.

The Arabic word 'الكلم' (words) appears in the Qur'an and is used in legal texts. Scholars disagree whether it is a plural (جمع) or a genus (جنس) – a difference that impacts how we derive general rules from verses like 'إليه يصعد الكلم الطيب'. In this lesson, we examine the arguments, focusing on the five proofs that lead the majority of Hanafi usulis to treat it as a genus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opposing positions
Determine what the minority (plural) and majority (genus) claim. Note the minority's simple proof: it always indicates three or more.
The minority view is presented briefly; the majority offers five detailed proofs.
2
Examine the five proofs of the majority
For each proof, identify the linguistic criterion (e.g., adjective agreement, word pattern, type of plural, diminutive form, pronoun reference) and how it disproves plural classification.
These proofs are dalil naqli and linguistic reasoning.
3
Analyze the question raised about a collective noun
The passage questions whether negating plural automatically implies genus. Consider the third possibility: 'اسم جمع' (collective noun).
This shows thoroughness: genus is not the only alternative.
4
Understand the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
How does treating 'الكلم' as genus vs. plural affect interpretation of texts? For example, a genus allows the word to be general and take masculine/feminine adjectives; a plural would restrict it to a feminine pattern.
This matters for deriving general rulings from general words (عموم).
5
Synthesize the Hanafi stance
Summarize why the majority view is stronger linguistically and how the question of collective noun enriches the analysis without overturning the genus classification.
The mufta bihi (operative position) is that 'الكلم' is a genus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اختلاف ائمہ میں ماہو المختار عند التاريخ
بعض حضرات کے نزدیک الکلم جمع ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس کا اطلاق ہمیشہ تین یا تین سے زائد پر ہوتا ہے۔ اگر یہ جنس ہوتا تو اس کا اطلاق واحد پر بھی ہوتا کیونکہ جنس قلیل و کثیر سب پر بولی جاتی ہے۔ اور جمہور کہتے ہیں کہ الکلم جنس ہے۔ ان کی پانچ دلیلیں ہیں۔ دلیل (1) یہ ہے کہ ہر وہ جمع کہ اس جمع اور اس کے واحد کے درمیان تا سے فرق کیا جاتا ہے۔ وہ جنس ہوتی ہے یعنی لفظوں کے اعتبار سے مفرد اور معنی کے لحاظ سے جمع ۔ اس اعتبار سے اس کی صفت مذکر و مونث دونوں طرح آ سکتی ہے۔ جیسے نخل خاویہ اور نخل منقعر ۔ اگر الکلم جمع کا صیغہ ہوتا تو اس کی صفت مذکر نہ آتی ۔ حالانکہ قرآن میں اس کی صفت مذکر آئی ہے۔ اليه يصعد الكلم الطيب -
دلیل (۲):- یہ ہے کہ گلیم فعل کے وزن پر ہے۔ اور فعل کا وزن جمع کے اور ان میں سے نہیں ہے تو معلوم ہوا کہ یہ جنس ہے جمع نہیں۔ دلیل (۳) : یہ ہے کہ یہ جمع ہے تو ہم پوچھتے ہیں کہ یہ جمع سالم ہے یا جمع مکسر ۔ اگر آپ کہیں کہ یہ جمع سالم ہے تو یہ درست نہیں کیونکہ جمع سالم واؤ نون یا الف تا کے ساتھ آتی ہے۔ اور اگر آپ کہیں کہ یہ جمع مکسر ہے تو یہ بھی درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ جمع مکسر وہ ہوتی ہے جس میں واحد کا صیغہ سالم نہ رہے اور یہاں ایسا نہیں ہے۔ معلوم ہوا کہ الکلم جمع نہیں ہے۔ دلیل (۴):۔ اگر یہ صیغہ کے لحاظ سے جمع ہو تو تصغیر کے لیے رد ہونا چاہیے تھا۔ مفرد کی طرف اور اس کی تصغیر کلمتہ سے آتی اور حلیمہ ہوتی حالانکہ اس کی تصغیر اس کے لفظ سے کلیم آتی ہے۔
دلیل (۵):۔ اگر یہ صیغہ کے لحاظ سے جمع ہو تو اس کی طرف مونث کی ضمیر راجع ہونی چاہیے تھی ۔ حالانکہ اس کی طرف مذکر کی ضمیر لوٹائی جا رہی ہے۔ جیسے یحرفون الکلم عن مواضعہ ۔
سوال:۔ یہ ہے کہ دلائل سے اتنا ثابت ہوتا ہے کہ یہ جمع نہیں ہے لیکن اس سے یہ تو لازم نہیں آتا کہ جب یہ جمع نہیں تو جنس ہو کیونکہ یہ بھی ہو سکتا ہے کہ یہ اسم جمع ہو۔
Dispute among imams and that which is chosen according to the date. Some scholars say that 'الكلم' (words) is a plural. Their proof is that it always applies to three or more. If it were a genus, it would also apply to the singular because genus applies to few and many. And the majority say that 'الكلم' is a genus. They have five proofs. Proof (1): Every plural where the difference between the plural and its singular is made by taa, that is a genus, meaning it is verbally singular and in meaning plural. Accordingly, its adjective can be both masculine and feminine, like 'نخل خاویہ' (barren palm trees) and 'نخل منقعر' (uprooted palm trees). If 'الكلم' were a plural form, its adjective would not be masculine, yet in the Quran, its adjective is masculine: 'إليْه يَصْعَدُ الْكَلِمُ الطَّيِّبُ' (To Him ascends good speech). Proof (2): It is that 'الكلم' is on the pattern of 'فَعَل', and the pattern 'فَعَل' is not among the patterns of plurals, so it is known that it is a genus, not a plural. Proof (3): If it is a plural, then we ask: is it a sound plural or broken plural? If you say it is sound plural, it is not correct because sound plural has waw-nun or alif-ta. And if you say it is broken plural, it is also not correct because broken plural is that in which the singular form is not preserved, and here it is not the case. So it is known that 'الكلم' is not a plural. Proof (4): If it were a plural in form, then for diminution it would have to be referred to the singular, and its diminutive would come from 'كلمتة' as 'حلیمہ'? But its diminutive comes from its own word as 'كليم'. Proof (5): If it were a plural in form, then a feminine pronoun would have to refer to it, but a masculine pronoun is referred to it, as in 'يُحَرِّفُونَ الْكَلِمَ عَنْ مَوَاضِعِهِ' (They distort words from their places). Question: It is that from the proofs it is established that it is not a plural, but it does not follow that when it is not plural, it must be a genus, because it could also be a collective noun.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute about the linguistic classification of the word 'الكلم' (words). Some scholars hold that it is a plural (جمع) because it always indicates three or more. They reason that if it were a genus (جنس), it would also apply to a single word, which it does not. The majority (جمہور) argue that 'الكلم' is a genus, providing five proofs: (1) In the Quran, 'الكلم' is described with a masculine adjective (الطيب), whereas a true plural of non-intelligent things takes a feminine adjective. (2) The word pattern 'فَعَل' is not a plural pattern. (3) It is neither a sound plural (due to lack of suffixes) nor a broken plural (the singular form 'كلمة' is preserved). (4) Its diminutive 'كليم' is formed directly from itself, not from a singular, indicating it is not a plural. (5) A masculine pronoun (مواضعہ) refers to it, whereas a plural of non-intelligent things would take a feminine pronoun. The passage concludes with a question (سوال) noting that these proofs only negate 'الكلم' being a plural; it could still be a collective noun (اسم جمع) rather than a genus. This dispute is important in Hanafi usul for determining how to interpret the generality (عموم) of 'الكلم' in legal texts.

Key Terms
الكلم (al-kalim): The Arabic word for 'words', here debated as plural or genus.
جمع (jama'): Plural as defined previously: applies to three or more with singular from same root.
جنس (jins): Genus: applies to both few and many, with singular often marked by taa.
اسم جمع (ism jama'): Collective noun: applies to three or more but lacks singular from same root.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which proof does the majority use from the Quran to argue that 'الكلم' is a genus, not a plural?
A) It is on the pattern 'فَعَل' which is not a plural pattern.
B) Its diminutive is formed directly without reverting to singular.
C) A masculine adjective is used with it in the verse.
D) It cannot be classified as sound or broken plural.

Key Takeaway
The classification of 'الكلم' as a genus (جنس) rather than a plural (جمع) is supported by multiple linguistic proofs and affects how general rulings are derived from texts containing it.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Classifying 'al-Kalim': Jins or Jam'? A Hanafi Usul Analysis
Analysis of arguments for and against 'al-Kalim' as plural

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the five Hanafi linguistic proofs to classify 'al-Kalim' as a collective noun (jins) rather than a true plural (jam'), and evaluate the justification for the particle 'in' (if) in the matn.

Core Idea
A word's adjective and pronoun agreement, morphological pattern, and diminutive form reveal its true grammatical category.

In Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh, precise linguistic analysis is the foundation for interpreting divine texts. This passage from Al-Tarweeh debates whether the Quranic word 'al-Kalim' (speech/words) is a true plural (jam') or a collective noun (jins). The dispute is not merely grammatical; it affects how we understand verses about divine speech and the interpretation of general commands. The commentator presents five persuasive proofs that 'al-Kalim' is jins, then defends the matn's use of the particle 'in' (if) against critics, offering two sophisticated justifications rooted in the realities of scholarly ikhtilaf and pedagogical address.

Guided Path
1
State the disputed term and positions
Identify that some grammarians consider 'al-Kalim' a plural, while the majority (Jumhoor) call it a collective noun (jins). Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: if it is plural, it emphasizes multiplicity; if jins, it denotes the concept of speech.
The Quranic usage of the word is the key to resolving this ikhtilaf.
2
Analyze the five proofs for jins
For each proof (adjective gender, fa'l pattern, sound/broken plural tests, diminutive, pronoun gender), note the specific evidence from Quran (35:10, 4:46) and standard Arabic morphology. The proofs collectively show that 'al-Kalim' behaves like a singular masculine noun.
Proof 1 (adjective) and Proof 5 (pronoun) are directly from Quranic text.
3
Examine the objection and rebuttal
The objection that 'al-Kalim' might be an ism jam' (collective noun without singular) is rebutted because it has a known singular 'kalimah'. Refine your understanding of the categories: jam', jins, and ism jam'.
This step reinforces the precision of Arabic grammatical classification.
4
Address the criticism of the matn's wording
Critics argue that since the classification is certain, using 'in' (if) implies inappropriate doubt. The commentator provides two answers: (a) due to conflicting authorities (Sibawayh vs. Farra/Akhfash), and (b) due to the addressee's doubt. Weigh the strength of each answer.
The second answer is considered stronger; it shows 'in' can be used for the addressee's doubt, not the author's.
5
Conclude the Hanafi position
The Hanafi position is that 'al-Kalim' is certainly jins, and the matn's use of 'in' is justified. Recognize that this analysis is an example of how Hanafi usul integrates grammar, Quranic evidence, and critical reasoning.
This conclusion is mufta bihi (operative) for Hanafi usul.

جواب:۔ یہ ہے کہ جس طرح یہ جمع نہیں ہے اسم جمع بھی نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ اسم جمع کا مفرد نہیں پایا جاتا اور اس کا مفرد کلمہ پایا جاتا ہے۔ بعض حضرات کی دلیل کا جواب :۔ یہ ہے کہ کلم اصل میں تو قلیل وکثیر سب پر بولا جاتا ہے۔ لیکن اس میں کثیر کو غلبہ دے دیا گیا ہے اس لیے بعض لوگوں نے سمجھ لیا کہ شاید یہ جمع ہے۔ جنس نہیں ہے تاریخ نے یہاں جمہور کے مذہب کو ترجیح دی ہے۔ نتیجہ یہ نکلا کہ علم میں جمعیت معنویہ کا پایا جانا یقینی ہے معنی جنسی کے اعتبار سے اور جمعیت صیغوی ( جمع حقیقی ) کا نہ پایا جانا یقینی ہے۔ پس اس کے تمر تمرہ کی طرح جمع ہونے میں شک نہیں کرنا چاہیے بلکہ یقیناً اسی طرح ہے اور رتب نسب کی طرح ہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ رتبہ اور نسبتہ کی جمع صیغوی ہیں۔ کیا ماتن کا ان کان جمعا میں کلمہ شک استعمال کرنا درست ہے؟ ففی قولہ ان کان :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا آخری حصہ ہے۔ غرض شارح ماتن پر اعتراض کرنا ہے ۔ جنس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جب دلائل سے یہ بات ثابت ہوگئی کہ اس میں کسی قسم کا شک نہیں ہے کہ الکلم لفظ مفرد ہے۔ اور معنا جمع ہے۔ جب یہ بات یقینی تھی ۔ تو ماتن کا کلمہ شک استعمال کرنا درست نہیں کیونکہ ماتن نے کہا ان کان جمعا اور ان شک کے لیے آتا ہے ۔ ماتن کو ان کان جمعا کی بجائے وان کان جمعا کہنا چاہیے تھا۔ پھر معنی ہوتا ہے۔ کہ کم اگر چہ جمع ہے ۔ اس صورت میں شک لازم نہ آتا۔ جواب (۱):۔ ماتن کا کلمہ شک استعمال کرنا بجا ہے۔ کیونکہ ائمہ فن کے اقوال میں تعارض ہے۔ چنانچہ سیبویہ فرماتے ہیں جمع اور اسم جمع اور جنس میں فرق ہے۔ جبکہ فراء اور انخفش کہتے ہیں کہ ہر وہ اسم جس کا واحد اور مفرد ہے چاہے وہ جنس کیوں نہ ہو وہ سب جمع ہیں۔ خلاصہ یہ ہے مصنف نے ائمہ فن کے اقوال کے تعارض کی وجہ سے کلمہ شک ذکر کیا ہے۔ لیکن یہ جواب کمزور ہے کیونکہ تحقیق سے جب یہ بات ثابت ہو گئی کہ سیبویہ کا مذہب حق ہے تو پھر اقوال آئمہ کے تعارض کی وجہ سے شک کرنا مناسب نہیں۔ جواب (۲):- یہ ہے کہ کلمہ ان کو مخاطب کے شک کی وجہ سے ذکر کیا ہے ۔ کیونکہ لفظ ان جسطرح متکلم کے شک کے لیے مستعمل ہوتا ہے۔ اسی طرح مخاطب کے شک کے لیے بھی استعمال ہوتا ہے۔ اب مطلب یہ ہوگا۔ کہ تمہیں کلم کے جمع حقیقی و
According to some [scholars], 'al-Kalim' is a plural. Their evidence is that it is always used for three or more. If it were a collective (jins), it would also be used for a single [item] because Jins is used for both few and many. The majority (Jumhoor) say that 'al-Kalim' is a collective (jins). They have five proofs. Proof (1): Every plural that is distinguished from its singular by a ta [marbutah] is a Jins, i.e., it is singular in word and plural in meaning. Accordingly, its adjective can be both masculine and feminine, like 'nakhil khawiyah' and 'nakhil munqa'ir'. If 'al-Kalim' were a plural form, its adjective would not be masculine, yet in the Qur'an its adjective comes as masculine: 'ilayhi yas'adu al-kalimu al-tayyib' (to Him ascends good speech). Proof (2): 'al-Kalim' is on the pattern of 'fa'l', and the pattern 'fa'l' is not among the patterns of plurals, so it is known that it is a Jins, not a plural. Proof (3): If it were a plural, we ask whether it is a sound plural or a broken plural. If you say it is a sound plural, that is not correct because sound plurals come with waw-nun or alif-ta. And if you say it is a broken plural, that is also not correct because a broken plural is one in which the singular form is not preserved, and that is not the case here. Hence it is known that 'al-Kalim' is not a plural. Proof (4): If it were a plural in form, it should revert to the singular for diminutive, and its diminutive would come from 'kalimah' and would be 'kulaymah', whereas its diminutive comes from its own word as 'kulayyim'. Proof (5): If it were a plural in form, the pronoun referring to it should be feminine, whereas a masculine pronoun is used, as in 'yuharrifuna al-kalima 'an mawadi'ihi' (they distort words from their places). Question: From the proofs, it is established that it is not a plural, but that does not necessarily mean it is a Jins, because it could also be an 'ism jam'' (collective noun). Answer: Just as it is not a plural, it cannot be an 'ism jam'' because the singular of 'ism jam'' is not found, whereas its singular 'kalimah' is found. Reply to the evidence of some [scholars]: The word 'kalim' originally applies to both few and many, but the preponderance of usage for many caused some to think it is a plural, not a Jins. The author (Tariq) here preferred the view of the majority. The conclusion is that in [the word] 'ilm', the presence of a collective meaning is certain in terms of Jins meaning, and the absence of a morphological plural (true plural) is certain. So one should not doubt that it is like 'tamr' and 'tamrah' in being [a collective], but rather it is certainly so, and they are like 'rutab' and 'nusub', because these are morphological plurals of 'rutbah' and 'nisbah'. Is it correct for the author of the matn to use the word of doubt in 'in kana jam'an'? 'fi qawlihi in kana': This is the last part of the commentary's expression. The aim is that the commentator objects to the author of the matn. The gist is that when it has been established from proofs that there is no doubt that 'al-Kalim' is singular in word and plural in meaning, since this matter is certain, then the author's use of the word of doubt is not correct, because he said 'in kana jam'an' and 'in' is for doubt. The author should have said 'wa in kana jam'an' instead of 'in kana jam'an'. Then the meaning would be: 'even if it is plural'; in that case, no doubt would be implied. Answer (1): The author's use of the word of doubt is justified because there is a conflict among the authorities of the field. Indeed, Sibawayh says there is a difference between plural, 'ism jam'', and Jins, while Al-Farra' and Al-Akhfash say that every noun that has a singular—even if it is Jins—is a plural. The conclusion is that the author mentioned the word of doubt due to the conflict of authorities. However, this answer is weak because once investigation establishes that Sibawayh's view is correct, then doubt due to conflict of authorities is not appropriate. Answer (2): This is that the word 'in' is mentioned due to the addressee's doubt, because the word 'in' is used for the speaker's doubt and similarly for the addressee's doubt. Now the meaning would be: 'You [the addressee] doubt whether 'al-Kalim' is a true plural or...' (cut off).
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage from the sharh (commentary) engages in a detailed linguistic-legal analysis of the word 'al-Kalim' (speech/words), which appears in Quranic verses like 'ilayhi yas'adu al-kalimu al-tayyib' (35:10) and 'yuharrifuna al-kalima 'an mawadi'ihi' (4:46). The discussion exemplifies how Hanafi usul scholars rigorously analyze the Arabic language to derive rulings and resolve ambiguities. The passage has two main parts: first, a dispute about whether 'al-Kalim' is a true plural (jam') or a collective noun (jins); second, a critique of the matn's wording 'in kana jam'an' (if it is plural) and whether using the particle 'in' (indicating doubt) is appropriate given that the matter is settled. The commentator sides with the majority (Jumhoor) that 'al-Kalim' is jins, not jam', using five proofs based on morphology, adjective agreement, plural patterns, diminutive forms, and pronoun gender. They then address an objection that it could be an 'ism jam'' (collective noun), replying that 'ism jam'' lacks a singular, whereas 'al-Kalim' has a singular 'kalimah'. The second part defends the matn's use of 'in' by pointing to scholarly disagreement (Sibawayh vs. Farra and Akhfash) or by interpreting 'in' as addressing the addressee's doubt. The passage concludes that 'al-Kalim' is certainly a collective in meaning, like 'tamr' (dates) and 'rutab' (fresh dates), and one should not doubt it.

Key Terms
الكلم (al-kalim): An Arabic noun meaning 'speech' or 'words', under analysis for whether it is a true plural (جمع) or a collective noun (جنس).
جنس (jins): A collective noun that is singular in form but plural in meaning, e.g., نخل (date-palms). It is distinguished from جمع by taking masculine adjectives and having a singular form (كلمة).
جمع (jam'): A plural form indicating three or more, either sound (جمع سالم) or broken (جمع مكسّر). The passage argues that 'الكلم' is not a جمع because it does not fit these patterns.
اسم جمع (ism jam'): A noun that has no singular form but indicates a plural meaning. The passage rejects this possibility for 'الكلم' because it has a singular 'كلمة'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority (جمہور) in the passage, which linguistic category does the word 'الكلم' belong to?
A) جمع سالم (sound plural)
B) جمع مكسّر (broken plural)
C) جنس (collective noun)
D) اسم جمع (collective noun without singular)

Key Takeaway
The precise linguistic classification of Quranic terms like 'al-Kalim' is essential for correct usul analysis; Hanafi scholars use morphological and syntactic evidence to determine whether a word is a true plural or a collective noun, and even settled rulings may be introduced with 'if' due to scholarly disagreement or pedagogical nuance.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
8 min
The Hierarchy of Kalam, Usul al-Fiqh, and Fiqh
Dispute over the ranking of three sciences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rationale for ranking kalam above usul al-fiqh above fiqh, and evaluate the objection to this ranking based on the nature of dependence (tawaqquf).

Core Idea
The ranking depends on the type of dependence: tool-dependence vs. root-branch dependence.

This lesson explores a methodological dispute within Hanafi usul al-fiqh regarding the relative merits of three core sciences: kalam (theology), usul al-fiqh (principles of jurisprudence), and fiqh (positive law). The commentator argues that kalam is highest, then usul, then fiqh, based on a chain of dependence. However, an objector challenges this reasoning by pointing to a counterexample: tafsir depends on grammar (nahw/sarf) but grammar is lower. This leads to a nuanced discussion about the types of dependence and the meaning of superiority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claimed hierarchy
State the ranking of the three sciences as presented in the passage: kalam is highest, then usul al-fiqh, then fiqh.
This is the position the commentator supports and defends.
2
Understand the proof from dependence
Trace the reasoning: fiqh depends on usul al-fiqh for universal proofs, and usul al-fiqh depends on kalam for knowledge of Allah and prophethood. In a root-branch relationship, the relied-upon (mawquf 'alayh) is superior to the dependent (mawquf).
This is a logical proof (talil), not a textual one.
3
Analyze the objection
The objector rejects the premise that the relied-upon is always superior. Counterexample: tafsir depends on grammar (nahw/sarf), yet grammar is considered lower in rank.
The objection attacks the universal claim that dependence implies superiority.
4
Examine the first response and its refutation
First response: Dependence is of two types—tool-dependence (where the tool is lower) and root-branch dependence (where the root is higher). The relationship between fiqh and usul is claimed to be root-branch. However, this is refuted: if fiqh did not exist, usul would not have been compiled, making fiqh the root and usul the tool. Also, books of fiqh are placed above usul books.
The refutation shows that the first response is flawed and actually reverses the hierarchy.
5
Examine the second response
Allama Chalabi reinterprets 'superiority' as sequential learning: one must learn kalam first, then usul, then fiqh. This preserves practical precedence but abandons the claim of inherent honorific superiority.
This answer undermines the commentator's goal of elevating usul al-fiqh.

قولہ اذ بالشرعیہ :۔ یہ عبارت کا چوتھا حصہ ہے۔ اس میں ان اشیاء کے نعمت ہونے پر دلیل بیان کی ہے۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ شرعیہ جو کہ عام ہے۔ فقہ، اصول فقہ، علم کلام ، دلائل کلیہ، دلائل تفصیلہ اس سے دینا کا کام چلتا ہے ۔ اور آخرت میں ثواب ملتا ہے۔ اور فقہ کے دقیق ہونے سے علماء کے درجات بلند ہوں گے اور قیامت کے دن اس کو بہت بڑا اجر ملے گا۔ تو معلوم ہوا کہ یہ بہت بڑی نعمتیں ہیں۔ بیان درجات علوم ثلاثہ یعنی سے کم ہے۔ خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ سب سے اونچا مرتبہ علم کلام کا ہے۔ اس سے نچلا درجہ اصول فقہ کا ہے اور اس سے کم درجہ علم فقہ کا ہے۔ دلیل: یہ ہے کہ علم اصول فقہ میں بحث ہوتی ہے۔ ادلتہ کلیہ سے۔ اور فقہ میں بحث ہوتی ہے احکام جزئیہ سے ۔ اور احکام جزئیہ کی معرفت موقوف ہے اولہ کلیہ کی معرفت پر پس علم فقہ یہ موقوف ہوا علم اصول فقہ پر ۔ لہذا علم اصول فقہ کا مرتبہ زائد ہوا علم فقہ پر موقوف علیہ ہونے کی وجہ ہے۔ اور ادلہ کلیہ کی معرفت موقوف ہے۔ اللہ کی ذات وصفات و نبوت و رسالت کی معرفت پر پس علم اصول فقہ موقوف ہوا علم کلام پر اور موقوف علیہ عظیم الشان ہوتا ہے۔ موقوف سے الہذا علم کلام کا مرتبہ زائد ہوا علم اصول فقہ پر ۔ باقی رہا یہ کہ متن میں علوم ثلثہ کے مراتب کی طرف اشارہ کیسے ہوا۔ وہ اس طرح کہ ماتن نے کہا اصول الشرعیہ الخ کہ اصول فقہ کوفقہ کے لیے اصل قرار دیا۔ اور مٹی کا اصل بھی سے فائق ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا علم اصول فقہ یہ فائق ہو اعلم فقہ سے پھر علم کلام کو مبانی قرار دیا ہے علم اصول فقہ کا۔ لہذا علم کلام مبنی علیہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اعلیٰ مرتبہ پر ہوا اور اس طرح علم کلام فائق ہوا علم اصول فقہ پر۔ سوال :۔ اس بات کو ہم تسلیم نہیں کرتے کہ موقوف علیہ موقوف پر مرتبہ مقدم ہوتا ہے۔ اس لیے کہ علم تفسیر کا سمجھنا موقوف ہے۔ علم صرف و نحو پر حالانکہ علم صرف ونحو کا مرتبہ علم تفسیر سے کم ہے۔ جواب (۱): توقف کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ نمبر ا ۔ ذی آلتہ کا موقوف ہونا آلہ پر جیسے تو قف نجار اس کے آلات پر اور مشروط کا موقوف ہونا شرط پر جیسے صلوۃ کا تو قف وضو پر تو اس صورت میں موقوف علیہ کا موقوف پر مرتبہ مقدم ہونا درست نہیں ہے۔ جیسے تفسیر موقوف ہے صرف و نحو پر نمبر ۲ - فرع کا موقوف ہونا اصل پر۔ اس صورت میں موقوف علیہ موقوف پر مرتبہ مقدم ہوتا ہے یہاں بھی دوسرا معنی مراد ہے لیکن یہ جواب درست نہیں کیونکہ یہاں تو قف الفقہ علی الاصول توقف الفرع علی الاصل کے قبیل سے نہیں بلکہ یہ بھی توقف ذی لا لہ علی الآلہ کے قبیل سے ہے کیونکہ یوں کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ اگر علم فقہ نہ ہوتا تو اصول فقہ کی تدوین ہی نہ ہوتی تو معلوم ہوا کہ فقہ اصل ہے اور اصول فرع اور آلہ ہے اور اس کی تائید اس سے بھی ہوتی ہے کہ اصول کی اضافت فقہ کی طرف مدح کے لئے ہے اس سے بھی فقہ کا اصل اور اشرف ہونا معلوم ہوتا ہے نیز صاحب غنیۃ نے لکھا ہے کہ فقہ کی کتابیں قرآت میں علم کلام اصول فقہ پر مقدم ہے اور اصول فقہ کا تعلم فقہ پر مقدم ہے کیونکہ موقوف کی معرفت موقوف علیہ کی معرفت کے بغیر نہیں ہوتی لیکن اس جواب سے ظاہر ہے کہ ماتن و شارح جو اصول فقہ کی شرافت کو بلند کرنا چاہتے ہیں وہ منہدم ہو کر رہ جاتی ہے۔
His statement: 'by the shar'i' — this is the fourth part of the phrase. In it, he provides evidence that these things are blessings. The gist is that shar'i sciences, which are general — fiqh, usul al-fiqh, kalam, universal proofs, detailed proofs — by means of them the affairs of religion are conducted, and in the hereafter reward is obtained. And due to the subtlety of fiqh, the ranks of scholars become elevated, and on the Day of Resurrection they will have a great reward. So it became known that these are great blessings. Statement about the ranks of the three sciences, namely kalam, usul al-fiqh, and fiqh. His statement: 'and in this speech' — this is the fifth part of the phrase. In it, the commentator explains the excellence of the text: that the text has indicated that the rank of usul al-fiqh is higher than fiqh, and lower than kalam. The summary is that the highest rank is of kalam, below it is usul al-fiqh, and below that is fiqh. The proof: In usul al-fiqh, discussion is about universal proofs, while in fiqh, discussion is about particular rulings. And knowledge of particular rulings depends on knowledge of universal proofs. So fiqh is dependent on usul al-fiqh. Hence the rank of usul al-fiqh is superior to fiqh because it is the relied-upon. And knowledge of universal proofs depends on knowledge of Allah's essence, attributes, prophethood, and messengership. So usul al-fiqh depends on kalam. And the relied-upon is greater than the dependent. Hence the rank of kalam is superior to usul al-fiqh. As for how the text indicated the ranks of the three sciences, it is as follows: the author said 'usul al-shar'iyyah' etc., making usul al-fiqh the root for fiqh. And the root is superior to the branch. Thus usul al-fiqh is superior to fiqh. Then he made kalam the foundation for usul al-fiqh. So kalam, being the foundation, attained a higher rank. Thus kalam became superior to usul al-fiqh. Objection: We do not accept that the relied-upon is superior to the dependent in rank. For understanding tafsir depends on nahw and sarf, yet the rank of nahw and sarf is lower than tafsir. Answer (1): Dependence is of two types. First: the dependent having a tool depends on the tool, like the carpenter depends on his tools, and the conditioned depends on the condition, like prayer depends on wudu. In this case, it is not correct that the relied-upon is superior to the dependent, like tafsir depends on nahw and sarf. Second: the branch depends on the root. In this case, the relied-upon is superior to the dependent. Here, too, the second meaning is intended. But this answer is not correct because the dependence of fiqh on usul is not of the type of branch on root. Rather, it is of the type of the dependent on the tool, because it can be said: if fiqh did not exist, usul al-fiqh would not have been compiled. So it becomes clear that fiqh is the root and usul is the branch and tool. This is supported also by the fact that the addition of usul to fiqh is for praise, which shows that fiqh is the root and more noble. Also, the author of Ghunyah wrote that books of fiqh should be placed above books of usul al-fiqh and even above books of kalam. Answer (2): Allama Chalabi gave this answer: the word 'superior' mentioned in the text means superiority in learning and seeking, i.e., kalam comes before usul al-fiqh in seeking and reading, and usul al-fiqh comes before fiqh. Because the knowledge of the dependent cannot be attained without knowledge of the relied-upon. But from this answer it is apparent that what the author and commentator wanted to elevate the nobility of usul al-fiqh is destroyed.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn discussing the virtues and ranking of three Islamic sciences: kalam (theology), usul al-fiqh (jurisprudence), and fiqh (positive law). The commentator explains that the matn indicates usul al-fiqh is higher than fiqh but lower than kalam. The reasoning is based on the concept of dependence (tawaqquf): fiqh depends on usul al-fiqh because usul provides the universal proofs (adillah kulliyyah) from which particular rulings (ahkam juz'iyyah) are derived; usul al-fiqh depends on kalam because kalam establishes the knowledge of God, His attributes, prophethood, etc., which are prerequisites for the universal proofs. Thus the relied-upon (mawquf 'alayhi) is superior to the dependent (mawquf). However, an objector points out an apparent counterexample: tafsir depends on nahw and sarf (grammar and morphology), but nahw and sarf are considered lower in rank than tafsir. The commentator presents two responses: First, dependence is of two types—tool-dependence (where the tool is lower) and root-branch dependence (where the root is higher). The objector's example is of the first type, while the relationship between the three sciences is claimed to be of the second type. However, this answer is refuted by noting that if there were no fiqh, usul al-fiqh would not have been compiled, indicating that fiqh is actually the root and usul is the tool. This is supported by the fact that books of fiqh are placed above books of usul in libraries. The second answer, from Allama Chalabi, reinterprets 'superiority' as sequential learning: one must first learn kalam, then usul, then fiqh. This preserves the practical precedence but undermines the intended honorific superiority. The passage thus critically examines the claim and shows its weakness.

Key Terms
توقف (tawaqquf): Dependence or reliance of one thing on another for its knowledge or existence.
موقوف علیہ (mawquf 'alayh): That upon which something depends; the relied-upon in a dependence relationship.
اصل (asl): Root or foundation; the fundamental source in a hierarchy.
فرع (far'): Branch or derivative; that which depends on the root.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the first response (distinguishing two types of dependence) considered incorrect?
A) Because there is no such distinction in the Hanafi tradition.
B) Because the dependence of fiqh on usul is actually of the tool-type, not root-branch.
C) Because the objector's example is not valid.
D) Because Allama Chalabi's response is better.

Key Takeaway
The hierarchy of sciences cannot be straightforwardly deduced from dependence; the nature of dependence (tool vs. root) matters, and even then, the strongest argument is sequential learning, not inherent nobility.

The Hierarchy of Fiqh and Usul al-Fiqh
Response to an objection about fiqh's dependence on usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the relationship between fiqh and usul al-fiqh according to the Hanafi school, distinguishing between branch-foundation dependence and tool-object dependence, and critically evaluate opposing arguments.

Core Idea
Fiqh is the foundation; usul al-fiqh is its tool—usul depends on fiqh for its existence.

This passage addresses a common objection about the hierarchy between fiqh and usul al-fiqh. Some argue that since fiqh depends on usul for deriving rulings, usul must be foundational. The Hanafi response clarifies the nature of this dependence: it is not like a branch depending on its foundation, but like a tool depending on its user. Without fiqh, usul would never have been codified. This lesson unpacks the rational and textual evidence for the Hanafi position and contrasts it with an alternative interpretation that is rejected.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of dependence
The passage distinguishes between توقف الفرع على الأصل (branch on foundation) and توقف ذي الآلة على الآلة (thing depending on its tool). In the first, the depended-upon is superior; in the second, the tool serves the primary object.
2
State the objector's claim
The objector holds that fiqh depends on usul like a branch on a foundation, making usul prior and foundational. This is refuted by the text.
This view is not attributed to a specific school but is a conceptual objection.
3
Explain the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response asserts that the dependence is of the tool-object type. If fiqh did not exist, usul would not have been compiled. Therefore, fiqh is the foundation (اصل), and usul is the branch and tool (فرع وآلة).
This is a rational (عقلي) argument based on historical observation.
4
Analyze supporting evidence
Two pieces of evidence: (1) Usul is attributed to fiqh for praise (إضافة الفقہ إلى الأصول مدح), showing fiqh's nobility. (2) Books of fiqh are placed above books of usul and kalam, indicating superiority.
The author of Ghunyat is cited for the placement practice.
5
Evaluate Allama Chalasi's alternative
Allama Chalasi interpreted 'above' as precedence in learning (تقدم في التعلم), making usul prior in study. The text rejects this because it undermines the intended nobility of usul that the matn and sharh aimed to establish.
The rejection shows that the debate is about intrinsic rank, not sequence of learning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الترويج لحل التَّوْضِيح والتنويج جیسے تفسیر موقوف ہے صرف و نحو پر نمبر ۲ - فرع کا موقوف ہونا اصل پر۔ اس صورت میں موقوف علیہ موقوف پر مرتبہ مقدم ہوتا ہے یہاں بھی دوسرا معنی مراد ہے لیکن یہ جواب درست نہیں کیونکہ یہاں تو قف الفقہ علی الاصول توقف الفرع علی الاصل کے قبیل سے نہیں بلکہ یہ بھی توقف ذی لا لہ علی الآلہ کے قبیل سے ہے کیونکہ یوں کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ اگر علم فقہ نہ ہوتا تو اصول فقہ کی تدوین ہی نہ ہوتی تو معلوم ہوا کہ فقہ اصل ہے اور اصول فرع اور آلہ ہے اور اس کی تائید اس سے بھی ہوتی ہے کہ اصول کی اضافت فقہ کی طرف مدح کے لئے ہے اس سے بھی فقہ کا اصل اور اشرف ہونا معلوم ہوتا ہے نیز صاحب غنیۃ نے لکھا ہے کہ فقہ کی کتابیں اصول فقہ کی کتابوں بلکہ علم کلام کی کتابوں کے بھی اوپر رکھنی چاہیں ۔ جواب (۲):۔ علامہ چلسی نے یہ جواب دیا کہ تاریخ نے جو فوق کا لفظ ذکر کیا ہے اس سے مراد فوقیت و تقدم في التعلم والطلب ہے یعنی طلب اور قرآت میں علم کلام اصول فقہ پر مقدم ہے اور اصول فقہ کا تعلم فقہ پر مقدم ہے کیونکہ موقوف کی معرفت موقوف علیہ کی معرفت کے بغیر نہیں ہوتی لیکن اس جواب سے ظاہر ہے کہ ماتن و شارح جو اصول فقہ کی شرافت کو بلند کرنا چاہتے ہیں وہ منہدم ہو کر رہ جاتی ہے۔
Al-Tarwih li Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih: Just as tafsir depends on grammar and syntax, number 2 - the branch's dependence on the foundation. In this case, the depended-upon is prior in rank to the dependent. Here also the second meaning is intended, but this answer is incorrect because here 'fiqh depends on usul' is not of the type of branch depending on foundation, but rather of the type of something depending on its tool. Because it can be said: If knowledge of fiqh did not exist, usul al-fiqh would not have been codified. So it becomes known that fiqh is the foundation and usul is the branch and tool. And this is also supported by the fact that usul is attributed to fiqh for praise, which also indicates that fiqh is the foundation and nobler. Also, the author of Ghunyat wrote that books of fiqh should be placed above books of usul al-fiqh and even above books of kalam. Answer (2): Allama Chalasi gave this answer: The word 'above' mentioned in history means precedence in learning and seeking, i.e., in seeking and reading, kalam is prior to usul al-fiqh, and learning usul al-fiqh is prior to fiqh, because knowledge of the dependent cannot occur without knowledge of the depended-upon. But it is obvious from this answer that what the matn and sharh wanted to elevate of the nobility of usul al-fiqh is destroyed.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of an objection regarding the relationship between fiqh and usul al-fiqh. The objector claimed that usul al-fiqh is foundational because fiqh depends on it (like grammar and tafsir). The response clarifies that this dependence is not of a branch on its foundation, but of a thing on its tool. In fact, fiqh is the original science, and usul al-fiqh is derived from it; without fiqh, usul would not have been codified. This is supported by the practice of placing fiqh books above usul books and by the fact that usul is attributed to fiqh for praise. A second answer from Allama Chalasi suggests that 'above' refers to precedence in learning, but this answer is rejected because it undermines the intended nobility of usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
توقف الفرع على الأصل (tawaqquf al-far' 'ala al-asl): The dependence of a branch on its foundation; the branch's existence and knowledge depend on the foundation.
آلة (ālah): Tool or instrument; something that serves another (here usul serves fiqh).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the passage conclude about the relationship between fiqh and usul al-fiqh?
A) Fiqh depends on usul al-fiqh like a branch on its foundation.
B) Usul al-fiqh depends on fiqh as a tool; fiqh is the foundation.
C) They are independent and unrelated sciences.
D) Both are equal in rank and nobility.

Key Takeaway
Fiqh is the foundational science (aṣl) and usul al-fiqh is its tool (ālah); understanding this hierarchy preserves the intended nobility of both sciences.

Objections to the Definition of I'jaz: Scope of Turuq
Raising and responding to objections on i'jaz definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and analyze the two objections regarding the scope of 'turuq' in the Hanafi definition of i'jaz, and explain the Hanafi response to each.

Core Idea
I'jaz requires matchlessness against all possible methods, not just those that have occurred.

The definition of i'jaz (miraculous inimitability of the Quran) is a foundational concept in Usul al-Fiqh. This passage presents two objections to a widely accepted definition: 'conveying meaning in the most eloquent manner compared to all other methods.' The objections center on the scope of 'methods' (turuq) and the singularity of the method of i'jaz. Understanding these objections sharpens your ability to critically evaluate definitions and appreciate the precision required in legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition under criticism
The commentator critiques the definition: 'it conveys meaning in the manner that is more eloquent than all other methods.' Note the key term 'turuq' (methods).
This definition is from the text being commented on.
2
Understand Objection 1: Actual vs. Potential Methods
The objector asks: does 'turuq' refer only to methods that have actually occurred (turuq muhqqaqah) or also to potential future methods (turuq muqaddarah)? Analyze the consequences of each interpretation for the condition of i'jaz.
If only actual methods, a future method could surpass the Quran, negating its matchlessness. If both, then even Allah's ability to produce a like would violate the definition, which is unacceptable.
3
Understand Objection 2: Singular Method of I'jaz
The objector challenges the claim that i'jaz has only one method, citing works like Miftah and Nihayat al-I'jaz that mention multiple methods. This objection is incomplete in the passage but raises the issue of whether eloquence alone is sufficient.
This objection hints at a broader debate about the dimensions of i'jaz (e.g., eloquence, scientific knowledge, legal perfection).
4
Consider the Hanafi Response (Inferred)
From the passage and Hanafi usul, the response likely distinguishes between human incapacity and divine power. I'jaz is defined relative to all possible human methods, not divine methods. The definition must be nuanced to exclude Allah's power while including all potential human speech.
The commentator would clarify that 'all other methods' means all methods within human capability, not including divine power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And here there are two research points: This is the last part of the commentary; the commentator intends to mention two questions and answer them. Question (1): The statement of the question is that you defined i'jaz in speech as 'that it conveys the meaning in the manner that is more eloquent than all other methods.' What is meant by 'methods' here? If you say that by this only actualized methods (those that have come into existence in past time) are intended, then this definition of i'jaz would not be correct, because for i'jaz it is necessary that the speech cannot be opposed, whereas in this case opposition would be possible—there may be among potential methods (those possible in the future) some method that can compete with the speech. And if you say that by 'methods' both actualized and potential (existing in potentiality) are meant, then in that case producing the like of this speech would be impossible, but this condition is not stipulated for miraculous speech, because despite the Quran being miraculous, Allah is able to produce its like. That is, among potential methods there could be a method that equals this Quran in eloquence and rhetoric. So what is the meaning of the author's statement 'more eloquent than all other methods'? Question (2): You have stated that i'jaz has only one method, whereas in the book Miftah and in Nihayat al-I'jaz...
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage introduces two critical objections to the definition of i'jaz as 'conveying meaning in the most eloquent manner possible'. The first objection (sawal 1) concerns the scope of 'turuq' (methods): if only actual methods are meant, then a future method could theoretically surpass the Quran, negating its i'jaz. If both actual and potential methods are meant, then no one can produce the like, but Allah can—yet the definition implies absolute superiority over all methods, even those within Allah's power. The second objection (sawal 2, incomplete) challenges the claim that i'jaz has only one method, citing works like Miftah and Nihayat al-I'jaz that mention multiple methods. The passage primarily presents the objections; the answers are not fully given here but would follow in subsequent text.

Key Terms
طرق محققہ (turuq muhqqaqah): Methods of expression that have actually come into existence in the past or present.
طرق مقدرہ (turuq muqaddarah): Potential methods of expression that could exist in the future, even if not yet actualized.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first objection, what problem arises if 'turuq' is interpreted as only actualized methods?
A) The definition becomes too broad.
B) A future method could potentially surpass the Quran, violating the condition of i'jaz.
C) The Quran would be less eloquent than previous methods.
D) The definition would apply to non-miraculous speech.

Key Takeaway
The definition of i'jaz must encompass all possible human methods of expression to preserve the Quran's matchlessness, while clearly distinguishing divine power from human incapacity.

The Dispute over the Order of Definitions of Usul al-Fiqh
Explaining the two definitions of Usul al-Fiqh and the scholarly dispute over presentation order.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two definitions of Usul al-Fiqh (addafi and laqabi) and evaluate the Hanafi preference for the addafi definition based on the arguments from source precedence and avoidance of repetition.

Core Idea
The addafi definition of Usul al-Fiqh is presented first in Hanafi texts because the source (manqul 'anhu) precedes the transferred (manqul).

This passage explores a methodological dispute among usul scholars: should we define Usul al-Fiqh by its literal construct meaning (addafi) or by its transferred proper name (laqabi)? The Hanafi author argues for the addafi definition first, citing the principle that the original source takes precedence over the derived, and that presenting the laqabi first leads to unnecessary repetition. Understanding this debate reveals the Hanafi emphasis on clarity and avoidance of redundancy in legal definitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two aspects of 'Usul al-Fiqh'
Recognise that the term has a literal aspect (as a construct of 'usul' and 'fiqh') and a transferred aspect (as a proper name for the science).
2
State the opposing view and its proofs
Some scholars prefer the laqabi definition first, arguing that the scientific meaning is intended (so it takes precedence) and that the term is like a simple word (simple precedes compound).
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The author gives two counter-proofs: the addafi is the source (manqul 'anhu) and must precede the transferred, and presenting laqabi first requires defining 'fiqh' twice, causing repetition.
4
Evaluate the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf is the order of definitions in usul textbooks; Hanafi texts place addafi first to avoid repetition and reflect source precedence.
5
Determine the Hanafi tarjih
The author's position is relied upon: the addafi definition is presented first. This is the prevailing Hanafi pedagogical method.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

واصول الفقہ :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا حصہ نہم ہے۔ تاریخ اصول فقہ کی دو تعریفوں کا پس منظر بیان کرتے ہیں کہ اصول الفقہ کی دو حیثیتیں ہیں۔ (۱) لفظی (۲) معنوی لفظوں کے اعتبار سے یہ مرکب اضافی ہے۔ لیکن معنوی حیثیت یہ ہے کہ مرکب اضافی سے منقول ہو کر اس علم کا لقب ہو چکا ہے۔ اب ہر حیثیت سے اس کی تعریف ہوگی ۔ منقول عنہ ہونے کے اعتبار سے تعریف اضافی ہوگی اور منقول ہونے کے اعتبار سے تعریف لقمی ہوگی۔
قدم بعضہم :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا حصہ دہم ہے۔ غرض اس میں علماء کے طریق کار کے اختلاف پر دلائل ذکر کرنا ہے۔ بعض حضرات نے حدیقی کو مقدم کیا ہے اور مصنف نے حد اضافی کو مقدم کیا ہے۔ دونوں حضرات کی دو دو دلیلیں ہیں۔ تاریخ نے دونوں کی دلیلوں کو بیان کیا ہے۔ بعض کی دلیل اول: کہ تعریف لقمی معنی علمی کے اعتبار سے ہے۔ اور اعلام میں مقصود معنی علمی ہوتا ہے۔ تو معنی علمی یعنی اضافی کے اعتبار سے مقصود ہوا اور معنی اضافی غیر مقصود اور ضابطہ ہے کہ مقصود غیر مقصود پر مقدم ہوتا ہے۔ اس لیے حد لقمی حد اضافی پر مقدم ہونی چاہیے۔ دلیل ثانی: اصول الفقہ حدیقی کے اعتبار سے بمنزلہ مفرد اور بسیط کے ہے۔ اور تعریف اضافی کے اعتبار سے بمنزل مرکب اسے نمول مرکب کے ہے ۔ لفظ اصول اور فقہ سے۔ اور بسیط مقدم ہوتا ہے مرکب سے اس لیے تعریف لھی کومقدم ہونا چاہیے۔ مصنف رحمتہ اللہ کی دو دلیلیں۔ دلیل (۱):- تعریف اضافی منقول عنہ ہے اور تعریف لقمی منقول ہے۔ اور منقول عنہ مقدم ہوتا ہے منقول سے اس لیے تعریف اضافی کو مقدم کیا۔
ولیل (۲) اگر لقی کو تعریف اضافی پر مقدم کریں تو اس میں تکرار محض لازم آتا ہے۔ وہ اس طرح کہ تعریف لھی میں فقہ کی قید موجود ہے۔ کیونکہ اصول فقہ کی حد قمی یہ ہے۔ ھو العلم بالقواعد التی توصل بھا الی الفقہ ۔ اور کامل تعریف وہ ہوتی ہے کہ تعریف سے اس کے اجزاء کی معرفت بھی معلوم ہو جائے ۔ اور یہاں چونکہ فقہ جز ہے۔ اس لیے اس کی تعریف کرنی پڑے گی۔ پھر حد اضافی میں مضاف الیہ (فقہ) کے دوبارہ تعریف کرنی پڑے گی۔ ورنہ تعریف اضافی متحقق نہیں ہوگی ۔ ہاں اگر تعریف
[Section] Fahseen Tashawwuq: This is the eighth part of the commentary's text. In this passage, the commentator explains the matn (text) that the author mentioned two constructions of the phrase "Usul al-Fiqh". The commentator clarifies: when it is necessary to know the definition, because through definition the science is distinguished for the student, the student developed a desire to know the definition of this science to the extent that it was close that the listener would ask. The author, to suppress the question, said "This is Usul al-Fiqh", or he placed himself in the position of the student and asked from that side, then began the definition. [Section] Wa Usul al-Fiqh: This is the ninth part of the commentary's text. It explains the background of the two definitions of Usul al-Fiqh: that Usul al-Fiqh has two aspects: (1) literal (lafzi) and (2) meaning-based (ma'nawi). In terms of words, it is a construct (murakkab idafi). However, in terms of meaning, it has been transferred from being a construct to being a title (laqab) for this science. Now it will be defined from each aspect: from the aspect of being the source (manqul 'anhu), the definition will be addafi, and from the aspect of being transferred (manqul), the definition will be laqabi. [Section] Qaddama Ba'dahum: This is the tenth part of the commentary's text. The purpose is to mention proofs regarding the difference of scholars' methods. Some scholars (ba'd) presented the laqabi (haqiqi) definition first, while the author (musannif) presented the addafi definition first. Both have two proofs each. The text mentions both proofs. The first proof of 'some' (laqabi proponents): The laqabi definition is in terms of the scientific meaning. In names (a'lam), the intended meaning is the scientific meaning. So the scientific meaning (i.e., addafi) is intended, while the additive meaning is unintended. The principle is that the intended takes precedence over the unintended. Therefore, the laqabi definition should precede the addafi. Second proof: Usul al-Fiqh in terms of laqabi is like a simple (mufrad/baseet) entity, while in terms of addafi it is like a compound (murakkab) from the words 'usul' and 'fiqh'. The simple precedes the compound, so the laqabi definition should precede. The author's (musannif's) two proofs: First proof: The addafi definition is the source (manqul 'anhu), while the laqabi is transferred (manqul). The source precedes the transferred, so the addafi definition is presented first. Second proof: If the laqabi is presented before the addafi, unnecessary repetition (takrar mahd) would occur. That is because the laqabi definition includes the qualification of fiqh; indeed the laqabi definition of Usul al-Fiqh is: 'It is the knowledge of the rules that lead to fiqh.' And a complete definition is one through which knowledge of its parts is also known. Here, since fiqh is a part, it would have to be defined. Then, in the addafi definition, the addaf ilayh (fiqh) would have to be defined again, otherwise the addafi definition would not be realized. However, if the definition...
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the two types of definitions of Usul al-Fiqh and the scholarly dispute over which definition should be presented first in a textbook. The commentator explains the background: the term 'Usul al-Fiqh' has two aspects. In terms of its wording, it is a construct (murakkab idafi) meaning 'the principles of fiqh'. But in the discipline, it has become a proper name (laqab) for the science itself. Hence, there are two definitions: an addafi definition (based on the literal construct meaning) and a laqabi definition (based on the transferred title meaning). Some scholars (referred to as 'ba'd' or 'some') argue that the laqabi definition should be presented first. They give two reasons: first, the scientific meaning is the intended one, so it takes precedence over the unintended additive meaning. Second, in terms of laqab, the term is like a single simple word (mufrad/baseet), while in terms of addaf, it is compound (murakkab); the simple precedes the compound. The author (musannif) prefers the addafi definition first, also with two proofs. First, the addafi definition is the original source (manqul 'anhu) from which the title was transferred, and the source precedes the derived. Second, if the laqabi definition is given first, it will require defining 'fiqh' (since laqabi definition includes 'fiqh' as a part). Then when the addafi definition is given, 'fiqh' would need to be defined again, leading to unnecessary repetition. Therefore, the author places the addafi definition first. This is a classic Hanafi methodological dispute: the order in which definitions are presented reflects the author's approach to pedagogy and the nature of the science. The Hanafi tradition often emphasizes clarity and avoidance of repetition, hence the preference for the addafi definition first.

Key Terms
تعریف اضافی (ta'rif idafi): The definition of Usul al-Fiqh based on its literal meaning as a construct (idafah) of 'usul' and 'fiqh'.
تعریف لقبی (ta'rif laqabi): The definition of Usul al-Fiqh as a proper name (laqab) for the science of the principles of fiqh.
منقول عنہ (manqul 'anhu): The original source from which the title is transferred; here, the addafi meaning.
منقول (manqul): The transferred title; here, the laqabi meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is simpler than the laqabi definition.
B) It is the source (manqul 'anhu) from which the title is transferred, and the source takes precedence.
C) It conveys the intended scientific meaning.
D) It avoids defining the term 'usul'.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school presents the addafi definition of Usul al-Fiqh first due to the principle that the original source precedes the transferred and to avoid repetition.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Four Objections on the Definition of Asl and Their Answers
Commentator refutes objections against the definition of 'asl'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify four objections to the definition of 'asl' in Hanafi usul and evaluate the commentator's counter-arguments by distinguishing between lexical and true definitions, and between essential foundation and mere causality.

Core Idea
The Hanafi definition of asl requires inclusive true definition and foundational subordination, not just causality.

In this passage, the commentator engages critically with four objections raised against the definition of 'asl' (origin) in Hanafi usul. By analyzing these objections and their responses, you will sharpen your understanding of what constitutes a valid definition in usul al-fiqh and how the Hanafi school distinguishes between essential foundation and mere agency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four objections
Read the passage and list each objection against the definition of 'asl'. Note the basis of each objection: (1) inclusion not necessary, (2) definition applies to efficient cause, (3) [referenced but not detailed], (4) definition excludes imagined matters.
The third objection is not fully quoted but mentioned as arising from a statement by the author in the chapter on majaz.
2
Analyze the commentator's response to the first objection
The first objection claims that definitions need not be inclusive (ṭard). The commentator responds by distinguishing lexical definition (تعریف لفظی), where inclusion is not required, from true definition (تعریف حقیقی), where inclusion is essential. This preserves the requirement for 'asl'.
In Hanafi usul, a true definition must cover all instances (ṭard) and exclude non-instances (ʿaks).
3
Analyze the response to the second objection
The second objection argues that the definition applies to the efficient cause (fāʿil) as well. The commentator clarifies that 'based upon' (ibtināʾ) means essential foundational subordination, not mere causality. The efficient cause is effective but not a foundation.
The distinction between material cause (ʿilla mādiyya) and efficient cause (ʿilla fāʿiliyya) is crucial here.
4
Analyze the response to the fourth objection
The fourth objection says the definition does not cover imagined matters (umūr mawhūma) as an origin for thought. The commentator explains that intellectual basedness (ibtināʾ ʿaqlī) is not limited to the subordination of a ruling to evidence; it includes any intellectual subordination. Thought is intellectually based on imagined matters, so the definition is inclusive.
The commentator redefines intellectual basedness broadly: one thing being subordinated to another in the intellect.
5
Synthesize the refined definition of asl
From the responses, derive the refined Hanafi definition of 'asl': it is that upon which another essentially and foundationally rests, either in reality or in the intellect, and the term must be linguistically applicable. This excludes mere causal relations and ensures the definition is both inclusive and exclusive.
This definition is used in qiyas where the asl (original case) provides the ruling for the farʿ (branch).

اولها: اعتراض :(۱):۔ اس عبارت میں شاریخ نے پہلا اعتراض نقل کیا ہے کہ مصنف نے کہا ہے کہ تعریفات میں طرد کا ہونہ شرط ہے۔ خصوصاً تعریف اسی میں ہم اس کو تسلیم نہیں کرتے اس لئے کہ متقین نے تصریح کی ہے تعریفات نا قصہ لفظ عام سے ہو سکتی ہیں کیونکہ بسا اوقات ھی کی تفسیر سے مقصود کسی شی معین سے امتیاز ہوتا ہے اور یہ امتیاز تفسیر بالا ئم سے حاصل ہو جاتا ہے مثلاً جب اصل اور فرع میں امتیاز مقصود ہو تو اصل کی تعریف محتاج الیہ کیسا تھ کرنا جائز ہے لھذ اجب تعریف عام ہو گی وہ معرف پر بھی صادق آئے گی اور غیر معرف پر بھی صادق آئے گی معلوم ہوا کہ طرد شرط نہیں ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ لغت کی کتابیں بھری پڑی ہیں جہاں الفاظ کی تفسیر عام لفظ سے کی گئی ہے۔
جواب :۔ لفظ کی تفسیر بالا ئم ہو تو اس کو تعریف لفظی کہتے ہیں نہ کہ تعریف ائی اور تعریف لفظی میں طرد شرط نہیں ہے بخلاف تعریف امی کے کہ اسمیں طرد شرط ہے خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ شاریخ کا یہ دعوئی پہلا دلیل ہے۔
ثانیہا: اعتراض (۲):۔ دوسرے اعتراض کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جس طرح محتاج الیہ کی تعریف علت فاعلی پر صادق آتی ہے اسی طرح ما تنبلی علیہ غیر کی تعریف بھی صادق آتی ہے کیونکہ ابتنا ء کا یہی معنی ہے کہ ایک شئی پر اس کا غیر مرتب ہو اور فعل بھی فاعل پر مرتب ہوتا ہے گویا کہ آپ کی تعریف بھی دخول غیر سے مانع نہ ہوئی تو پھر آپ نے صاحب محصول پر اعتراض کیوں کیا؟ جواب: ابتناء سے مراد ابناء اساسی ہے یعنی ایک چیز دوسری کے لئے بنیاد ہو اور فعل میں فاعل مؤثر تو ہے لیکن اس کے لئے بنیاد نہیں ہے لھذ اما بیتی عالیہ غیرہ والی تعریف صرف علت مادی پر صادق آئی نہ کہ علت فاعلی پر۔ خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ اصل کے لئے دو چیزوں کا ہونا بہت ضروری ہے۔
(1) اصل غیر کے لئے بینی علیہ ہو۔
(۲) لغت میں بھی اس پر اصل کا اطلاق ہوتا ہو۔ یہاں ایک چیز تو پائی جاتی ہے کہ فاعل پر فعل کا ترتب ہے اور فعل فاعل کی طرف مستند ہے لیکن دوسری بات موجود نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ لغت میں فعل کے لئے فاعل کو اصل نہیں کہا جاتا ۔
رابعها: اعتراض (۴)۔ اس عبارت میں شاریخ چو تھا اعتراض بیان فرماتے ہیں جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ آپ نے اصل کی تعریف جو ایجنی علیہ غیرہ کیساتھ کی ہے یہ جامع لجميع الافراد نہیں ہے کہ کیونکہ امور موحومہ کو تر تیب دینا فکر کے لئے اصل ہے لیکن اس پر تعریف صادق نہیں آتی کیونکہ فکر کا امور موحومہ کی ترتیب پر ابتناء نہ تو حسی ہو سکتا ہے کیونکہ یہ محسوس بالحواس نہیں ہے اور یہ ابتنا عقلی بھی نہیں ہے کیونکہ ابتاء عقلی کہتے ہیں حکم کا دلیل پر مرتب ہونا۔ اور ظاہر ہے کہ امور موہومہ کی ترتیب فکر کیلئے دلیل نہیں ہے اور نہ ہی فکر اس کیلئے حکم ہے۔ جواب:۔ فکر کا امور موهومہ کی ترتیب پر بنی ہونا ابتنا عقلی ہے کیونکہ ترتیب الحکم علی دلیلہ یہ ابناء عقلی کی تعریف نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ تو ایک مثال ہے اصل میں ابتداء عقلی کی تعریف یہ ہے کہ عقل میں ایک چیز کا دوسری چیز پر مرتب ہونا اور فکر بھی امور موحومہ کی ترتیب پر عقلا مرتب ہے بعد اس پر اصل کی تعریف صادق آتی ہے بعد اتعریف جامع مجمع الافراد ہے۔
Here is a discussion: This is the last part of the passage. The author of the commentary narrated four objections on the matn. First objection (1): In this passage, the commentator narrated the first objection that the author said that in definitions, inclusion (tard) is not a condition. Especially in this definition, we do not accept this because the early scholars have stated that incomplete definitions can be given with a general word because sometimes the purpose of interpreting the li'am is to distinguish something specific, and this distinction is achieved by an inclusive interpretation. For example, when distinguishing between the origin and the branch is intended, it is permissible to define the origin as that which needs something else. Thus the definition would be general, applying to both the defined and non-defined. So it is known that inclusion is not a condition. This is the reason why dictionaries are full of interpretations of words with a general word. Answer: If a word is interpreted by li'am, it is called a lexical definition, not a true definition. In lexical definition, inclusion is not a condition, unlike a true definition where inclusion is a condition. In summary, the commentator's claim is the first proof. Second objection (2): The gist of the second objection is that just as the definition of 'that which needs something' applies to the efficient cause, similarly the definition of 'what another is based upon' also applies because the meaning of 'being based' is that something else is subordinated to a thing, and the act is also subordinated to the agent. So your definition also did not prevent the inclusion of other things. So why did you object to the author of Al-Mahsul? Answer: By 'being based' is meant essential foundation, i.e., one thing is the foundation for another. In the act, the agent is effective but not the foundation. Therefore, the definition 'based upon another' applies only to the material cause, not the efficient cause. In summary, for the origin, two things are necessary: (1) the origin must be a foundation for another, (2) in language it must also be called 'asl'. Here one thing is found: the act is subordinated to the agent and the act is attributed to the agent. But the second thing is not present because in language the agent is not called 'asl' for the act. Third objection (3): [missing in text but referenced in commentary]. Fourth objection (4): In this passage, the commentator states the fourth objection, the gist of which is that you defined the origin as 'what something else is based upon' but this is not inclusive of all individuals because arranging imagined matters is an origin for thought, but this definition does not apply to it because the thought's being based upon the arrangement of imagined matters cannot be physical since it is not perceived by the senses, nor is it intellectual because intellectual basedness is said to be the subordination of a ruling to its evidence. It is apparent that the arrangement of imagined matters is not evidence for thought, nor is thought a ruling for it. Answer: Thought's being based on the arrangement of imagined matters is intellectual basedness because the subordination of a ruling to its evidence is not the definition of intellectual basedness; rather, that is an example. In reality, the definition of intellectual basedness is the subordination of one thing to another in the intellect. Thought is also intellectually subordinated to the arrangement of imagined matters. Thus the definition of origin applies to it, and the definition is inclusive of all individuals.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage presents a critical discussion on the definition of 'asl' (origin) in the context of usul al-fiqh. The commentator narrates four objections raised against the definition given by the author of the matn (possibly in Al-Tawdih). The definition under scrutiny is that 'asl' is 'that upon which another is based' (مبتنی علیہ غیرہ). The first objection argues that definitions need not be inclusive (طرد), as scholars allow partial definitions using general terms. The answer distinguishes between lexical definition (تعریف لفظی) and true definition (تعریف حقیقی); only true definition requires inclusion. The second objection claims the definition applies equally to the efficient cause (علت فاعلی), making it not exclusive. The answer clarifies that 'based upon' implies foundational subordination, not mere efficacy; the efficient cause is not a foundation. The third objection (mentioned but not detailed) references a statement by the author in the chapter on majaz. The fourth objection asserts the definition does not cover imagined matters (امور موہومہ) as an origin for thought. The answer explains that intellectual basedness (ابتناء عقلی) includes thought's subordination to imagined matters, so the definition is indeed inclusive. This discussion refines the precise meaning of 'asl' and shows the commentator's critical engagement with the matn.

Key Terms
طرد (ṭard): Inclusion of all individuals of the defined concept in the definition.
تعریف حقیقی (taʿrīf ḥaqīqī): A real definition that specifies the essence and distinguishes it from all others.
ابتناء أساسی (ibtināʾ asāsī): Essential foundation: one thing being the basis upon which another rests.
اصل (aṣl): That upon which something else is based (مبتنی علیہ غیرہ).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator reject the objection that the definition of 'asl' applies to the efficient cause?
A) Because the efficient cause is not a cause but an agent.
B) Because the efficient cause is not a foundation (بنیاد) upon which the effect rests; it is merely an agent.
C) Because the efficient cause is not subordinated to the effect.
D) Because the efficient cause is external to the definition.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of 'asl' requires both inclusive true definition and foundational subordination, excluding mere causes and encompassing intellectual bases.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Did the Author Reject Abu Hanifa's Definition of Fiqh? A Refutation of the Commentator's Claim
Refutes claim that author implicitly rejected Imam Abu Hanifa's definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the claim that the author of al-Tawdih implicitly rejected Abu Hanifa's definition of fiqh by distinguishing between rejection and refinement for technical scope.

Core Idea
Providing a narrower definition does not imply rejection; it refines the scope for a specific discipline.

In usul al-fiqh, definitions are crucial for delineating the subject matter. The Hanafi tradition honors Imam Abu Hanifa, but later scholars sometimes narrow definitions for technical precision. This passage from Altarweeh defends the author of al-Tawdih against the charge of disrespecting Imam Abu Hanifa by clarifying that his new definition was meant to define technical fiqh, not to reject the inclusive definition of the great Imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Commentator's Claim
The commentator (sharih) claimed that the author of al-Tawdih used kinayah (allusion) to implicitly reject Imam Abu Hanifa's definition of fiqh. Notice that the author explicitly rejected Imam al-Shafi'i's definition.
Kinayah is a rhetorical device often used out of respect.
2
Examine the Author's Action
The author provided a third definition of fiqh from himself, in addition to quoting the definitions of Abu Hanifa and al-Shafi'i. The commentator interprets this as dissatisfaction with Abu Hanifa's definition.
The author could have simply omitted Abu Hanifa's definition if he rejected it entirely.
3
Analyze the Author's Intention
The author of Altarweeh explains that the author wanted to define fiqh according to its technical meaning (fiqh istilahi), which excludes kalam and tasawwuf. Abu Hanifa's definition was inclusive, covering those sciences.
Technical fiqh focuses on practical rulings, not speculative theology or spirituality.
4
Compare Inclusivity vs. Exclusivity
Abu Hanifa's definition: al-ma'rifah bi al-ahkam al-shar'iyyah min adillatiha al-tafsiliyyah (knowledge of the detailed legal rulings from their evidences), which can include kalam and tasawwuf. The author's definition narrows it to practical fiqh.
Inclusivity does not make a definition invalid; it may be too broad for a specific field.
5
Conclude: Refinement, Not Rejection
By providing a new definition, the author showed that Abu Hanifa's definition is inclusive, not that it is unacceptable. This respects the Imam while serving the technical purpose.
The Altarweeh's refutation is based on the author's explicit purpose of defining technical fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مقبول ہے لیکن یہاں مصنف نے امام شافعی کی تعریف کی غیر مقبولیت کو صراحتا ذ کر کیا ہے اور امام صاحب کی تعریف کی غیر مقبولیت کو کنا یہ ذکر کیا ہے اور اسکی وجہ شاید یہ ہے کہ امام صاحب چونکہ امام اعظم ہیں تو انکے ادب کی وجہ سے مصنف نے انکی تعریف کو صراحتا غیر مقبول نہیں کہا بلکہ اپنی طرف سے تیری تعریف کو نقل کر کے اسکے غیر مقبول ہونے کی طرف اشارہ کر دیا ہے فائدہ:۔ شاریخ کی یہ بات درست نہیں ہے کہ مصنف نے امام صاحب کی تعریف کو کنایہ غیر مقبول کہا ہے بلکہ حقیقیت یہ ہے کہ مصنف نے اپنی طرف سے نئی تعریف اس لئے کی کہ امام صاحب کی تعریف میں شمول تھا یعنی وہ علم کلام اور علم تصوف کو بھی شامل تھی اور مصنف تصرف فقہ اصطلاحی کی تعریف کرنا چاہتے تھے اس لئے انہوں نے اپنی طرف سے تیسری تعریف نقل کی ہے جو صرف فقہ اصطلاحی پر صادق آتی ہے علم کلام اور علم تصوف کو شامل نہیں اور اپنی طرف سے تعریف ذکر کر کے یہ بتایا کہ امام صاحب کی تعریف میں شمول ہے نہ یہ کہ امام صاحب کی تعریف غیر مقبول ہے۔
Accepted, but here the author explicitly mentioned the non-acceptance of Imam Shafi'i's definition and implicitly mentioned the non-acceptance of Imam Abu Hanifa's definition. The reason perhaps is that because Imam Abu Hanifa is the greatest Imam, out of respect for him the author did not explicitly say his definition is unacceptable, but rather transmitted a third definition from himself and indicated its unacceptability. Benefit: The commentator's statement that the author implicitly called Imam Abu Hanifa's definition unacceptable is incorrect. Rather the reality is that the author formulated a new definition because Imam Abu Hanifa's definition was inclusive, i.e., it included kalam and tasawwuf. The author wanted to define fiqh according to its technical meaning, so he transmitted a third definition that applies only to technical fiqh and does not include kalam and tasawwuf. By mentioning his own definition, he showed that Imam Abu Hanifa's definition is inclusive, not that his definition is unacceptable.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute about the author's treatment of the definitions of fiqh given by Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Abu Hanifa. The commentator (sharih) claimed that the author of the matn (al-Tawdih) explicitly rejected al-Shafi'i's definition and implicitly rejected Abu Hanifa's definition via allusion (kinayah). The author of Altarweeh (this work) refutes that claim. He explains that the author's intention was not to reject Abu Hanifa's definition, but to provide a definition that specifically fits the technical fiqh (fiqh istilahi) and excludes the sciences of kalam and tasawwuf, which Abu Hanifa's definition included. Thus, the author's action of providing a third definition (from himself) was to show inclusivity, not non-acceptance. This is a common Hanafi usul approach: respecting the founding imam while clarifying the technical scope of a discipline.

Key Terms
کنا یہ (kināyah): Implicit or allusive speech, as opposed to explicit (sarih). The commentator claimed the author used kinayah to reject Abu Hanifa's definition.
شمول (shumūl): Inclusivity; here it means that Abu Hanifa's definition of fiqh included kalam and tasawwuf, making it broader than the technical definition.

Makruh Tahrimi and Its Effect on Intercession
Clarifying the consequence of makruh tahrimi on intercession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi usul classification of actions into makruh tanzihi and makruh tahrimi, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the consequences of committing makruh tahrimi, specifically its effect on shafa'ah.

Core Idea
Makruh tahrimi deprives one of intercession for elevation in ranks, though not salvation—a distinction that resolves apparent conflict with hadith.

In Hanafi usul, acts are classified not only as halal or haram but also into intermediate categories: makruh tanzihi (close to halal) and makruh tahrimi (close to haram). This lesson unpacks a key intra-Hanafi dispute: does committing makruh tahrimi warrant punishment or merely rebuke? The passage also addresses an apparent contradiction with the Prophet's hadith on intercession for major sinners, resolving it through a subtle but crucial distinction between two types of shafa'ah. By the end, you'll see how precise classification leads to coherent rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the classification criterion
Start by understanding the basis for distinguishing makruh tanzihi from makruh tahrimi: if an act is not prohibited (haram), it is either close to halal (tanzihi) or close to haram (tahrimi). This is the foundation of the discussion.
The criterion is the degree of likeness to halal or haram, not a separate textual proof.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Muhammad holds that the perpetrator of makruh tahrimi deserves punishment by fire, while later mashayikh hold that only ta'bir (rebuke or deprivation) is deserved, not hellfire. The passage notes that the matn author adopted Imam Muhammad's view for this context.
This is a thamarah al-ikhtilaf (fruit of disagreement) with practical implications.
3
Examine the objection and its basis
An objector cites the hadith 'My intercession is for the major sinners of my Ummah' to argue that even major sinners receive intercession, so how can a less severe act (makruh tahrimi) deprive one of it?
The hadith is a dalil naqli used by the objector.
4
Apply the resolution: two types of shafa'ah
The answer distinguishes intercession for salvation from hell (which includes major sinners) from intercession for elevation in Paradise (which requires freedom from even near-haram acts). Makruh tahrimi only deprives of the latter.
This distinction harmonises the hadith with the ruling on makruh tahrimi.
5
Conclude the effect on shafa'ah
Thus, the perpetrator of makruh tahrimi is not deprived of all intercession; only the type that raises ranks is withheld. The dispute over punishment (fire vs. ta'bir) remains, but both views agree on some form of consequence.
The passage does not explicitly prefer one view, but presents both.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سے منع کیا گیا ہوگا یا نہیں اگر منع کیا گیا ہے تو یہ حرام ہے اگر منع نہیں کیا گیا تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں کہ وہ حلت کے قریب ہوگا یا حرمت کے اگر حلت کے قریب ہے تو مکروہ تنزیہی ہے اور اگر حرمت کے قریب ہے تو مکروہ تحریمی ہے۔ وهو المناسب مهنا: یہ شرح کی عبارت کا آٹھواں حصہ ہے۔ شارع نے مقام کے لحاظ سے مناسب مذہب کو متعین کیا کہ ماتن نے چونکہ تنزیہی کو جواز اور مکروہ تحریمی کو عدم جواز میں شمار کیا ہے اور یہی مذہب امام محمد کا ہے اس لئے اس مقام پر ان کی وجہ حصر کو لیتا ہی مناسب ہے۔ ثمره اختلاف شارع نے یہ بیان فرمایا ہے کہ امام محمد کے نزدیک مکروہ تحریمی کا مرتکب عقاب اور عذاب بالنار کا مستحق ہے اور مشین کے نزدیک مکروہ تحریمی کا مرتکب عقاب بالنار کا تو مستحق نہیں البتہ تعبیر کا مستحق ہوگا مثلا وہ شفاعت سے کروم ہو گا ۔ کیا مکروہ تحریمی کا مرتکب شفاعت سے محروم ہو گا اعتراض:- آپ علیہ السلام کا فرمان ہے شفاعتى لاهل الكبائر من امتی اس سے پتا چلتا ہے کہ کبیرہ گناہ یعنی حرام کا مرتکب بھی شفاعت سے محروم نہیں ہوگا تو وہ شخص کیسے شفاعت سے کیسے محروم ہوسکتا ہے جو صرف حرام کے قریبی فعل کا مرتکب ہو یعنی مکروہ تحریمی کا۔ جواب:۔ شفاعت کی دو تمیں میں ایک ہے جہنم سے نجات کے لئے شفاعت اور دوسری ہے جنت میں ترقی درجات کیلئے شفاعت (جیسے اولاد کا والدین کے پاس پہنچنا ) تو حدیث میں اول شفاعت کا ذکر ہے اور مصنف نے جو بات کی ہے اس سے مراد وہ شفاعت ہے جو ترقی درجات کیلئے ہوتی ہے یعنی مکروہ تحریمی کا مرتکب ترقی درجات والی شفاعت سے محروم ہو گا۔
...whether it has been prohibited or not. If it has been prohibited, then it is haram. If it has not been prohibited, it is not free from two states: either it is close to permissible or close to impermissible. If it is close to permissible, then it is makruh tanzihi; if close to impermissible, then it is makruh tahrimi. And 'wa huwa al-munasib huna': this is the eighth part of the commentary's phrase. The Lawgiver determined the appropriate school according to context: since the matn author counted tanzihi as permissibility and tahrimi as non-permissibility, and this is the madhhab of Imam Muhammad, therefore in this context taking his exclusive view is appropriate. 'Thamara al-ikhtilaf': The author has stated that according to Imam Muhammad, the perpetrator of makruh tahrimi deserves punishment and torment by fire, and according to the mashayikh, the perpetrator does not deserve punishment by fire but does deserve rebuke, for example he will be deprived of intercession. 'Will the perpetrator of makruh tahrimi be deprived of intercession?' Objection: The Prophet said, 'My intercession is for the major sinners of my Ummah.' This shows that even the perpetrator of a major sin (haram) is not deprived of intercession, so how can one who commits an act close to haram (makruh tahrimi) be deprived? Answer: Intercession is of two types: one for salvation from hell, and the other for elevation in ranks in Paradise. The hadith refers to the first type, and what the author says refers to the second: the perpetrator of makruh tahrimi will be deprived of intercession for elevation in ranks.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the classification of ahkam, specifically the distinction between makruh tanzihi and makruh tahrimi, and their consequences. The author first explains the criterion: if an act is prohibited, it is haram; if not prohibited, it is either close to halal (tanzihi) or close to haram (tahrimi). The commentator then notes that the matn author's placement aligns with Imam Muhammad's view that tanzihi is permissible and tahrimi is not. The 'thamar al-ikhtilaf' (fruit of disagreement) is that Imam Muhammad holds that one who commits makruh tahrimi deserves punishment in hell, while the later mashayikh hold that such a person does not deserve hellfire but is subject to ta'bir (rebuke or deprivation of some good). The text then addresses an objection: if the Prophet's intercession is for major sinners (ahl al-kaba'ir), how can someone who only approaches sin (makruh tahrimi) be deprived of intercession? The answer distinguishes two types of intercession: one for salvation from hell (which the hadith refers to) and another for elevation in ranks in Paradise. The perpetrator of makruh tahrimi is deprived of the latter, not the former. This shows the precision of Hanafi usul in differentiating between degrees of prohibition and their respective consequences. The passage relies on a hadith about intercession, but the key reasoning is based on the classification of ahkam and the agreed-upon understanding that not all intercession is the same.

Key Terms
مکروہ تحریمی (makruh tahrimi): An act prohibited but without definitive proof; close to haram, its perpetrator deserves ta'bir (rebuke or deprivation) but not necessarily hellfire according to mashayikh.
شفاعت (shafa'ah): Intercession; divided into two types: one for salvation from hell (for all believers including major sinners) and one for elevation of ranks in Paradise (for those free from even minor or close-to-haram acts).
تعبیر (ta'bir): Rebuke or deprivation of some good; the consequence for makruh tahrimi according to mashayikh, as opposed to punishment by fire.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
