Defending the Four Sources: Why Other Evidences Are Subsumed
Refutes claims of additional sources by subsuming them into the four.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of subsumption to identify whether a claimed additional source (shara'i' man qablana, custom, qawl sahabi, rational proof) is actually part of the four principal sources.

Core Idea
Any claimed additional source is either included in Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, or Qiyas — the four are exhaustive.

This passage addresses a common objection: that there are more than four sources of Islamic law. The objector cites examples like previous divine laws, prevailing custom, companion sayings, and rational proofs. The Hanafi response systematically subsumes each into the established four, defending the sufficiency and completeness of the Hanafi usul framework.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection and examples
Recognize that the objector claims additional sources: shara'i' man qablana, ta'amul, qawl sahabi, and dalil 'aqli. Understand that the Hanafi school limits sources to four.
The objection is a hypothetical challenge to the four-source framework.
2
Trace the response for shara'i' man qablana
Note that previous laws are either in Quran or in Sunnah; thus subsumed under those two sources.
No need for a separate category.
3
Trace the response for ta'amul and qawl sahabi
Custom is subsumed under ijma (silent consensus). For qawl sahabi: if it agrees with qiyas, it is under qiyas; if contrary, it must be from the Prophet, hence under Sunnah.
This preserves the four-source structure while including these proofs.
4
Trace the response for dalil 'aqli
Rational proof alone is not valid unless supported by text or ijma; therefore it falls under Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma.
This prevents rational speculation from being an independent source.
5
Summarize the principle of subsumption (idraj)
Conclude that the Hanafi method systematically reduces all claimed additional proofs to the four principal sources, maintaining consistency and avoiding multiplication of sources.
This is a key defense of Hanafi usul.

Source Text

Laws of those before us, custom of people, saying of a companion, rational proof, etc. are included in the four sources. As for 'shara'i' man qablana': This is the third part of the text. The commentator answers a presupposed question. Question: Confining shar'i proofs to four is incorrect because there are many other proofs used, e.g., rulings of previous ummahs mentioned in Quran or hadith without rejection become binding; similarly, people's custom becomes proof, like reciters of Egypt reading 'dal' instead of 'dad' — they deem prayer valid due to custom. Sometimes a companion's saying becomes proof though not in Quran, hadith, ijma, or qiyas. Also rational proof (ma'qul) is used, as by the author of Hidayah. So confining to four is wrong. Answer: Confinement is correct because laws of previous ummahs are either in Quran (so included) or hadith (so in Sunnah). Custom is included in ijma. Companion's saying: if consistent with qiyas, it is qiyas; if contrary, it must have been heard from the Prophet, so it is hadith. Rational proof is derived from nass or ijma, as absolute rational proof is not valid unless supported by text or consensus, so it is included in Quran, hadith, or ijma. Hence no objection.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (ikhtilaf) where an objector claims that there are more than four sources, citing examples: previous divine laws (shara'i' man qablana), customary practice (ta'amul al-nas), a companion's saying (qawl al-sahabi), and rational proof (dalil 'aqli). The Hanafi commentator refutes each: previous laws are either in Quran or hadith, so subsumed; custom is part of ijma (the silent consensus of scholars); a companion's saying either agrees with qiyas (hence qiyas) or, if contrary, must have been heard from the Prophet (hence hadith); rational proof is only valid when supported by text or consensus, thus also subsumed. This reinforces the Hanafi position that the four sources are exhaustive. The response is a key defense of Hanafi usul against claims of additional independent sources.

Key Terms
شرائع من قبلنا (shara'i' man qablana): The divine laws revealed to previous prophets and communities.
قول صحابی (qawl al-sahabi): A legal statement or opinion of a companion of the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It is included in Sunnah (hadith)
D) It is included in Ijma

Key Takeaway
The four sources of Hanafi usul are exhaustive; any claimed additional proof is actually subsumed under Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, or Qiyas.

Objection and Answer on the Phrase 'Ala Wajh al-Tahqiq
Objection to a restriction in the definition and its refutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the purpose of the restriction 'ala wajh al-tahqiq in the definition of usul al-fiqh and explain why it is necessary despite the word tawassul.

Core Idea
The restriction 'ala wajh al-tahqiq is needed to explicitly exclude sciences like disputation that only indirectly lead to fiqh, preventing their mistaken inclusion.

In defining usul al-fiqh, scholars used the phrase 'ala wajh al-tahqiq ('on the basis of verification') to specify that this science leads to fiqh through direct, verified means. An objection was raised that this restriction is redundant because the word tawassul ('reaching') already implies proximate reaching. This passage presents that objection and the answer that clarifies why the restriction is necessary to avoid confusion with other sciences that discuss fiqh issues but do not directly yield rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the restriction and its stated purpose
Find the phrase 'ala wajh al-tahqiq in the definition. The commentator says it was added to exclude 'ilm al-munazarah (disputation) and 'ilm al-jadal (dialectics).
2
Understand the objection
The objector claims the restriction is unnecessary because 'tawassul' itself implies proximate reaching, and disputation only leads to fiqh distantly, so it is already excluded.
The objector's logic: if tawassul means proximate reaching, then distant sciences are automatically excluded.
3
Analyze the logic of distant vs proximate reaching
Consider how disputation leads to fiqh: a dialectician either defends his own ruling or refutes an opponent's, and only after that does one reach fiqh. This is a distant, indirect path.
Proximate reaching means the discipline's primary output is fiqh rulings; distant means fiqh is a secondary byproduct.
4
Examine the answer and its basis
The answer concedes that proximate reaching excludes disputation, but notes that disputation contains so many fiqh issues that one might mistakenly think it is part of fiqh. The restriction is a safeguard against this error.
The abundance of fiqh topics in munazarah creates a wahm (illusion) of inclusion.
5
Conclude the need for explicit restriction
Summarize: the restriction 'ala wajh al-tahqiq is not redundant; it is a necessary clarification to prevent misclassification, despite tawassul already implying proximity.
This demonstrates a principle in definition-making: explicit exclusions guard against probable mistakes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تفصیل مذکور نہیں ہوتی تو لفظ قواعد ہی اجمال کی طرف مشعر ہے۔ 354 وزاد: یہ شرح کی عبارت کا ساتواں حصہ ہے مصنف نے علی وجہ تحقیق کی قید لگائی علم مناظرہ وعلم جدل وغیرہ کو خارج کرنے کیلئے۔ ولقائل:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا آخری حصہ ہے غرض شاریخ اعتراض کر کے اس کا جواب دینا ہے۔ اعتراض: ۔ یہ ہے کہ علی وجہ التحقیق کی قید کی ضرورت نہیں ہے کیونکہ توصل سے توصل قریب مراد ہے اور علم مناظرہ سے توصل بعید ہوتا ہے کیونکہ جدلی یا تو اپنے حکم اور اصل کی حفاظت کرے گا یا مخالف کے حکم کو توڑے گا پھر اس کے بعد فقہ تک توصل ہوگا تو علم خلاف سے جب توصل بعید ہوتا ہے تو علی وجہ التحقیق کی ضرورت ہی نہیں تھی کیونکہ علم خلاف تو توصل کی قید ہی سے خارج ہو جاتا ہے۔ جواب: ٹھیک ہے توصل قریب سے علم جدل و مناظرہ نکل گیا لیکن علم مناظرہ میں فقہ کے مسائل اتنی کثرت سے ہوتے ہیں کہ وہم ہونے لگا ہے کہ شاید یہ فقہ میں داخل ہیں تو قید لگائی کہ یہ فقہ میں داخل نہیں ہیں۔
The detail is not mentioned, so the word 'qawa'id' itself indicates ambiguity. 354 And he added: This is the seventh portion of the commentary's text. The author placed the restriction 'ala wajh al-tahqiq to exclude the science of disputation (munazarah) and dialectics (jadal) etc. And for the objector: This is the last portion of the commentary's text. In short, the commentator raises an objection and answers it. The objection: This is that the restriction 'ala wajh al-tahqiq is not needed because 'tawassul' means proximate reaching, and from the science of disputation there is distant reaching, because the dialectician either preserves his own ruling and source or refutes the opponent's ruling, then after that reaching to fiqh occurs. So when from the science of disputation there is distant reaching, then the restriction 'ala wajh al-tahqiq was not needed, because the science of disputation is excluded by the restriction of 'tawassul'. Answer: It is true that proximate reaching excludes the science of dialectics and disputation, but in the science of disputation there are so many legal issues that it becomes probable that they might be included in fiqh, so the restriction was placed that they are not included in fiqh.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage is a teacher's explanation of a particular restriction in the definition of usul al-fiqh. The author (of the sharh) explains that the phrase 'ala wajh al-tahqiq (on the basis of verification) was added to exclude fields like disputation (munazarah) and dialectics (jadal) from the definition. An objector argues that this restriction is redundant because the word 'tawassul' (means to reach) already implies proximate reaching, and disputation only leads to fiqh distantly, so it is already excluded. The answer clarifies that although disputation leads distantly, it contains many legal issues that could mistakenly be considered part of fiqh. Therefore, the restriction was needed to explicitly exclude them.

Key Terms
على وجه التحقيق (‘alā wajh al-taḥqīq): A restriction meaning 'on the basis of verification,' indicating that the discipline leads to fiqh through direct, verified means.
توصل (tawassul): Means 'to reach' or 'to attain'; here it refers to how a discipline leads to the knowledge of fiqh.
علم مناظرہ (‘ilm al-munāẓarah): The science of disputation; a field that involves debate but does not directly yield fiqh rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To include the science of dialectics.
B) To exclude fields like disputation and dialectics that only indirectly lead to fiqh.
C) To emphasize that usul al-fiqh is only for mujtahids.
D) To make the definition more general.

Key Takeaway
The restriction 'ala wajh al-tahqiq is a necessary clarification to prevent the science of disputation from being mistakenly considered part of usul al-fiqh.

6 min
Objection to Including Taqlid in Usul al-Fiqh
Commentator refutes matn's view that muqallid can be mutawassil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on the status of taqlid discussions in usul al-fiqh and evaluate the commentator's critique of the matn author's view.

Core Idea
Taqlid is discussed in usul only as a foil to ijtihad, not as a subject of the discipline.

In this passage, the commentator (sharih) critiques a suggestion from the matn author that discussing taqlid might be part of usul al-fiqh. He argues that no scholar has ever considered taqlid as a subject of usul; rather, it is mentioned only to clarify ijtihad by contrast. Understanding this clarifies the epistemological boundaries of usul al-fiqh as a discipline limited to the four proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being critiqued
Find the matn author's suggestion that it is not unlikely to say that taqlid discussions belong to usul al-fiqh.
The matn phrasing: 'wa la yub'adu an yuqala'.
2
State the commentator's objection
The commentator says this view is far-fetched (ba'id) and no one has adopted it.
3
Find the basis of the objection
The commentator cites the consensus of usul scholars who explicitly state that they discuss taqlid only to clarify ijtihad by contrast, not because it is a subject of usul.
Principle: al-ashya' tu'raf bi-addadiha.
4
Explain the methodological reason
Taqlid is the opposite of ijtihad; discussing it helps define ijtihad, not because taqlid itself is a source of law.
This is a pedagogical tool, not a substantive inclusion.
5
Determine the practical consequence
If taqlid were part of usul, a muqallid could be considered a faqih, contradicting the Hanafi definition of fiqh as knowledge derived directly from the four proofs.
Thamarah al-khilaf: the scope of who is a faqih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ ) وَلَا يَبْعُدُ أَنْ يُقَالَ ( الظَّاهِرُ إِنَّهُ بَعِيدٌ لَمْ يَذْهَبُ إِلَيْهِ أَحَدٌ وَالْمُتَعَرِّضُونَ لِمَبَاحِثِ التَّقْلِيدِ فِى كُتُبِهِمُ مُصَرِّحُونَ بِأَنَّ الْبَحْتَ عَنْهُ إِنَّمَا وَقَعَ مِنْ جِهَةِ كَوْنِهِ فِي مُقَابَلَةِ الاجْتِهَادِ لَا مِنْ جِهَةِ أَنَّهُ مِنْ أُصُولِ الْفِقْهِ
قوله ولا يبعدان يقال : ظاہر یہ ہے کہ بیشک یہ بعید ہے۔ نہیں گیا اس کی طرف کوئی ایک۔ اور درپے ہونے والے تقلید کی مباحث میں وہ تصریح کرتے ہیں اپنی کتابوں میں کہ بیشک بحث اس سے سوائے اس کے نہیں کہ واقع ہوئی ہے اس جہت سے وہ اجتہاد کے مقابلہ میں ہے۔ نہ اس جہت سے کہ یہ اصول فقہ سے ہے۔
His statement: 'And it is not unlikely that it be said' — apparent meaning: indeed it is unlikely; no one has adopted it. And those who engage in discussions of taqlid in their books explicitly state that the investigation of it only occurred because it is in contrast to ijtihad, not because it is from usul al-fiqh. Urdu: His saying 'wa la yub'adu an yuqala' — apparent meaning: indeed it is unlikely. No one has gone towards it. And those engaged in discussions of taqlid in their books explicitly state that the discussion about it is only because it is in contrast to ijtihad, not from the perspective that it is from usul al-fiqh.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (usul_dispute) between the commentator (sharih) and the matn author (Sadr al-Shariah). The matn had suggested that it is not unlikely that a muqallid could be considered a mutawassil (one who reaches fiqh) alongside a mujtahid, making the discussion of taqlid part of usul al-fiqh. The commentator objects, stating that this view is far-fetched and no scholar has adopted it. He points out that those who discuss taqlid in their books do so only to clarify ijtihad by contrast (since things are known by their opposites), not because taqlid is a subject of usul al-fiqh. The Urdu translation and brief commentary follow the Arabic, reinforcing that the inclusion of taqlid discussions in usul works is a methodological tool, not a substantive inclusion.

Key Terms
تَقْلِيد (taqlid): Following the ruling of a mujtahid without knowing the dalil

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafi usul scholars include discussions of taqlid in their books, according to the commentator?
A) Because taqlid is a fundamental source of Islamic law
B) Because it is necessary to understand the rules of ijtihad by contrast
C) Because the matn author considered it part of usul
D) Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded it

Key Takeaway
Taqlid is discussed in usul al-fiqh only as a contrast to ijtihad, not as an integral subject.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
10 min
The Role of Rulings in Usul al-Fiqh: Subordination to Evidences
Explaining the structural relationship between evidences and rulings in usul al-fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi view that rulings are discussed after or subordinate to evidences in usul al-fiqh and identify the two meanings of 'ilhaq' (attachment).

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, rulings are always secondary to evidences — they are mentioned later and as subordinates.

This lesson examines the structural relationship between evidences (adillah) and rulings (ahkam) in usul al-fiqh. The commentator explains that rulings are 'appended' (yulhaq) to evidences, either in order of priority or as a subordinate topic. Understanding this hierarchy is crucial for grasping how Hanafi usul al-fiqh organizes its subject matter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase 'yulhaq bihi'
Find the phrase in the Arabic text where it says that the discussion of rulings is appended to the discussion of evidences. Note that the pronoun refers to the discussion of evidences.
The discussion of evidences is the primary topic.
2
Understand the two meanings of attachment
The commentator explains that attachment can mean (1) posteriority — rulings are mentioned after evidences because evidences are more important, or (2) subordination — rulings are discussed as a subordinate topic, similar to how logic discusses quiddities as means to the end.
Both meanings emphasize the primacy of evidences.
3
Relate to the subject of usul al-fiqh
Usul al-fiqh primarily deals with the evidences (adillah) themselves, and rulings are only included in relation to those evidences. This is a distinctive feature of the Hanafi approach.
Some other books of usul might not even include rulings, but here they are included as subordinate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

اسی طرح یہاں ہے اور اصول فقہ کی بعض کتابوں میں نہیں شمار کیا جاتا حکم کی مباحث کو اس علم کی مباحث سے لیکن صحیح وہ احتمال اول ہے۔ اور اس کا قول و ھو الحکم پس اگر مراد لیا جائے حکم سے وہ خطاب جو متعلق بحث کرنا اور محکوم علیہ سے بحث کرنا اور محکوم بہ سے بحث کرنا یہ متعلقات حکم میں داخل ہے۔

قوله وهو كحكم : اس عبارت سے سوال مقدر کا جواب دیا ہے۔ سوال: یہ ہے کہ مطیع میں کہا تھا یلحق به عما یعنی ان چیزوں سے بحث ہوتی ہے جو دلائل سے ثابت ہوں اور دلائل سے حکم ثابت ہوتا ہے اب حکم سے کیا مراد ہے اگر حکم سے مراد خطاب اللہ المتعلق با فعال المتکلمین ہے تو یہ دلائل سے ثابت نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ جو چیز دلائل سے ثابت ہو وہ پہلے معدوم ہوتی ہے اور خطاب اللہ قدیم ہے تو اگر حکم سے مراد خطاب اللہ لیتے ہیں تو خطاب اللہ کا حادث ہونا لازم آئے گا اور اگر حکم سے خطاب اللہ کے اثر و نتیجہ (یعنی اباحت حرمت وغیرہ کو ) مراد لیں تو ان کا دلائل ثلاثہ سے ثبوت یقینی ہے لیکن یہ قیاس سے ثابت نہیں ہوتے اس لیے کہ قیاس مثبت نہیں ہے وہ صرف مظہر احکام ہے پھر ادلہ کے بارے میں مطلقا کیسے کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ یہ مثبت احکام ہیں۔

جواب: - ماتن نے فرمایا کہ حکم کی دونوں جہتیں یعنی خطاب اللہ تعالیٰ اور اس کا اثر مراد لے سکتے ہیں اور اگر پہلی صورت میں خطاب اللہ کا حادث ہونا لازم آتا ہے تو اس کا جواب یہ دیا کہ ادلہ سے خطاب اللہ کا نفس ثبوت مراد نہیں بلکہ ثبوت لعلمنا مراد ہے یعنی ہمارے علم میں ثابت ہے اب ہم حادث ہیں تو ہمارا علم بھی حادث ہے نفس خطاب حادث نہیں ہے اور اگر آثار مراد ہوں پھر بھی درست ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں ہم کہتے ہیں کہ ادلہ ثلاثہ سے ثبوت یقینی ہے اور قیاس سے ثبوت ظنی ہوگا۔ سوال:۔ آپ کی تقریر میں جمع بین الحقیقت والجاز ہے وہ اس طرح کہ آپ نے الہ ثلاثہ سے ثبوت قطعی مراد لیا بی ثبوت کا اطلاق قطعیت میں حقیقت ہے اور قیاس سے فنی ثبوت مراد لیا ہے اور ثبوت کا اطلاق طنی معنی پر مجاز ہے لہذا یہ جمع بین الحقیقت والمجاز ہے اور یہ درست نہیں ہے۔

جواب : یہ عموم مجاز ہے کہ ثبوت سے مراد مطلقا اور اک ہے چاہے قطعی ہو یا ظنی ہو یعنی ان آثار کا ادراک ادلہ اربعہ سے ہوتا ہے پھر عام ہے کہ اور اک قطعا ہو یا ظناً ہو یا یہ کہ ثبوت سے مراد یہ ہے کہ غلبہ بطن ادلہ اربعہ سے حاصل ہوتا ہے اور غلبہ ظن عام ہے رائج ہو یا مرجوح ہو ۔ رائج ہے تو یہ ثبوت قطعی ہے اور اگر مرجوح ہے تو ثبوت ملنی ہے اور عموم مجاز کہتے ہیں کہ ایسا معنی مراد لیں کہ حقیقی و مجازی معنی اس کے فرد بن جائیں (واللہ اعلم بالصواب)

تلویح
قَوْلُهُ ) أَن يُذْكَرَ مَبَاحِبُّ الْحُكُم بَعْدَ مَبَاحِثِ الْأَدِلَّةِ ؛ لأنَّ الدَّلِيلَ مُقَدَّم
(The passage is in Urdu with Arabic phrases; literal English translation:) The discussion on the method of tabeeyah (subordination) regarding the states of the concept of the thing sought, just as in logic, the discussion is about quiddities which accept definitions. So this discussion is mentioned in the manner of being subordinate. Similarly here, and in some books of usul al-fiqh, the discussions of rulings are not counted among the discussions of this science, but the correct view is the first possibility. And his statement 'and it is the ruling': if by 'ruling' is meant that address which relates to the actions of the legally responsible, and it is eternal, then its being established by the evidences is like the establishment of our knowledge of it. And if by 'ruling' is meant the effect of the address, such as obligation and prohibition, then its being established by some of the four evidences is correct and by some not, such as by analogy, because analogy does not establish obligation but rather establishes for us overwhelming probability regarding obligation, as it is said that analogy is a discloser, not an establisher. Then the meaning of 'establishment' here would be the establishment of overwhelming probability. And if it is objected that one word cannot be used for both its real and metaphorical meanings together, then we will answer that we intend by it, in all cases, the establishment for us of knowledge or the establishment for us of overwhelming probability. The explanation of the attachment of the discussions of rulings and their dependencies to the discussions of evidences: from what preceded in 'yulhaq bihi', it became clear that in usul al-fiqh there is discussion of evidences and their states. Now he says that the discussion of the ruling and its dependencies will be attached to this discussion. And after the text of al-Tanqih, the author clarifies the text and defines the meaning of attachment: he said 'and appended to it is the discussion of that which is established by the evidences, i.e., the ruling and that which pertains to the ruling.' The summary is that the discussions of evidences are followed by the discussions of rulings. And attachment has two meanings: (1) posteriority, i.e., the rulings and their dependencies will be mentioned later, because evidences are more important and rulings are less important, and the evidence is prior by essence and the ruling is posterior, so the states of evidences come first and the states of rulings later; (2) subordination, i.e., the discussion of rulings is mentioned in a subordinate manner, meaning that the subject of usul al-fiqh is evidences, and rulings are treated as subordinate, just as the subject of logic is concept and assent as means, but the discussion of the concept of the thing sought is concomitant. And he explained the dependencies of the ruling: what is meant by dependencies is discussing the ruling, discussing the subject of the ruling (mahkum alayh), and discussing the subject matter of the ruling (mahkum bih). These are included in the dependencies of the ruling. His statement 'and it is so-and-so' is a response to a presumed objection. The objection: In the matn it was said 'yulhaq bihi ma' meaning that there is discussion of things that are established by the evidences, and the ruling is established by the evidences. So what is meant by 'ruling'? If by 'ruling' is meant the address of Allah related to the actions of the legally responsible, then it is not established by the evidences because something established by evidences must have been previously non-existent, and the address of Allah is eternal. If we take 'ruling' to mean the address of Allah, then the address would have to be temporal. And if we take 'ruling' to mean the effect and result of the address (such as permission, prohibition, etc.), then their establishment by the three evidences is certain, but they are not established by analogy, because analogy is not an establisher but only a discloser of rulings. So how can it be said absolutely that the evidences are establishers of rulings? The answer: The author said that we can intend both aspects of the ruling, i.e., the address of Allah and its effect. And if in the first case the address must be temporal, the answer is that what is meant by 'establishment' from the evidences is not the actual establishment of the address, but rather establishment in our knowledge, i.e., it is established in our knowledge. We are temporal, so our knowledge is also temporal, but the address itself is not temporal. And if the effects are meant, then it is also correct, because in that case we say that from the three evidences the establishment is certain, and from analogy the establishment would be probable. Another objection: Your argument contains a combination of the real and metaphorical meanings, because you took from the three evidences a certain establishment, and the application of 'establishment' to certainty is real, and from analogy you took probable establishment, and the application of 'establishment' to probable meaning is metaphorical. Hence this is a combination of real and metaphorical, which is not correct. The answer: This is a general metaphor ('umum al-majaz), meaning that by 'thubut' is intended absolutely and generally, whether certain or probable. That is, the perception of these effects occurs through all four evidences, and it is general that they are either certainly or probably perceived. Or that by 'thubut' is meant the obtaining of overwhelming probability from the four evidences, and overwhelming probability is general, whether it is preponderant or outweighed. If it is preponderant, it is certain establishment; if outweighed, it is probable establishment. And 'umum al-majaz' means that we intend such a meaning that both the real and metaphorical meanings become individuals under it. (And Allah knows best.) At-Talwih: 'His statement: that the discussions of the ruling are mentioned after the discussions of the evidence because the evidence is prior.'
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on At-Tawdih addressing how discussions of rulings (ahkam) relate to discussions of evidences (adillah) in usul al-fiqh. It begins by explaining the phrase 'yulhaq bihi' (appended to it), clarifying that rulings are discussed after or subordinate to evidences. The commentator then tackles a key objection: if 'hukm' (ruling) refers to Allah's eternal address, how can it be 'established' by created evidences? The answer distinguishes between the address itself and our knowledge of it. Similarly, if 'hukm' refers to the resulting effects (obligation, prohibition), these are established by the three primary sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma) with certainty, but by qiyas (analogy) only with probability (ghalabat al-zann), as qiyas is a 'muzhir' (discloser) not a 'muthbit' (creator) of rulings. The passage then defends against the charge of combining real and metaphorical meanings by introducing 'umum al-majaz' (general metaphor), where the word 'thubut' is used in a sense that includes both certain and probable establishment. This demonstrates the Hanafi usul methodology of defending the role of qiyas and clarifying the scope of legal terms.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): In this context, either the eternal address of Allah or the effect of that address (obligation, prohibition, etc.).
ثبوت (thubut): Establishment; here meaning either certain knowledge (qat'i) or probable knowledge (zanni) of the ruling.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction; considered a 'muzhir' (discloser) of rulings, not a 'muthbit' (establisher) in the sense of creating the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what does 'thubut' (establishment) of a ruling by qiyas mean?
A) Qiyas creates the ruling as a new entity.
B) Qiyas produces overwhelming probability (ghalabat al-zann) about the ruling, not certainty.
C) Qiyas provides certain knowledge like the Quran.
D) Qiyas does not establish any ruling; it is only a logical exercise.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, rulings are subordinate to evidences, and the establishment of hukm by qiyas is understood as probable knowledge, with the term 'thubut' covering both certain and probable senses.

15 min
The Hanafi Response to the Objection on the Establishment of Hukm
Addressing objections about the establishment of hukm by evidences, especially qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the objection against the establishment of hukm by qiyas and explain the Hanafi response using the concepts of 'thubut li 'ilmina' and 'umum al-majaz'.

Core Idea
Hukm is established in our knowledge, not in itself; qiyas provides probable knowledge, and 'umum al-majaz' reconciles certainty and probability.

This lesson delves into a key objection raised against the inclusion of qiyas as a source of hukm: if hukm is eternal, how can it be established by temporal evidences? If it is an effect, how can qiyas establish it if qiyas only discloses? The Hanafi response clarifies that 'thubut' refers to our knowledge, not the existence of the ruling, and that the term can be used in a general sense covering both certain and probable knowledge, through the literary device of 'umum al-majaz'.

Guided Path
1
State the objection
Clearly articulate the two-pronged objection: (1) If hukm means Allah's eternal address, evidences cannot establish it because it pre-exists. (2) If hukm means the effect (obligation, prohibition), qiyas cannot establish it because it is only a discloser, not an originator.
The objection is directed at the claim that rulings are 'established' by evidences.
2
Identify the two meanings of hukm
Recognize that the Hanafi response first distinguishes between two valid definitions of hukm: the address (khitab) and its effect (athar). The response then addresses each meaning separately.
This dual definition is central to Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the Hanafi answer for each meaning
For the address: 'thubut' means establishment in our knowledge (thubut li 'ilmina), not creation of the address itself. For the effect: the three primary sources give certainty, while qiyas gives probability (ghalabat al-zann).
Qiyas is thus a valid source of probable hukm.
4
Examine the second objection about combining real and metaphorical meanings
The objector argues that using 'thubut' for both certain (real) and probable (metaphorical) is invalid. The Hanafi response introduces 'umum al-majaz' (general metaphor): a single term can cover both meanings if they fall under a broader concept.
'Umum al-majaz' is a recognized rhetorical figure in Arabic.

جواب: - ماتن نے فرمایا کہ حکم کی دونوں جہتیں یعنی خطاب اللہ تعالیٰ اور اس کا اثر مراد لے سکتے ہیں اور اگر پہلی صورت میں خطاب اللہ کا حادث ہونا لازم آتا ہے تو اس کا جواب یہ دیا کہ ادلہ سے خطاب اللہ کا نفس ثبوت مراد نہیں بلکہ ثبوت لعلمنا مراد ہے یعنی ہمارے علم میں ثابت ہے اب ہم حادث ہیں تو ہمارا علم بھی حادث ہے نفس خطاب حادث نہیں ہے اور اگر آثار مراد ہوں پھر بھی درست ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں ہم کہتے ہیں کہ ادلہ ثلاثہ سے ثبوت یقینی ہے اور قیاس سے ثبوت ظنی ہوگا۔ سوال:۔ آپ کی تقریر میں جمع بین الحقیقت والجاز ہے وہ اس طرح کہ آپ نے الہ ثلاثہ سے ثبوت قطعی مراد لیا بی ثبوت کا اطلاق قطعیت میں حقیقت ہے اور قیاس سے فنی ثبوت مراد لیا ہے اور ثبوت کا اطلاق طنی معنی پر مجاز ہے لہذا یہ جمع بین الحقیقت والمجاز ہے اور یہ درست نہیں ہے۔

جواب : یہ عموم مجاز ہے کہ ثبوت سے مراد مطلقا اور اک ہے چاہے قطعی ہو یا ظنی ہو یعنی ان آثار کا ادراک ادلہ اربعہ سے ہوتا ہے پھر عام ہے کہ اور اک قطعا ہو یا ظناً ہو یا یہ کہ ثبوت سے مراد یہ ہے کہ غلبہ بطن ادلہ اربعہ سے حاصل ہوتا ہے اور غلبہ ظن عام ہے رائج ہو یا مرجوح ہو ۔ رائج ہے تو یہ ثبوت قطعی ہے اور اگر مرجوح ہے تو ثبوت ملنی ہے اور عموم مجاز کہتے ہیں کہ ایسا معنی مراد لیں کہ حقیقی و مجازی معنی اس کے فرد بن جائیں (واللہ اعلم بالصواب)

تلویح
قَوْلُهُ ) أَن يُذْكَرَ مَبَاحِبُّ الْحُكُم بَعْدَ مَبَاحِثِ الْأَدِلَّةِ ؛ لأنَّ الدَّلِيلَ مُقَدَّم
(The passage is in Urdu with Arabic phrases; literal English translation:) The discussion on the method of tabeeyah (subordination) regarding the states of the concept of the thing sought, just as in logic, the discussion is about quiddities which accept definitions. So this discussion is mentioned in the manner of being subordinate. Similarly here, and in some books of usul al-fiqh, the discussions of rulings are not counted among the discussions of this science, but the correct view is the first possibility. And his statement 'and it is the ruling': if by 'ruling' is meant that address which relates to the actions of the legally responsible, and it is eternal, then its being established by the evidences is like the establishment of our knowledge of it. And if by 'ruling' is meant the effect of the address, such as obligation and prohibition, then its being established by some of the four evidences is correct and by some not, such as by analogy, because analogy does not establish obligation but rather establishes for us overwhelming probability regarding obligation, as it is said that analogy is a discloser, not an establisher. Then the meaning of 'establishment' here would be the establishment of overwhelming probability. And if it is objected that one word cannot be used for both its real and metaphorical meanings together, then we will answer that we intend by it, in all cases, the establishment for us of knowledge or the establishment for us of overwhelming probability. The explanation of the attachment of the discussions of rulings and their dependencies to the discussions of evidences: from what preceded in 'yulhaq bihi', it became clear that in usul al-fiqh there is discussion of evidences and their states. Now he says that the discussion of the ruling and its dependencies will be attached to this discussion. And after the text of al-Tanqih, the author clarifies the text and defines the meaning of attachment: he said 'and appended to it is the discussion of that which is established by the evidences, i.e., the ruling and that which pertains to the ruling.' The summary is that the discussions of evidences are followed by the discussions of rulings. And attachment has two meanings: (1) posteriority, i.e., the rulings and their dependencies will be mentioned later, because evidences are more important and rulings are less important, and the evidence is prior by essence and the ruling is posterior, so the states of evidences come first and the states of rulings later; (2) subordination, i.e., the discussion of rulings is mentioned in a subordinate manner, meaning that the subject of usul al-fiqh is evidences, and rulings are treated as subordinate, just as the subject of logic is concept and assent as means, but the discussion of the concept of the thing sought is concomitant. And he explained the dependencies of the ruling: what is meant by dependencies is discussing the ruling, discussing the subject of the ruling (mahkum alayh), and discussing the subject matter of the ruling (mahkum bih). These are included in the dependencies of the ruling. His statement 'and it is so-and-so' is a response to a presumed objection. The objection: In the matn it was said 'yulhaq bihi ma' meaning that there is discussion of things that are established by the evidences, and the ruling is established by the evidences. So what is meant by 'ruling'? If by 'ruling' is meant the address of Allah related to the actions of the legally responsible, then it is not established by the evidences because something established by evidences must have been previously non-existent, and the address of Allah is eternal. If we take 'ruling' to mean the address of Allah, then the address would have to be temporal. And if we take 'ruling' to mean the effect and result of the address (such as permission, prohibition, etc.), then their establishment by the three evidences is certain, but they are not established by analogy, because analogy is not an establisher but only a discloser of rulings. So how can it be said absolutely that the evidences are establishers of rulings? The answer: The author said that we can intend both aspects of the ruling, i.e., the address of Allah and its effect. And if in the first case the address must be temporal, the answer is that what is meant by 'establishment' from the evidences is not the actual establishment of the address, but rather establishment in our knowledge, i.e., it is established in our knowledge. We are temporal, so our knowledge is also temporal, but the address itself is not temporal. And if the effects are meant, then it is also correct, because in that case we say that from the three evidences the establishment is certain, and from analogy the establishment would be probable. Another objection: Your argument contains a combination of the real and metaphorical meanings, because you took from the three evidences a certain establishment, and the application of 'establishment' to certainty is real, and from analogy you took probable establishment, and the application of 'establishment' to probable meaning is metaphorical. Hence this is a combination of real and metaphorical, which is not correct. The answer: This is a general metaphor ('umum al-majaz), meaning that by 'thubut' is intended absolutely and generally, whether certain or probable. That is, the perception of these effects occurs through all four evidences, and it is general that they are either certainly or probably perceived. Or that by 'thubut' is meant the obtaining of overwhelming probability from the four evidences, and overwhelming probability is general, whether it is preponderant or outweighed. If it is preponderant, it is certain establishment; if outweighed, it is probable establishment. And 'umum al-majaz' means that we intend such a meaning that both the real and metaphorical meanings become individuals under it. (And Allah knows best.) At-Talwih: 'His statement: that the discussions of the ruling are mentioned after the discussions of the evidence because the evidence is prior.'
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on At-Tawdih addressing how discussions of rulings (ahkam) relate to discussions of evidences (adillah) in usul al-fiqh. It begins by explaining the phrase 'yulhaq bihi' (appended to it), clarifying that rulings are discussed after or subordinate to evidences. The commentator then tackles a key objection: if 'hukm' (ruling) refers to Allah's eternal address, how can it be 'established' by created evidences? The answer distinguishes between the address itself and our knowledge of it. Similarly, if 'hukm' refers to the resulting effects (obligation, prohibition), these are established by the three primary sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma) with certainty, but by qiyas (analogy) only with probability (ghalabat al-zann), as qiyas is a 'muzhir' (discloser) not a 'muthbit' (creator) of rulings. The passage then defends against the charge of combining real and metaphorical meanings by introducing 'umum al-majaz' (general metaphor), where the word 'thubut' is used in a sense that includes both certain and probable establishment. This demonstrates the Hanafi usul methodology of defending the role of qiyas and clarifying the scope of legal terms.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): Either the eternal address of Allah or the effect of that address (obligation, prohibition, etc.).
ثبوت (thubut): Establishment; in this context, it means either certain knowledge (qat'i) or probable knowledge (zanni) of the ruling, not necessarily the existence of the ruling itself.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction; in Hanafi usul, it is considered a 'muzhir' (discloser) of rulings, not a 'muthbit' (establisher) in the sense of creating the ruling.
عموم المجاز (umum al-majaz): A general metaphor where a word is used in a sense that encompasses both its literal and metaphorical applications as individuals under a broader concept.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi response to the objection that using 'thubut' for both certain and probable establishment is a forbidden combination of real and metaphorical meanings?
A) They change the subject and avoid the issue.
B) They argue that both are real meanings in their own context.
C) They invoke 'umum al-majaz', where a general meaning includes both real and metaphorical senses.
D) They admit that the word is used loosely and accept the criticism.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defends qiyas as a valid source of probable hukm by clarifying that 'thubut' refers to epistemic establishment and by using 'umum al-majaz' to allow the term to cover both certainty and probability.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
12 min
The Dispute over Multiplicity of Subject Matters in Usul and Logic
Critique and defense of the claim that a science cannot have multiple subjects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Hanafi and Mutakallim positions on taddud al-mawdu' and apply the Hanafi argument against multiplicity to critique the opposing view.

Core Idea
A science must have one subject in essence; apparent multiplicity is only in considerations, not reality.

This passage tackles a foundational issue in usul al-fiqh: can a single science have multiple subject matters? The matn author (al-Tawdih) denies multiplicity, but his own examples from usul al-fiqh (the four proofs) and logic (conception and assent) seem to contradict his claim. The commentator (sharih) refines the position by distinguishing between the concept (mafhum) and its instances (masadiq), arguing that taking instances as subject leads to infinite regress. The apparent multiplicity is resolved by a unifying consideration: all instances share the attribute of being evidence (in usul) or being conducive (in logic).

Guided Path
1
Identify the core claim and the apparent contradiction
The matn author asserts that a science cannot have multiple subjects. Yet his examples from usul al-fiqh (the four proofs) and logic (conception and assent) appear to show multiple subjects. Pinpoint exactly where the examples seem to support multiplicity.
Focus on the fact that essential attributes are predicated on instances, not on the meaning.
2
Understand the opposing argument from al-Talwih (Taftazani)
Al-Talwih argues that because the essential attributes (e.g., being evidence) apply to the instances (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) and not to the abstract meaning, the instances become the actual subject, thereby making the subject multiple. Similarly in logic, the attributes of conception and assent apply to their instances, making the subject multiple.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different views of what constitutes the subject of a science.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response focusing on the infinite regress argument
The Hanafi response uses a reductio: if instances are taken as subject, then in grammar, the subject 'word' would have to be the infinite instances of words, which is impossible. The same applies to usul al-fiqh. Therefore, the subject must be the concept (mafhum), not the instances. The multiplicity is only in the considerations (mazamin), not in the essence of the subject.
The key is that all instances share a single common attribute (e.g., being evidence) which is the real subject.
4
Distinguish between real multiplicity and multiplicity in considerations
The commentator shows that the apparent multiplicity is not real because the discussion of essential attributes ultimately serves one purpose: establishing rulings (in usul) or establishing knowledge (in logic). Thus, the subject is one in essence, and multiplicity is only in the aspects or considerations under which the subject is studied.
This resolves the contradiction: the examples only show multiplicity in the instances, but the science's subject remains a unified concept.

شئی سے خارج ہوتی ہے اور جو چیز شئی سے خارج ہو وہ عرض کے قبیل سے ہوتی ہے۔ وان ليس لأحد الخ ... باقی تمہیں یہ پریشانی تھی کہ ہر شخص اصطلاح قائم کریگا کہ موضوعات کے تعدد کے باوجود یہ علم واحد ہے مثلاً ایک شخص یہ کہتا ہے کہ علم فقہ اور علم ہندسہ یہ علم واحد ہے کہ یہ اصطلاح قائم کرے کہ علم فقہ اور علم ھندسہ علم واحد ہیں یہ کوئی پریشانی نہیں اس لئے کہ کسی کو یہ حق نہیں ہے کہ یہ اصطلاح قائم کرے کہ علم فقہ اور علم ہندسہ علم واحد ہیں باوجود یکہ موضوع میں تعدد ہے لیکن یہ جائز تب ہو گا جب اس میں تناسب ہوگا حالانکہ ان کے موضوعات میں کوئی تناسب نہیں ہے۔ ماتن کی بیان کردہ مثالوں پر شاریخ کا رد
ثم انه اوردفيما الخ... شارحٌ مصنف پر سوال کر رہے ہیں کہ آپ نے یہ دعوی کیا کہ موضوع میں تعدد جائز نہیں ہے اور جو مثالیں تم نے پیش کی ہیں ان سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ موضوع میں تعدد جائز ہے آپ نے دو مثالیں دی ہیں اصول فقہ کی اور منطق کی۔
مثال اول: یہ ہے کہ فن اصول فقہ کے محمولات یعنی عوارض ذاتیہ کا دلیل کے مفہوم کیلئے اثبات نہیں ہوگا بلکہ مصداق دلیل کیلئے اثبات ہوگا اور اس کا مصداق تو کتاب اللہ ۔ سنت رسول ما اجماع اور قیاس ہے یعنی بعض عوارض ایسے ہوں گے جو مختص ہوں گے صرف کتاب اللہ کے ساتھ۔ یا مختص ہوں گے سنت کے ساتھ یا اجماع کے ساتھ یا قیاس کے ساتھ اور بعض عوارض مشترک ہو نگے دو دو کے درمیان تو چار چیزوں کے عوارض ذاتیہ سے اس علم میں بحث ہوگی اور جن چیزوں کے عوارض ذاتیہ سے بحث ہو وہ اس کا موضوع ہوتی ہیں لہذا اصول فقہ کا موضوع چار چیزیں ہوئیں اور تم نے کہا کہ موضوع میں تعدد نہیں ہوتا۔
سوال:۔ اس صورت میں تو صاحب تو ضیح بھی تعدد موضوع کے قائل ہیں۔ جواب:۔ صاحب توضیح جس تعداد کے قائل ہیں وہ مضامین کے اعتبار سے ہے لیکن جو تعددان کے علاوہ ہو ان کے قائل نہیں ہیں اور صاحب تلویح جس تعدد کے قائل ہیں وہ قطع نظر مضامین کے ہے کیونکہ مضافین کے اعتبار سے تو موضوع دو ہی ہونگے یعنی مضاف اور مضاف الیہ لیکن علامہ صاحب نے ان مضافین کے علاوہ تعدد ثابت کیا ہے انہی مثالوں سے جن کو مائن نے ذکر کیا تھا۔ علامہ کے اصل اعتراض کا جواب
کہ جیسے علامہ صاحب نے تعدد موضوع اصول فقہ کے لئے ثابت کیا ہے بایں وجہ کہ ادلہ کے اعراض ذاتیہ کو مفہوم ادلہ کے لئے ثابت نہیں کیا جاتا بلکہ مصادیق ادلہ کے لئے ثابت کیا جاتا ہے لہذاوہ ( ما صدق علیہ الا دلتہ ) موضوع بنا حالانکہ وہ متعدد ہیں لہذا موضوع متعدد ہو گئے ۔ ہم یہ کہتے ہیں اگر یہاں اولہ کو موضوع بنا کر اس کے عوارض ذاتیہ کو اس کے لئے ثابت نہیں کیا بلکہ ما صدق علیہ الا دلتہ کو موضوع بنایا ہے تو پھر علم نحو میں بھی جائز ہوگا کہ کلمہ کو موضوع نہ بنایا جائے بلکہ ماصدق علیہ الکلمتہ کو موضوع بنایا جائے اور یہ میچ نہیں کیونکہ ماصدق علیہ الکلمتہ غیر متناہی ہے اور موضوع کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ وہ متناہی ہو اس طرح یہ بات تمام علوم کے موضوعات میں جاری ہو گی حالانکہ یہ محال کو ستلزم ہے اس لئے جیسے علم نحو میں موضوع (کلمہ ) سے مراد مصداق موضوع ( کلمہ ) مراد نہیں لیا جا سکتا اسی طرح یہاں اصول فقہ میں بھی ادلہ سے ان کے مصادیق مراد نہیں لئے جاسکتے لہذا العدد ثابت نہیں ہو گا کہ یوں کہیں کہ یہ مثالیں خود مائن کے قول کے مناقض ہیں۔
مثال ثانی۔ آپ نے منطق کی پیش کی تھی اس سے بھی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ موضوع میں تعدد جائز ہے اس لئے کہ یہاں تصور موصل اور تصدیق موصل کے عوارض ذاتیہ مفہوم کیلئے ثابت نہیں ہوں گے بلکہ مصداق کیلئے ثابت ہونگے اور تصور کا مصداق اس کا حد تام ہونا حد ناقص ہو نا رسم تام اور رسم ناقص ہوتا ہے اور تصدیق کا مصداق حجت ہونا استقراء اور تمثیل ہونا وغیرہ ہے لہذا اس سے بھی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ موضوع میں تعدد جائز ہے۔
جواب:۔ یہ ہے کہ یہ کون کہتا ہے کہ تعدد ہے بلکہ ان سب کا اشتراک ہے موصل ہونے میں اور ایصال من حیث الا صال یہ امر واحد ہے اور ایسے ہی صاحب توضیح رحمتہ اللہ علیہ علم اصول فقہ کے موضوع میں جس تعدد کے قائل ہیں یہ مضامین کے اعتبار سے ہے اور یہ بات بادی النظر میں اختلاف ہے حقیقت میں کوئی اختلاف نہیں ہے کیونکہ ان کے عوارض سے جو بحث ہوگی وہ اثبات احکام کے لحاظ سے ہوگی اور اثبات امر واحد ہے۔
A thing that is external to another thing is of the category of accident. And it is not for anyone... The remaining worry was that every person would establish a convention that despite the multiplicity of subjects, this science is one. For example, one person says that the science of fiqh and the science of geometry are one science; he establishes this convention that the science of fiqh and the science of geometry are one science. This is not a problem because no one has the right to establish such a convention that the science of fiqh and the science of geometry are one science despite the multiplicity of subject, but it would be permissible only if there is proportionality between them, whereas there is no proportionality between their subjects. The response of the commentator to the examples mentioned by the matn author. Then he mentioned in such and such... The commentator questions the author: You claimed that multiplicity in subject is not permissible, but from the examples you presented it appears that multiplicity in subject is permissible. You gave two examples: one from usul al-fiqh and one from logic. First example: In the discipline of usul al-fiqh, the predications, i.e., essential attributes, are not established for the meaning of evidence but for the instances of evidence. And its instances are the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Messenger, consensus, and analogy. So some attributes are specific to the Book of Allah alone, or to the Sunnah alone, or to consensus alone, or to analogy alone, and some attributes are shared between two. Thus, the essential attributes of four things are discussed in this science, and whatever things' essential attributes are discussed constitute its subject. Therefore, the subject of usul al-fiqh becomes four things, while you said that multiplicity of subject does not occur. Objection: In that case, the author of al-Tawdih also believes in multiplicity of subject. Answer: The author of al-Tawdih believes in multiplicity according to the considerations, but he does not believe in any multiplicity beyond that. And the author of al-Talwih believes in multiplicity irrespective of considerations, because according to the relational terms, the subject would only be two: the relatum and the relatum-to. But the venerable author (Allamah) established multiplicity beyond these relational terms through the very examples that the matn author mentioned. The response to the Allamah's original objection: Just as the Allamah established multiplicity of subject for usul al-fiqh on the grounds that the essential attributes of the proofs are not established for the meaning of the proofs but for the instances of the proofs, so those instances become the subject, and they are multiple; thus the subject becomes multiple. We say: If here the first is not taken as subject and its essential attributes established for it, but rather the instances of the proofs are made subject, then in the science of grammar it would also be permissible not to make 'word' the subject but to make the instances of 'word' the subject. But this is not acceptable because the instances of 'word' are infinite, and it is necessary for the subject to be finite. Thus, this would apply to the subjects of all sciences, and it would entail impossibility. Therefore, just as in grammar the subject 'word' is not intended to mean the instances of the word, similarly here in usul al-fiqh the proofs cannot be intended to mean their instances. Hence, multiplicity is not established to the extent that these examples themselves contradict the matn author's statement. Second example: You presented logic, and from this it is also known that multiplicity in subject is permissible because here the essential attributes of conducive conception and conducive assent are not established for the meaning but for the instances. The instance of conception is its being a complete definition, incomplete definition, complete description, or incomplete description; and the instance of assent is its being an argument, induction, or example, etc. Hence, from this also it is known that multiplicity in subject is permissible. Answer: This is that who says there is multiplicity? Rather, all of them share in being conducive, and rendering conducive in terms of being rendering is a single matter. Likewise, the author of al-Tawdih, may Allah have mercy on him, holds multiplicity in the subject of usul al-fiqh according to considerations. And this matter is apparently a dispute but in reality there is no dispute, because the discussion of their attributes will be in terms of establishing rulings, and establishing is a single matter.
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage presents a critical refinement of a claim in the matn (al-Tawdih) regarding the unity of subject matter in a science. The matn author argued that a science cannot have multiple subjects. However, his own examples from usul al-fiqh (the four proofs) and logic (conception and assent) seem to imply multiplicity. The commentator (sharih) responds by distinguishing between absolute multiplicity and multiplicity under different considerations (mazamin). The real issue is whether the subject of usul al-fiqh is the meanings of the proofs (mafahim) or their actual instances (masadiq). If the latter, the subject becomes multiple and possibly infinite, which is problematic. The resolution is that all the proofs share the aspect of being evidence (dalil), and the discussion of their essential attributes ultimately serves to establish rulings, which is a single goal. Thus, the multiplicity is only apparent, not real.

Key Terms
تعدد الموضوع (taddud al-mawdu'): The claim that a single science can have more than one subject matter.
المصداق (al-misdaq): The actual instances that fall under a concept, e.g., the four proofs as instances of the concept 'evidence'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the main problem with taking the actual instances (masadiq) of the proofs as the subject of usul al-fiqh?
A) The instances are infinite in number.
B) The instances are not known with certainty.
C) The instances are not essential to the science.
D) The instances are contradictory to each other.

Key Takeaway
The subject of a science must be a single concept; apparent multiplicity from instances is resolved by a unifying consideration (being evidence or being conducive).

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Differentiating Sciences by Essential Accidents
Arguing for distinguishing sciences by essential accidents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi argument for distinguishing sciences by essential accidents (mahmulat) and critique the opposing position that sciences are distinguished only by subject matter.

Core Idea
Multiple sciences can share one subject — they are distinguished by the essential accidents (predicates) they investigate.

This passage from Al-Tarwīḥ addresses a fundamental dispute in the classification of Islamic sciences. The common view held that each science is defined solely by its subject matter (mawḍūʿ). The author argues that sciences can also be distinguished by the essential accidents (ʿaraḍ dhātī / maḥmūl) they study, even if the subject is identical. This has direct implications for usul al-fiqh: for instance, fiqh and usul al-fiqh may share the subject of acts of mukallaf but differ in the predicates they investigate (legal rulings vs. evidence). We will walk through the rational proof and the concrete example provided.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What does the author claim regarding the differentiation of sciences? The author (representing the Hanafi approach) holds that sciences can be distinguished by the essential accidents (mahmulat) they investigate, even if the subject is the same.
2
Identify the opposing view
What is the position of those who object? They hold that sciences are distinguished only by subject matter; sharing a subject is impossible.
3
Follow the rational proof (dalil aqli)
How does the author argue for the possibility? A single thing can have diverse essential accidents; investigating different types yields different sciences.
4
Examine the example of occurrence
What actual example does the author cite? Astronomy and the science of the heavens both study the bodies of the universe, but astronomy investigates shapes, while the heavenly science investigates natures. Thus they share a subject but differ in predicates.
5
Derive the usul al-fiqh relevance
How does this dispute affect our understanding of fiqh and usul al-fiqh? The thamarah al-khilaf: recognizing that two disciplines can share a subject but differ in essential accidents helps us organize and differentiate Islamic sciences properly.

بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
الترويج لحل التوضيح و التلويح
ذاتیہ کی ایک نوع سے بحث ہو گی اور دوسرے علم میں عوارض ذاتیہ کی دوسری نوع سے بحث ہوگی۔
وان ارید سے سال مقدر کا جواب ہے۔
سوال:- یہ ہے کہ بھائی ٹھیک ہے آپ نے جو دلیل دی ہے کہ علوم کا امتیاز محمولیت کی وجہ سے ہوتا ہے لیکن کیا کریں کہ قوم نے ا مطلاح قائم کرلی ہے کہ علوم کا امتیاز موضوع سے ہو گا محمول اور عوارض ذاتیہ سے نہیں ہو گا ؟
جواب:۔ دیتے ہوئے مصنف نے کہا ٹھیک ہے تمہاری اصطلاح اپنی جگہ لیکن حقیقت یہ ہے کہ علوم کا امتیاز جس طرح موضوع ہو سکتا ہے ایسے ہی عوارض ذاتیہ سے بھی ہو سکتا ہے۔
خارج میں دو علوم کا موضوع فی واحد واقع ہے
علی ان قولهم : ۔ دوسرے دعوی کی دلیل دی ہے دعوی یہ تھا کہ خارج میں دوعلموں کا موضوع کی واحد واقع ہے حکماء کہتے ہیں کہ علم ہیئت کا موضوع اجسام عالم میں من حیث اشکل یعنی جتنے جسم ہیں کرہ اور عناصر ار بعد ان سے بنے والی چیز میں ان کی شکل مثلث مربع وغیرہ تو علم ہیئت مستقل فن ہے اس کا موضوع اجسام عالم ہے من حیث اشکل اور علم طبعی کی کئی قسمیں ہیں ایک قسم علم السماء ہے اس کا موضوع بھی اجسام عالم ہے من حیث الطبع اب علم ہیئت کا موضوع اجسام عالم اور علم سماء کا موضوع بھی اجسام عالم دو علم ہیں اور موضوع شئی واحد ہے کیونکہ دونوں علموں میں نفس حیثیت سے بحث ہوتی ہے معلوم ہوا حیثیت عوراض ذاتیہ کا بیان ہے اور جب حیثیت بیان ہے تو موضوع سے خارج ہو گی جب حیثیت خارج ہے تو دونوں علوم کا موضوع ایک چیز ہے اور وہ اجسام عالم ہے باقی امتیاز علوم میں عوارض ذاتیہ سے ہوگا ایک علم میں عوارض ذاتیہ کی ایک نوع شکل سے بحث ہوگی اور دوسرے علم میں عوارض ذاتیہ کی دوسری نوع طبیعت سے بحث ہوگی تو اس نوع کے اعتبار سے امتیاز ہوگا (واللہ اعلم بالصواب)۔
تلویح
قَوْلُهُ وَمِنْهَا أَنَّ الْمَشْهُورَ) الْمَبْحَثُ الثَّالِثُ فِي جَوَازِ تَشَارُكِ الْعُلُومِ الْمُخْتَلِفَةِ فِي مَوْضُوعٍ وَاحِدٍ بِالذَّاتِ وَالاعْتِبَارِ وَ كَمَا خَالَفَ الْقَوْمَ فِي جَوَازِ تَعَدُّدِ الْمَوْضُوعِ لِعِلْمٍ وَاحِدٍ كَذَلِكَ خَالَفَهُمْ فِي امْتِنَاعِ الْحَادِ الْمَوْضُوعِ لِعُلُومَ مُتَعَدِّدَةٍ وَادَّعَى جَوَازَهُ ، بَلْ وُقُوعَهُ أَمَّا الْجَوَازُ فَلَانَّهُ يَصِحُ أَنْ يَكُونَ لِشَيْءٍ وَاحِدٍ أَعْرَاضٌ ذَاتِيَّةٌ مُتَنَوِّعَةٌ أَى مُخْتَلِفَةٌ بِالنَّوْعِ يُبْحَثُ فِي عِلْمٍ عَنْ بَعْضِ أَنْوَاعِهَا ، وَفِي عِلْمٍ آخَرَ عَنْ بَعْضٍ آخَرَ فَيَتَمَايَرُ الْعِلْمَانِ اَوِ الْعُلُومِ بِالْأَعْرَاضِ الْمَبُحُوثِ عَنْهَا ، وَإِنْ اتَّحَدَ الْمَوْضُوعُ ، وَذَلِكَ ، لأنَّ الْحَادَ الْعِلْمِ وَاخْتِلَافَهُ إِنَّمَا هُوَ بِحَسَبِ الْمَعْلُومَاتِ أَعْنِي الْمَسَائِلَ وَ كَمَا تَتَّحِدُ الْمَسَائِلُ بِاتِّحَادِ مَوْضُوعَاتِهَا بِأَنْ يَرْجِعَ الْجَمِيعُ إِلَى مَوْضُوعِ الْعِلْمِ وَتَخْتَلِفُ بِاخْتِلافِهَا كَذَلِكَ تَتَّحِدُ بِالْحَادِ مَحْمُولَاتِهَا بِأَنْ يَرْجِعَ الْجَمِيعُ إِلَى نَوْعٍ مِنْ الْأَعْرَاضِ الدَّاتِيَّةِ لِلْمَوْضُوعِ وَتَخْتَلِفُ بِاخْتِلَافِهَا فَكَمَا اُعْتُبِرَ اخْتِلافُ العُلُومِ بِاخْتِلافِ الْمَوْضُوعَاتِ يَجُوزُ أَنْ يُعْتَبَرَ بِاخْتِلَافِ الْمَحْمُولَاتِ بأن يُؤْخَذَ مَوْضُوعٌ وَاحِدٌ بِالذَّاتِ وَالاعْتِبَارِ وَيُجْعَلَ الْبَحْثُ عَنْ بَعْضِ أَعْرَاضِهِ الذَّاتِيَّةِ عِلْمًا وَعَنْ الْبَعْضِ الْآخَرِ عِلْمًا آخَرَ فَيَكُونَانِ عِلْمَيْنِ مُتَشَارِكَيْنِ فِي الْمَوْضُوع مُتَمَايِزَيْنِ فِى الْمَحْمُولِ .
وَأَمَّا الْوُقُوعُ فَلَانَّهُمْ جَعَلُوا أَجْسَامَ الْعَالَمِ وَهِيَ الْبَسَائِطُ مَوْضُوعَ عِلْمِ الْهَيْئَةِ مِنْ حَيْثُ الشَّكْلِ وَمَوْضُوعَ عِلْمِ السَّمَاءِ وَالْعَالَمِ مِنْ حَيْثُ الطَّبِيعِيَّةِ وَالْحَيْنِيَّةُ فِيهِمَا بَيَانُ الْأَعْرَاضِ الذَّاتِيَّةِ الْمَبُحُوثِ عَنْهَا أجْزَاء الْمَوْضُوع وَإِلَّا لَمَا وَقَعَ الْبَحْتُ عَنْهَا فِي الْعِلْمَيْنِ فَمَوْضُوعُ كُلِّ مِنْهُمَا أَجْسَامُ الْعَالَمِ عَلَى الْإِطْلَاقِ إِلَّا أَنَّ الْبَحْتَ فِي الْهَيْئَةِ عَنْ أَشْكَالِهَا ، وَفِي السَّمَاءِ وَالْعَالَمِ عَنْ طَبَائِعِهَا فَهُمَا عِلْمَانِ مُخْتَلِفَانِ بِاخْتِلَافِ مَحْمُولَاتِ الْمَسَائِلِ مَعَ اتَّحَادِ الْمَوْضُوعِ وَعِلْمُ السَّمَاءِ وَالْعَالَمِ عِلْمٌ تُعْرَفْ فِيهِ أَحْوَالُ الْأَجْسَامِ الَّتِي هِيَ أَرْكَانُ الْعَالَمِ وَهِيَ السَّمَاوَاتُ وَمَا فِيهَا وَالْعَنَاصِرُ الْأرْبَعَهُ وَطَبَائِعُهَا وَحَرَكَاتُهَا وَمَوَاضِعُهَا وَتَعْريفُ الْحِكْمَةِ فِي صُنْعِهَا وَتَنْضِيدِهَا ، وَهُوَ مِنْ أَقْسَامِ الْعِلْمِ الطَّبِيعِيِّ الْبَاحِثِ عَنْ أَحْوَالِ الْأَجْسَامِ مِنْ حَيْثُ التَّغَيرِ وَمَوْضُوعُهُ الْجِسْمُ الْمَحْسُوسُ مِنْ حَيْثُ هُوَ مَعْرُوضٌ لِلتَّغَيْرِ فِي
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Al-Tarwīḥ li-Ḥall al-Tawḍīḥ wa al-Talwīḥ. One type of essential accident will be discussed in one science, and another type of essential accident in another science. 'Wa in urīd' is the answer to an implied question. Question: It is that, brother, your proof that sciences are distinguished by predicability is correct, but what should we do since the people have established a convention that sciences are distinguished by subject, not by predicate and essential accidents? Answer: The author said: Your convention is valid in its place, but the reality is that sciences can be distinguished by essential accidents just as they can be distinguished by subject. Externally, two sciences have a single subject. On the basis of their statement: He gave proof for the second claim. The claim was that externally two sciences have a single subject. The philosophers say: The subject of astronomy is the bodies of the universe in terms of shape—i.e., whatever bodies exist, spheres and elements, and what is composed from them, their shapes like triangle, square, etc. So astronomy is an independent discipline; its subject is the bodies of the universe in terms of shape. And natural science has several branches; one branch is the science of the heavens; its subject is also the bodies of the universe in terms of nature. Thus, astronomy's subject is the bodies of the universe, and the science of the heavens' subject is also the bodies of the universe. Two sciences, and the subject is one thing. Because in both sciences, discussion occurs from the same aspect. It is known that the aspect expresses essential accidents. And when the aspect is expressed, it is outside the subject. When the aspect is external, both sciences have one subject, namely the bodies of the universe. The remaining distinction among sciences occurs through essential accidents: in one science, discussion is about one type of essential accident, shapes; in the other science, about another type, nature. So distinction occurs according to this type. (And Allah knows best what is correct). Al-Talwīḥ. His statement: 'And among them is that the well-known'—the third topic concerning the permissibility of different sciences sharing a single subject essentially and consideratively. Just as he opposed the people regarding the permissibility of multiple subjects for one science, similarly he opposed them regarding the impossibility of a single subject for multiple sciences and claimed its permissibility, indeed its occurrence. As for the permissibility, it is because it is valid for one thing to have diverse essential accidents—i.e., differing in kind. In one science, some of their kinds are investigated, and in another science, other kinds, so the two sciences or the sciences are distinguished by the accidents investigated, even if the subject is one. And that is because the unity and diversity of a science is only in terms of the objects of knowledge, i.e., the issues. And just as issues become unified by the unity of their subjects in that all return to the subject of the science, and become diverse by their diversity, similarly they become unified by the unity of their predicates in that all return to a type of essential accident of the subject, and become diverse by their diversity. So just as the diversity of sciences is considered by the diversity of subjects, it is permissible to consider it by the diversity of predicates: one subject is taken essentially and consideratively, and the investigation of some of its essential accidents is made one science, and of the other part another science. Thus they are two sciences sharing in subject but distinguished in predicate. As for the occurrence, it is because they made the bodies of the universe, which are the simples, the subject of astronomy in terms of shape, and the subject of the science of the heavens and the world in terms of nature. And the 'ayn' in both is a statement of the essential accidents investigated—parts of the subject—otherwise the investigation of them in the two sciences would not occur. So the subject of each of them is the bodies of the universe absolutely, except that astronomy investigates their shapes, and the science of the heavens and the world investigates their natures. So they are two different sciences differing by the diversity of predicates of the issues despite the unity of subject. And the science of the heavens and the world is a science in which are known the states of the bodies that are the pillars of the world, i.e., the heavens and what is in them, the four elements, their natures, motions, positions, and the definition of the wisdom in their making and arrangement. It is a branch of natural science that investigates the states of bodies in terms of change, and its subject is the sensible body inasmuch as it is subject to change.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute in the classification of sciences (usul al-fiqh methodology). The author addresses the principle of how sciences are distinguished. The common view among some scholars is that sciences are distinguished solely by their subject matter (mawdu'). The author argues, however, that sciences can also be distinguished by the essential accidents (a'rad dhatiyya) they investigate, even if they share the same subject. He provides both rational proof (dalil aqli) and empirical example. The rational proof: a single thing can have multiple types of essential accidents; investigating different types yields different sciences. The example: astronomy ('ilm al-hay'a) studies celestial bodies in terms of shape, while the science of the heavens ('ilm al-sama' wa al-'alam) studies the same bodies in terms of nature. Thus both sciences share the subject 'bodies of the universe' but are differentiated by the predicates they examine. This passage defends the permissibility and actual occurrence of multiple sciences sharing one subject, countering those who insist on subject-based distinction alone.

Key Terms
عرض ذاتی ('arad dhatiyy): An essential accident that is predicated of a subject and serves to differentiate sciences even when the subject is the same.
موضوع (mawdu'): The subject matter of a science; what the science investigates primarily.
محمول (mahmul): Predicate; what is attributed to the subject in a proposition; here, it refers to the essential accidents investigated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinguishes astronomy from the science of the heavens (al-sama' wa al-'alam)?
A) Their subject matter is different
B) They investigate different essential accidents of the same subject
C) They use different methodologies
D) Their practitioners are different

Key Takeaway
Sciences can be distinguished by the essential accidents (predicates) they investigate, even when the subject is identical.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
12 min
Can One Thing Be the Subject of Multiple Sciences? The Hanafi Argument
Dispute on whether a single entity can be subject of multiple sciences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on a single subject for multiple sciences, explain the proof based on predicates, and apply the concept of haythiyya to distinguish between fiqh and usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Sciences are defined by their issues (masā’il), which can vary by predicate even if the subject is the same.

In this passage, the author addresses a fundamental question in the classification of sciences: can one entity be the subject of more than one science? He argues against the opposing view that insists on strict subject unity, using rational proof and empirical examples. You will learn how the Hanafi school uses the concepts of 'aspect' (haythiyya) and 'essential property' ('arad dhati) to allow multiple sciences to share a subject.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opposing positions
The author makes two claims: (1) permissibility (jawaz) and (2) actual occurrence (wuqu'). The opposing school (al-qawm) denies both, insisting that a single entity cannot be subject to multiple sciences.
2
Understand the proof for possibility
Sciences are differentiated by their issues (masā'il), and issues are differentiated by predicates (essential properties) even if the subject is the same. Just as different subjects yield different sciences, different predicates can also differentiate sciences.
The rational proof is based on the principle that unity/diversity of sciences follows unity/diversity of masā'il.
3
Examine the evidence for actual occurrence
Astronomy (hay'a) and physics (sama' wa 'alam) both study the bodies of the universe, but astronomy studies them from the aspect of shape, while physics studies them from the aspect of physical nature. This shows a single subject studied under different aspects.
The aspect (haythiyya) restricts the essential properties investigated.
4
Define the key term 'haythiyya'
Haythiyya is the perspective or aspect under which a subject is considered; it determines which essential properties are relevant for a given science.
In Hanafi usul, haythiyya allows a subject to be shared without conflating sciences.
5
Apply to Islamic sciences
For example, the act of prayer (salat) is the subject of fiqh (its rulings), usul al-fiqh (the evidence for its obligation), and kalam (the nature of divine commands). Each science investigates different essential properties of the same act.
This shows the practical importance of the principle for the classification of Islamic knowledge.

الأدويحُ لحل التوضيح والتلويج

الأحوال وَالثَّبَاتِ فِيهَا وَيُبْحَثُ فِيهِ عَمَّا يَعْرَضُ لَهُ مِنْ حَيْثُ هُوَ كَذَلِكَ كَذَا ذَكَرَهُ أَبُو عَنِيٍّ وَلَا يَخْفَى أَنَّ الْحَيْثِيَّةَ فِي الطَّبِيعِي مَبْحُوتٌ عَنْهَا وَقَدْ صَرَّحَ بِأَنَّهَا قيد لِلْعُرُوض. ترجمہ: ۔ تیسری بحث علوم مختلفہ کے نشارک کے جائز ہونے میں ہے ایک موضوع میں بالذات والا عتبار اور جیسے مخالفت کی قوم کی تعدد موضوع کے جواز میں ایک علم کیلئے اسی طرح مخالفت کی ان کی اتحاد موضوع کے ممتنع ہونے میں علوم متعددہ کیلئے اور دعوی کیا ان کے جائز ہونے کا بلکہ واقع ہونے کا۔ بہر حال جائز ہونا پس کیونکہ صحیح ہے یہ کہ ہوں ایک شئی کیلئے اعراض ذاتیہ متنوعہ یعنی نوع کے اعتبار سے مختلف بحث کی جائے ایک علم میں ان کی بعض انواع سے اور دوسرے علم میں بعض دوسرے انواں سے پس ممتاز ہوں گے دونوں علم یا کئی علوم مبحوث عنہا کے اعراض کے ساتھ اگر چہ موضوع متحد ہو اور یہ اس لئے ہے کہ کیونکہ علم کا متحد ہونا اور اس کا مختلف ہونا جزی نیست وہ معلومات یعنی مسائل کے اعتبار کے ساتھ ہوتا ہے اور جیسے متحد ہوتے ہیں مسائل موضوع کے متحد ہونے کے ساتھ بائیں صورت کہ لوٹیں تمام مسائل علم کے موضوع کی طرف اور مختلف ہوتے ہیں اس موضوع کے مختلف ہونے کے ساتھ اسی طرح متحد ہوتے ہیں وہ (مسائل) معمولات کے متحد ہونے کے ساتھ ہائیں صورت کہ لوٹیں وہ تمام موضوع کے اعراض ذاتیہ کی ایک نوع کی طرف اور مختلف ہوتے ہیں وہ (مسائل) ان (موضوعات) کے مختلف ہونے کے ساتھ پس جس طرح اعتبار کیا جاتا ہے علوم کے مختلف ہونے کا موضوعات کے مختلف ہونے کے ساتھ جائز ہے یہ کہ اعتبار کیا جائے محمولات کے مختلف ہونے کے ساتھ بائیں طور پر کہ لیا جائے ایک موضوع بالذات والاعتبار اور بنائی جائے بحث اس کے بعض اعراض ذاتیہ سے ایک علم اور بعض دوسرے اعراض ذاتیہ سے دوسرا علم پس ہوں گے دونوں علم مشترک موضوع میں اور ممتاز ہوں گے محمول کے ساتھ۔ اور بہر حال واقع ہونا کیونکہ بنایا ہے انہوں نے اجسام عالم کو اور وہ بسائط ہیں موضوع علم حیثیت کا شکل کی حیثیت سے اور علم سماء و العالم کا موضوع طبعیت کی حیثیت سے اور حیثیت ان دونوں میں مبحوث عنہا کے اعراض ذاتیہ کا بیان ہے موضوع کے اجزاء کیلئے وگرنہ نہ واقع ہوتی بحث اس سے دونوں علموں میں پس موضوع ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کا اجسام عالم ہے علی الاطلاق مگر بیٹک بحث علم بیت میں اس کی شکلوں سے ہے اور علم سماء والعالم میں ان کی طبیعتوں سے ہے۔ پس وہ دونوں علم مختلف ہیں محمولات کے مختلف ہونے کیسا تھ موضوع کے متحد ہونے کے با وجود اور علم السماء و العالم ایسا علم ہے کہ اس میں پہچانا جاتا ہے ان اجسام کے احوال کو جو عالم کے ارکان ہیں اور وہ آسمان ہیں اور جو آسمانوں میں ہے اور عناصر اربعہ ہیں ان کی طبیعتیں اور ان کے حرکات اور ان کی جگہیں ہیں اور پہچانا جاتا ہے حکمت کو ان
