کے بنانے میں اور تہہ بہہ رکھنے میں اور وہ (علم سماء) اس علم طبعی کی اقسام میں سے ہے جس میں بحث ہوتی ہے اجسام کے احوال سے تغیر کی حیثیت سے اور اس کا موضوع جسم محسوس ہے اس حیثیت ہے کہ وہ در پے ہے تغیر کے احوال میں اور اس میں ثابت رہنے میں اور بحث کی جاتی ہے اس میں اس چیز سے جو لاحق ہو اس کو اس حیثیت سے اسی طرح ذکر کیا ہے اس کو بوعلی نے اور نہیں ہے مخفی کہ بے شک حیثیت علم طبعی میں مجوث عنہا ہے اور تحقیق تصریح کی ہے کہ بے شک وہ (حیثیت) قید ہے اور عروض کی۔
مات کے دو دعوے
تشریح: قولہ منہا المشہور : شارع ماتن پر اعتراض کرتے ہیں کہ ماتن نے جس طرح علم واحد کے متعدد موضوع ہونے کے بارے میں قوم کی مخالفت کی تھی ایسے ہی اس تیسری بحث میں قوم کی مخالفت کی قوم کہتی ہے کہ شئی واحد ذاتا اور اعتبارادو علوم کا موضوع نہیں ہو سکتی لیکن مصنف نے کہاشئی واحد ذاتا و اعتبارا ایک سے زائد علوم کا موضوع ہوسکتی ہے بلکہ واقع ہے خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ دو دعوے ہو گئے (۱) ذاتا و اعتبار اشتئی واحد کا دو علموں کا موضوع بنا ممکن ہے (۲) خارج میں شئی واحد دو علوم کیلئے موضوع بن رہی ہے اور یہ واقع ہے۔
دعوی اول کی دلیل
اما الجواز : ۔ بے شارع نے پہلے دعوی کی دلیل کو واضح کیا ہے کہ ایسا ہوسکتا ہے کہ ئی واحد کیلئے عوارض ذاتیہ کی مختلف انواع ہوں ایک علم میں عوارض ذاتیہ کی ایک نوع سے بحث ہو اور دوسرے علم میں دوسری نوع سے بحث ہو اور ان میں امتیاز عوارض ذاتیہ کی وجہ سے ہو اور اس بات کی دلیل کہ علوم کا اتحاد و اختلاف مسائل کے اتحاد اور اختلاف پرمبنی ہے اگر مسائل مختلف ہوں تو علوم مختلف ہیں کیونکہ موضوع سے جیسے اختلاف علوم ثابت ہوتا ہے ایسے ہی محمول سے بھی اختلاف علوم ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ مسائل موضوع کی طرف راجع ہیں تو ایک علم ہے اسی طرح اگر تمام مسائل عوارض ذاتیہ کی ایک نوع کی طرف راجع ہوں تو بھی ایک علم ہوگا۔ دعوی ثانی کی دلیل
اما الوقوع سے دوسرے دعوی کی دلیل دی ہے کہ خارج میں شئی واحد ذاتا واعتبارا علوم کا موضوع بن رہی ہے حکماء نے تصریح کی ہے کہ علم ہیئت کا موضوع اجسام عالم من حیث الشکل نہیں اور علم السماء کا موضوع اجسام عالم من حیث الطبع ہیں ان دونوں علوم میں حیثیت بیان ہے عوارض ذاتیہ کیلئے کیونکہ ان میں نفس حیثیت سے بحث ہوتی ہے تو معلوم ہوا کہ حیثیت بیان
Al-Tarwīḥ li Ḥall al-Tawḍīḥ wa al-Talwīḥ. 412. The states and stability therein, and it investigates what occurs to it from the perspective that it is such. Thus Abū ‘Alī mentioned it, and it is not hidden that the aspect in physics is investigated, and he explicitly stated that it is a restriction for occurrence. Translation: The third inquiry is about the permissibility of multiple sciences sharing one subject in essence and consideration, and just as he opposed the people in the permissibility of multiple subjects for one science, similarly he opposed them in the impossibility of one subject for multiple sciences, and he claimed its permissibility, rather its occurrence. Anyway, permissibility is because it is correct that a single thing can have diverse essential properties, i.e., different by type; in one science some of its types are investigated, and in another science other types, so the two sciences or multiple sciences will be distinguished by the properties investigated, even if the subject is unified. And this is because the unity and diversity of a science is not by the essence; rather it is by the consideration of the information (masā’il). And just as the masā’il are unified by the unity of the subject, in the manner that all masā’il of the science refer to the subject, and differ by the difference of the subject, similarly they (the masā’il) are unified by the unity of the predicates, in the manner that they all refer to one type of essential properties of the subject, and they differ by the difference of those (predicates). So just as the difference of sciences is considered by the difference of subjects, it is permissible that it be considered by the difference of predicates, in the manner that one subject is taken in essence and consideration, and research is made from some of its essential properties in one science, and from other essential properties in another science; then the two sciences will share in subject and be distinguished by predicate. And anyway, occurrence is because they made the bodies of the universe – and they are simple – the subject of the science of astronomy by the aspect of shape, and the subject of the science of the heavens and the world by the aspect of nature, and the aspect in both is an expression of the essential properties that are investigated for the parts of the subject; otherwise research from it would not occur in both sciences. So the subject of each of them is the bodies of the universe absolutely, but research in astronomy is about their shapes, and in the science of the heavens and the world about their natures. So the two sciences are different by the difference of predicates despite the unity of subject. And the science of the heavens and the world is a science in which are known the states of those bodies that are the pillars of the universe – and they are the heavens, what is in the heavens, and the four elements – their natures, their motions, and their places, and wisdom is known in their construction and arrangement. And it (the science of the heavens) is among the divisions of natural science, which investigates the states of bodies from the aspect of change, and its subject is the sensible body in the aspect that it is subject to change in states and stability therein, and research is made in it about what occurs to it from that aspect. Thus Bu ‘Alī mentioned it, and it is not hidden that the aspect in physics is investigated, and he explicitly stated that it (the aspect) is a restriction for occurrence. The matn's two claims. Commentary: His statement 'among them the famous' – the commentator objects to the matn author that just as the matn author opposed the people regarding multiple subjects for one science, similarly in this third inquiry he opposed them: the people say that a single thing in essence and consideration cannot be the subject of two sciences, but the author said that a single thing in essence and consideration can be the subject of more than one science, rather it occurs. The summary is that two claims are made: (1) It is possible for a single thing in essence and consideration to be the subject of two sciences; (2) Externally, a single thing is becoming the subject for two sciences, and this is actual. Proof of the first claim: As for permissibility: the commentator clarified the proof of the first claim that it is possible for a single thing to have different types of essential properties; in one science research is from one type of essential properties, and in another science from another type, and distinction is by the essential properties. And the proof of that is that the unity and diversity of sciences is based on the unity and diversity of the masā’il; if the masā’il are different then the sciences are different, because just as the difference of sciences is established by the subject, similarly the difference of sciences is established by the predicate. If the masā’il refer to the subject, then it is one science; similarly if all masā’il refer to one type of essential properties, then also it is one science. Proof of the second claim: As for occurrence, he gave proof for the second claim that externally a single thing in essence and consideration is becoming the subject of sciences. The philosophers have explicitly stated that the subject of astronomy is the bodies of the universe from the aspect of shape, and the subject of the science of the heavens is the bodies of the universe from the aspect of nature. In both sciences the aspect is an expression of the essential properties, because research in them is from the aspect itself. So it is known that the aspect is expressive.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute about whether a single entity can serve as the subject (mawdu') for more than one science. The author of the matn (al-Tawdih) argues against the predominant view ('al-qawm', likely the mutakallimin) that a thing cannot be subject to multiple sciences due to unity of essence. The author makes two claims: (1) it is possible (jawaz) and (2) it actually occurs (wuqu'). The proof for possibility is based on the principle that sciences are differentiated by their masā'il (issues), and masā'il can be unified or differentiated by either the subject or the predicates (ahkam, i.e., the essential properties or 'awarid dhatiyya). Just as different subjects yield different sciences, different predicates (types of essential properties) can also differentiate sciences even if the subject is the same. The proof for actual occurrence is given by example: the science of astronomy (hay'a) studies the bodies of the universe from the aspect of shape, while the science of the heavens and the world (sama' wa 'alam) studies the same bodies from the aspect of physical nature. Both have the same subject in essence, but the aspects (haythiyyat) differ, leading to two distinct sciences. The commentator (sharih) clarifies that 'aspect' (haythiyya) is a restriction (qayd) for the properties investigated, and it is these properties that are the real differentiators. This dispute is important in usul al-fiqh because it relates to the classification of sciences and the boundaries of subject matters, which in turn affects how legal rulings are derived within each science.

Key Terms
حيثية (haythiyya): The aspect or perspective under which a subject is considered and which differentiates the essential properties investigated in a science.
عرض ذاتي (‘arad dhati): Essential property that inheres in a subject and is investigated by a particular science; by varying these, sciences can be distinguished.
علم (‘ilm): A body of knowledge or discipline, which in this context is defined by its subject (mawdu‘) and the essential properties it investigates.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the main criterion for differentiating sciences when the subject is the same?
A) The physical location of the subject
B) The different essential properties or predicates investigated
C) The time period of the study
D) The language used in the science

Key Takeaway
A single entity can be the subject of multiple sciences when considered under different aspects and investigating different essential properties.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
8 min
Refuting Objection on Multiple Divine Attributes
Refuting an objection regarding proof of multiple essential attributes of God

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that an accident attaching through an essential accident is itself essential and evaluate the objection that the rational proof only establishes one essential attribute.

Core Idea
Multiple divine attributes are essential; what attaches through an essential accident is itself essential.

In this passage from the commentary on Al-Tawdih, the author defends the proof of multiple essential attributes for God against an objection that claims the proof only establishes one. Using the principles of attachment through another and the nature of differences in attributes, the Hanafi position is upheld. This lesson will guide you through the objection, the response, and the underlying rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objection states that the proof only establishes one essential attribute, not multiple types. Understand why the opponent claims this.
The opponent argues that the proof's dilemma (part or other) only proves one attribute; for others, they must attach through that first attribute, making them derived or leading to multiplicity.
2
Trace the Hanafi response
The response introduces two rules: (1) any attribute attaching through an essential accident is itself essential; (2) when the locus is one, differences in attributes are specific (naw'ī), not personal (shakhsī).
Rule (1) preserves essentiality of all attributes; rule (2) avoids implying composition.
3
Apply the rules to the objection
If all attributes attach through the first essential attribute, they become essential. If they attach directly, multiplicity does not imply composition because of the specific difference rule.
The key is that when the locus (God) is one, differences like knowledge and power are specific types, not separate essences.
4
Examine the commentary on the matn phrase
The author clarifies that the two defects of infinite regress and istikmāl min al-ghair arise based on what 'ghair' refers to: a contradictory thing or another attribute.
This shows the proof covers all possibilities, confirming essential attributes.

Source Text

جواب دیا کہ غیر سے مراد عام ہے امر مبائین یا صفات تو اگر صفات صفات کے واسطہ سے لاحق ہوں تو مسلسل والی خرابی لازم آئیگی اور اگر امر مباین کے واسطہ سے لاحق ہوں تو استعمال من الغیر والی خرابی سے لازم آئیگی۔
It has been established: the summary is that for the One Real who has no partner, various types of essential accidents can be proven; then for another, a fortiori they can be proven. Objection: The author's proof does not mention the contradictory thing; he only said that these attributes will be attached through a part or through another, but did not mention the contradictory thing, whereas its mention was necessary because without it the proof is not a proof. Reply: The author's habit is to often use allusion. Briefly, although the author did not explicitly mention the contradictory thing, he mentioned it implicitly because in the proof he said that these attributes cannot attach through another; otherwise either using from another or infinite regress becomes necessary. Using from the signifier only becomes necessary when 'other' is a contradictory thing. Whatever is attached through an essential accident is itself an essential accident. So he said: He raised the objection and then answered it himself. Question: This proof does not prove multiple essential accidents for God; it proves one essential accident. If multiple are proven, then multiplicity of essential accidents is proven, but not different types, whereas the goal is to prove different types of accidents, and this is not proven. You said that some of God's attributes attach to God essentially because they cannot attach through a part or through another; so one essential accident is proven. Now we say that the remaining attributes attach through that essential accident, so they are in the same ruling as that means. And if we accept that all attributes attach essentially without means, then multiplicity is proven so that the accidents are of different types. Reply: The rule is that whatever attaches through an essential accident is itself an essential accident. Now you accept that one attribute is essential; the rest that attach through it will also be essential. As for the second alternative, the rule is that if the locus is one and the attributes differ, this difference is specific difference. For example, hearing, sight, and speech in Zayd are specific differences because the locus is one. In this case, there is no personal difference because if there were personal difference, the locus would differ, like whiteness found in Zayd and in Amr. That is personal difference. But here the locus, God, is one. If there were personal difference, it would necessitate plurality of locus, leading to negation of monotheism. So it is known that the attributes of God are not different in type. (And God knows best). Commentary: His statement 'wa lā nah mullazim istikmālah': In the matn, it is 'wa lā nah mullazim istikmālah'. The commentators explained the construction: This sentence is conjuncted to the content of the previous sentence, which is: if the attributes of God attach through another, then infinite regress becomes necessary, or else it is conjuncted to that content, and 'wa lā nah mullazim isti'mālah min ghairih' now means: if the attributes of God attach through another, then infinite regress becomes necessary or istikmāl min al-ghair becomes necessary. What is meant by 'ghair' in 'istikmāl min al-ghair'? And there is consideration: If they attach through another, two defects arise: infinite regress or isti'māl min al-ghair. Question: What is meant by 'isti'māl min al-ghair'? If by 'ghair' the contradictory thing is meant, then from a separate thing isti'māl min al-ghair occurs, and this is the case. But this is not necessary because it is possible that the establishment is due to another attribute. And if 'ghair' includes both, i.e., either a separate thing or another attribute, then in both cases isti'māl min al-ghair is not necessary because God's attributes are in need of one another, and this need and deficiency does not entail isti'māl min al-ghair, like creation depends on knowledge, and power depends on will, but no deficiency results from that. He replied that 'ghair' is general: either a contradictory thing or attributes. So if attributes attach through attributes, then the infinite regress defect arises; and if they attach through a contradictory thing, then the defect of isti'māl min al-ghair arises.
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage is a detailed theological-legal dispute within the commentary on Al-Tawdih. The author is defending the proof that multiple essential attributes (a'radh dhatiyyah) can be attributed to God without implying composition or need. The objection is that the matn's proof omits mention of the 'contradictory thing' (al-mubāyin). The reply explains that the proof implicitly covers it via the dilemma of regress or dependence. A further objection argues that the proof only establishes one essential attribute, not multiple types. The response introduces two rules: (1) any attribute attaching through an essential accident is itself essential, so multiplicity is preserved; (2) when the locus (mahall) is one, differences in attributes are specific (naw'ī), not personal (shakhsī), thus avoiding polytheism. The commentary then clarifies the phrase 'wa lā nah mullazim istikmālah' from the matn, explaining that the two defects—infinite regress and istikmāl min al-ghair (being perfected by another)—apply depending on whether 'ghair' means a contradictory thing or another attribute. The final answer is that 'ghair' is general, covering both cases. This discussion is purely rational (dalīl 'aqlī) and reflects Hanafi theological methodology within usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
عرض ذاتی (arad dhati): An accident that is essential to the subject, not acquired through an external cause.
استكمال من الغیر (istikmal min al-ghair): Being perfected by another, implying deficiency and dependence in the subject.
تسلسل (tasalsul): Infinite regress in causes, which is impossible for divine attributes.
امر مباین (amr mubayin): A contradictory or separate thing that is different in essence.
استعمال من الغیر (isti'mal min al-ghair): Using from another, implying dependence.
نوعی (naw'i): Specific difference, a difference in kind within a single locus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consequence if attributes attach through another attribute?
A) Infinite regress
B) Istikmal min al-ghair
C) Their being non-essential
D) The unity of essence is compromised

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position on multiple divine attributes is rationally defensible using the rules of attachment through essential accidents and the nature of specific differences.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
The Basmalah: Hanafi vs Shafi'i on its Quranic Status
Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on basmalah with practical implications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the later Hanafi position on the basmalah, compare it with the Shafi'i view, and apply the concept of shubhah to derive practical rulings.

Core Idea
The basmalah is one Quranic verse repeated for separation; Shafi'is count it as 113 separate verses.

The status of the basmalah—'Bismillahir Rahmanir Rahim' at the start of surahs—is a classic ikhtilaf between Hanafis and Shafi'is. This lesson traces the Hanafi position from the early view to the later relied-upon view, and explains how the concept of shubhah (doubt) affects rulings like takfir and recitation by a junub.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two Hanafi positions
Distinguish between the early view (not Quranic except in Surah an-Naml) and the later view (a single separate Quranic verse).
The early view is recorded in books of the mutaqaddimun; the later view is the mufta bihi.
2
Understand the later Hanafi proof
The evidence: the basmalah was written in the mushafs in Quranic script without rejection by the Salaf, and it was revealed for separation between surahs.
This proof is based on ijma' of the Salaf by practice.
3
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
Shafi'is consider each basmalah at the start of every surah (except al-Tawbah) as a full verse belonging to that surah, totaling 113 verses.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the verse count.
4
Apply the concept of shubhah
See how doubt (shubhah) prevents takfir of someone who denies its Quranic status outside an-Naml, and allows a junub to recite it with intention of blessing.
Shubhah is a key usul principle in Hanafi thought.
5
Note the practical thamarah
The difference in verse count (1 vs 113) and the permissibility of recitation by junub with intention of blessing.
Prayer with basmalah alone is not valid due to shubhah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا التَّسْمِيَّةُ فَالْمَشْهُورُ مِنْ مَذْهَبِ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ عَلَى مَا ذُكِرَ فِي كَثِيرٍ مِنْ كُتُبِ الْمُتَقَدِّمِينَ أَنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ إِلَّا مَا تَوَاتَرَ بَعْضُ آيَةٍ مِنْ سُورَةِ النَّمْلِ ، وَإِنَّ قَوْلَهُمْ بِلَا شُبُهَةٍ احْتِرَازُ عَنْهَا إِلَّا أَنَّ الْمُتَأَخْرِينَ ذَهَبُوا إِلَى أَنَّ الصَّحِيحَ مِنَ الْمَذْهَبِ أَنَّهَا فِي أَوَائِلِ السُّوَرِ آيَةٌ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ أُنْزِلَتْ لِلْفَصْلِ بَيْنَ السُّوَرِ بِدَلِيلِ أَنَّهَا كُتِبَتْ فِي الْمَصَاحِفِ بِخَطِّ الْقُرْآنِ مِنْ غَيْرِ إِنْكَارٍ مِنْ السَّلَفِ وَعَدَمُ جَوَازِ الصَّلاةِ بِهَا إِنَّمَا هُوَ لِلشُّبُهَةِ فِي كَوْنِهَا آيَةً تَامَّةً وَجَوَازُ تِلَاوَتِهَا لِلْجُنُبِ وَالْحَائِضِ إِنَّمَا هُوَ عَلَى قَصْدِ التَّبَرُّكِ وَالتَّيَمُّنِ كَمَا إِذَا قَالَ الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ عَلَى قَصْدِ الشُّكرِ دُونَ السّلاوَةِ وَعَدَمُ تَكْفِيرِ مَنْ أَنْكَرَ كَونَهَا مِنْ الْقُرْآنِ فِي غَيْرِ سُورَةِ النَّمْلِ إِنَّمَا هُوَ لِقُوَّةِ الشُّبُهَةِ فِي ذَلِكَ بِحَيْثُ يَخْرُجُ كَوْنُهَا مِنْ الْقُرْآنِ مِنْ حَيْزِ الْوُضُوحِ إِلَى حَيْزِ الْإِشْكَالِ ، وَمِثْلُ هَذَا يَمْنَعُ التَّكْفِيرَ ، فَإِنْ قِيلَ فَعَلَى مَا اخْتَارَهُ الْمُتَأَخِّرُونَ هَلْ يَبْقَى اخْتِلَاتٌ بَيْنَ الْفَرِيقَيْنِ قُلْنَا نَعَمُ هِيَ عِنْدَ الشَّافِعِيَّةِ مِائَةٌ وَثَلَاثَ عَشْرَةَ آيَةٌ مِنْ السُّوَرِ كَمَا أَنَّ قَوْله تَعَالَى ) فَبِأَيِّ آلَاء رَبِّكُمَا تُكَذِّبَانِ ) عِدَّةُ آيَاتٍ مِنْ سُورَةِ الرَّحْمَنِ وَعِنْدَ الْحَنَفِيَّةِ آيَةٌ وَاحِدَةٌ مِنْ الْقُرْآنِ كُرِّرَتْ لِلْفَصْلِ وَالتَّبَرُّكِ وَلَيْسَتْ بِآيَةٍ مِنْ شَيْءٍ مِنْ السُّوَرِ وَجَازَ تَكْرِيرُهَا فِي أَوَائِلِ السُّوَرِ لِأَنَّهَا نَزَلَتْ لِذَلِكَ وَنُقِلَتْ كَذَلِكَ بِخِلَافِ مَنْ أَخَذَ يُلْحِقُ بِالْمُصْحَفِ آيَاتٍ مُكَرَّرَةً مِثْلَ أَنْ يُكتَبَ فِي أَوَّلِ كُلِّ سُورَةِ الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ فَإِنَّهُ يُعَدُّ زِنْدِيقًا أَوْ مَجْنُونًا
As for the basmalah, the well-known [position] from the madhhab of Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) according to what is mentioned in many books of the early scholars is that it is not part of the Quran except what is transmitted by tawatur [i.e., a part of a verse] from Surah an-Naml. And indeed their statement 'without doubt' is a precaution against it. Except that the later scholars went to the position that the correct [view] in the madhhab is that it is, at the beginnings of surahs, a verse from the Quran revealed for separation between surahs, evidenced by the fact that it was written in the mushafs in the script of the Quran without rejection from the Salaf. And the impermissibility of prayer with it is only due to doubt about it being a complete verse. And the permissibility of its recitation by the junub and menstruating woman is only with the intention of seeking blessing and auspiciousness, just as if one says 'Alhamdulillahi Rabbil 'Alamin' with the intention of thanks, not recitation. And the non-takfir of someone who denies it being from the Quran other than in Surah an-Naml is only due to the strength of doubt in that matter, such that its being from the Quran moves from the realm of clarity to the realm of ambiguity. And such prevents takfir. If it is said: According to what the later scholars chose, does the disagreement between the two groups remain? We say: Yes. According to the Shafi'is, it is one hundred and thirteen verses from the surahs, just as the saying of Allah (فَبِأَيِّ آلَاء رَبِّكُمَا تُكَذِّبَانِ) is counted as verses from Surah ar-Rahman. And according to the Hanafis, it is one single verse from the Quran repeated for separation and blessing, and it is not a verse from any of the surahs. And its repetition at the beginnings of surahs is permissible because it was revealed for that and transmitted so, unlike someone who adds repeated verses to the mushaf, such as writing 'Alhamdulillahi Rabbil 'Alamin' at the beginning of every surah, for he would be considered a heretic or insane.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage addresses the status of the basmalah ('Bismillahir Rahmanir Rahim') in the Quran. According to the early Hanafi position, the basmalah is not part of the Quran except for the one in Surah an-Naml (27:30), which is a part of a verse. However, later Hanafi scholars (mutakkhirin) adopted the view that the basmalah at the beginning of each surah is an independent Quranic verse revealed for the purpose of separating surahs. This is supported by its writing in the mushafs without objection. The dispute with the Shafi'is is that Shafi'is consider each basmalah at the start of every surah (except Surah at-Tawbah) to be a full verse that is part of that surah, totaling 113 verses. Hanafis count only one basmalah as a separate verse repeated for separation. The passage also explains related rulings: prayer is not valid with basmalah alone due to doubt about it being a complete verse; a junub may recite it with the intention of blessing; and one who denies its Quranic status in other surahs is not declared a disbeliever due to the ambiguity.

Key Terms
التسمية (al-tasmiyah): The phrase 'Bismillahir Rahmanir Rahim' (the basmalah)
الشبهة (al-shubhah): Doubt or ambiguity that prevents a ruling such as takfir or prohibition of recitation by junub
المتقدمون والمتأخرون (al-mutaqaddimun wa al-muta'akhkhirun): Early and later scholars of the Hanafi madhhab; later scholars revised the position on the basmalah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later Hanafi position, why is the basmalah at the beginning of surahs not considered a verse of that surah?
A) Because it is not written in the mushaf
B) Because it was revealed for separation between surahs and is a separate verse
C) Because the early Hanafis denied it completely
D) Because it is a hadith and not Quran

Key Takeaway
The later Hanafi position affirms the basmalah as a single Quranic verse for separation; the shubhah surrounding its completeness prevents takfir and allows recitation by junub with intention of blessing.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

The Basmalah: Intra-Hanafi Debate and Inter-Madhhab Implications
Analyzing the basmalah dispute: intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on the basmalah, evaluate the proofs for each, and explain the practical consequences of the disagreement with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
The basmalah's Quranic status is disputed within the Hanafi school and between madhahib—the later Hanafi view affirms it as one repeated verse.

This passage from the commentary on al-Tawozih wa al-Talweeh examines a celebrated usul dispute: whether the basmalah at the beginning of each surah is a Quranic verse. It first presents the early Hanafi position that it is not part of the Quran, then the later Hanafi correction, and finally contrasts the Hanafi and Shafi'i counts of Quranic verses. Understanding this dispute clarifies how transmission (tawatur vs. ahad), scriptural writing (rasm al-mushaf), and prophetic statements (munazzal min Allah) interact in usul al-fiqh to determine the status of a text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two Hanafi positions
Recognize that the early Hanafis (mutaqaddimin) held the basmalah at surah beginnings is not Quranic, while the later Hanafis (muta'akhkhirin) adopted the view that it is one Quranic verse repeated for separation.
The 'mashhur' view is the early one; the 'sahih' view is the later one.
2
Examine the proofs for the later view
Analyze the two proofs: (1) the basmalah is written in the Quranic script without Salaf objection, and (2) the Prophet said it is 'sent down from Allah' (hadith ahad).
Both proofs are zanni in thubut and dalala.
3
Analyze the Hanafi responses to objections
Understand why prayer with only basmalah is invalid (doubt about completeness), why junub can recite it (intention of blessing), and why a denier is not takfired (strong doubt).
These responses protect the integrity of the madhhab.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i position
Shafi'is hold each occurrence of basmalah at surah beginnings is a separate verse, totaling 113 verses. Hanafis consider it one verse repeated.
The disagreement is about the nature of repetition and Quranic count.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: the total number of Quranic verses differs between the schools, and the ruling on reciting basmalah in prayer (though both allow it, the reasoning differs).
This affects tawatur status and takfir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصَّلاةِ بِهَا إِنَّمَا هُوَ لِلشُّبُهَةِ فِي كَوْنِهَا آيَةً تَامَّةً وَجَوَازُ تِلَاوَتِهَا لِلْجُنُبِ وَالْحَائِضِ إِنَّمَا هُوَ عَلَى قَصْدِ التَّبَرُّكِ وَالتَّيَمُّنِ كَمَا إِذَا قَالَ الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ عَلَى قَصْدِ الشُّكرِ دُونَ السّلاوَةِ وَعَدَمُ تَكْفِيرِ مَنْ أَنْكَرَ كَونَهَا مِنْ الْقُرْآنِ فِي غَيْرِ سُورَةِ النَّمْلِ إِنَّمَا هُوَ لِقُوَّةِ الشُّبُهَةِ فِي ذَلِكَ بِحَيْثُ يَخْرُجُ كَوْنُهَا مِنْ الْقُرْآنِ مِنْ حَيْزِ الْوُضُوحِ إِلَى حَيْزِ الْإِشْكَالِ ، وَمِثْلُ هَذَا يَمْنَعُ التَّكْفِيرَ ، فَإِنْ قِيلَ فَعَلَى مَا اخْتَارَهُ الْمُتَأَخِّرُونَ هَلْ يَبْقَى اخْتِلَاتٌ بَيْنَ الْفَرِيقَيْنِ قُلْنَا نَعَمُ هِيَ عِنْدَ الشَّافِعِيَّةِ مِائَةٌ وَثَلَاثَ عَشْرَةَ آيَةٌ مِنْ السُّوَرِ كَمَا أَنَّ قَوْله تَعَالَى ) فَبِأَيِّ آلَاء رَبِّكُمَا تُكَذِّبَانِ ) عِدَّةُ آيَاتٍ مِنْ سُورَةِ الرَّحْمَنِ وَعِنْدَ الْحَنَفِيَّةِ آيَةٌ وَاحِدَةٌ مِنْ الْقُرْآنِ كُرِّرَتْ لِلْفَصْلِ وَالتَّبَرُّكِ وَلَيْسَتْ بِآيَةٍ مِنْ شَيْءٍ مِنْ السُّوَرِ وَجَازَ تَكْرِيرُهَا فِي أَوَائِلِ السُّوَرِ لِأَنَّهَا نَزَلَتْ لِذَلِكَ وَنُقِلَتْ كَذَلِكَ بِخِلَافِ مَنْ أَخَذَ يُلْحِقُ بِالْمُصْحَفِ آيَاتٍ مُكَرَّرَةً مِثْلَ أَنْ يُكتَبَ فِي أَوَّلِ كُلِّ سُورَةِ الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ فَإِنَّهُ يُعَدُّ زِنْدِيقًا أَوْ مَجْنُونًا

ترجمہ: اور بہر حال تسمیہ پس مشہور امام ابوحنیفہ کے مذہب میں سے اس کے مطابق جس کو ذکر کیا اکثر متقدمین نے کہ بیشک وہ نہیں ہے قرآن میں سے مگر وہ جو تواتر سے منقول ہے بعض آیت سورۃ نمل کی اور بے شک ان کا قول بلا شصتہ احتراز ہے اس سے مگر بیشک متاخرین چلے گئے ہیں اس بات کی طرف کہ بیشک صحیح مذہب یہ ہے کہ سورتوں کے شروع میں بسم اللہ قرآن کی آیت ہے نازل کی گئی ہے سورتوں کے درمیان فاصلہ کیلئے اس دلیل کے ساتھ کہ بے شک اسے لکھا گیا ہے مصاحف میں خط قرآنی کے ساتھ بغیر کسی انکار کے سلف کی طرف سے اور نماز کا جائز نہ ہونا اس کے ساتھ جز این نیست وہ شبہ کی وجہ سے ہے اس کے آیت تامہ ہونے میں اور اس کی تلاوت کا جائز ہونا جنبی اور حائضہ کیلئے جز این نیست وہ میمن اور برکت حاصل کرنے کے ارادہ پر ہے جیسا کہ جب وہ کہے الحمد اللہ رب العالمین شکر کے ارادہ پر نہ کہ تلاوت کے ارادہ پر اور تکفیر نہ کر نا اس کی جوانکار کرے اس کے قرآن میں سے ہونے کا سورۃ نمل کے غیر میں جز این نیست وہ اس میں شبہ کی قوت کی وجہ سے ہے اس حیثیت سے کے اس کا ہونا قرآن میں سے حیز وضوح سے خیز اشکال کی طرف ہے اور اس کی مثل مانع ہے تکفیر سے پس اگر اعتراض کیا جائے کہ اس مذہب پر جس کو اختیار کیا ہے متاخرین نے کیا باقی رہ جاتا ہے اختلاف دونوں جماعتوں کے درمیان

(احناف و شوافع ) ہم کہتے ہیں جی ہاں شافعیہ کے ہاں ایک سو تیرہ آیات ہیں سورتوں میں سے جیسا کہ اس کا قول فبای آلاء ربکما تکذبان کئی آیات ہیں سورت رحمان کی اور حنفیہ کے ہاں قرآن میں سے ایک آیت ہے تکرار کیا گیا فا صلے اور برکت کیلئے اور نہیں ہے یہ کوئی آیت سورتوں میں سے کسی سورۃ کی اور جائز ہے اس کا تکرار سورتوں کی ابتداء میں کیونکہ یہ نازل ہوئی اس مقصد کیلئے اور نقل کی گئی ہے اسی طرح بخلاف اس شخص کے جو شروع کر دے لاحق کرنا مصحف کے ساتھ آیات کو کر ر مثلا ۔ یہ کہ لکھدے وہ ہر سورۃ کی ابتداء میں الحمد اللہ رب العالمین بیشک اسے شمار کیا جائے گا زندیق یا مجنون ۔
متاخرین کے ہاں تسمیہ امام اعظم کے ہاں قرآن کا جزء ہے
اما تسمیہ :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے اس عبارت میں شاریخ نے بسم اللہ کا مسئلہ بیان کیا ہے ایک بسم اللہ سورہ نمل کی آیت کا ایک حصہ ہے وہ بالا تفاق قرآن کا جزو ہے کیونکہ وہ تواتر سے منقول ہے اور جو سورتوں کے شروع میں بسم اللہ ذکر کی کتی ہے یہ قرآن کا جز ہے یا نہیں امام ابو حنیفہ کے علاوہ تمام کے ہاں یہ قرآن کا جز ہے اور امام صاحب کے دو قول ہیں۔ (۱) مشہور قول یہ ہے کہ یہ جز نہیں ہے اور یہی متقدمین احناف کہتے ہیں۔
(۲) قول غیر مشہور لیکن صحیح قول یہ ہے کہ قرآن کا جز ہے اور یہی متاخرین کہتے ہیں اور اس صحیح قول کے دو دلائل ہیں ۔ دلیل اول: بسم اللہ کوقرآن کے خط میں لکھا گیا ہے اور سلف نے اس پر کوئی اعتراض نہیں کیا حالانکہ سلف کی کوشش ہوتی تھی کہ پوری طرح غیر قرآن کو قرآن سے جدا کیا جائے حتی کہ وہ سورتوں کے نام بھی حاشیہ پر لکھتے تھے۔ دلیل ثانی:۔ متاخرین کی دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بسم اللہ کے بارہ میں فرمایا کہ یہ منزل من اللہ ہے تو گویا منزل على الرسول مع ہوئی لہذا یہ قرآن ہے۔
متاخرین کے قول پر اعتراضات اور ان کے جوابات
متاخرین جو کہتے ہیں کہ امام صاحب کا صحیح مذہب یہ ہے کہ بسم اللہ قرآن کا جز ہے اس پر کئی اعتراضات ہوتے ہیں اعتراض اول: جب امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک بسم اللہ کتاب کا جز ہے تو پھر اس کی تلاوت سے نماز ہو جانی چاہئے حالانکہ کوئی آدمی نماز میں صرف بسم اللہ پڑھے تو امام صاحب کے ہاں اس کی نماز نہیں ہوتی جب کہ ایک آیت کے پڑھنے سے بھی نماز ہو جاتی ہے تو یہ بھی ایک آیت ہے اس سے بھی نماز صحیح ہونی چاہیے۔
جواب:۔ امام صاحب نے جو کہا کہ نماز نہیں ہوتی یہ شک کی وجہ سے کہا کہ یہ پوری آیت ہے یا بعض آیت ہے یعنی مکمل
Prayer with it is only due to doubt about it being a complete verse. And its recitation being permissible for the junub and menstruating woman is only with the intention of seeking blessing and auspiciousness, as when one says 'Alhamdu lillahi rabbil 'alamin' with the intention of thanks, not recitation. And not declaring a disbeliever one who denies it being from the Quran outside Surah an-Naml is only due to the strength of doubt in that, such that its being from the Quran moves from clarity to ambiguity. And the likes of this prevent takfir. If it is said: According to what the later scholars chose, does disagreement remain between the two groups? We say: Yes. For the Shafi'is, it is one hundred and thirteen verses from the surahs, just as His statement 'Which of the favors of your Lord will you deny?' is several verses from Surah ar-Rahman. For the Hanafis, it is one verse from the Quran, repeated for separation and blessing, and not a verse from any of the surahs. Its repetition at the beginnings of surahs is permissible because it was revealed for that and transmitted thus, contrary to one who takes to appending repeated verses to the mushaf, like writing 'Alhamdu lillahi rabbil 'alamin' at the beginning of every surah; he would be considered a heretic or mad.

Translation: And in any case, regarding the basmalah, according to the well-known school of Imam Abu Hanifa, as mentioned by most of the early scholars, it is not from the Quran except that which is transmitted by tawatur, a part of the verse in Surah an-Naml. And indeed their statement 'without exception' is a precaution against that. But indeed the later scholars have moved to the view that the correct school is that basmalah at the beginnings of surahs is a Quranic verse, revealed for separation between surahs, with the proof that it is written in the mushafs in Quranic script without any rejection from the Salaf. And the prayer not being valid with it is only due to doubt about it being a complete verse. And its recitation being permissible for the junub and menstruating woman is only with the intention of seeking blessing and auspiciousness, as when one says 'Alhamdu lillahi rabbil 'alamin' with the intention of thanks, not recitation. And not declaring a disbeliever one who denies it being from the Quran outside Surah an-Naml is only due to the strength of the doubt in that, such that its being from the Quran moves from clarity to ambiguity. And the likes of this prevent takfir. Then if it is objected: According to this school which the later scholars have chosen, does the disagreement remain between the two groups (Hanafis and Shafi'is)? We say: Yes. For the Shafi'is, there are one hundred and thirteen verses from the surahs, as His statement 'Which of the favors of your Lord will you deny?' is several verses from Surah ar-Rahman. For the Hanafis, it is one verse from the Quran, repeated for separation and blessing, and it is not a verse from any surah. Its repetition at the beginnings of surahs is permissible because it was revealed for that and transmitted thus, contrary to one who takes to appending repeated verses to the mushaf, for example, writing 'Alhamdu lillahi rabbil 'alamin' at the beginning of every surah; indeed he would be considered a heretic or mad.

[Urdu Commentary] According to the later scholars, the basmalah is part of the Quran according to Imam A'zam.

As for the basmalah: This is the third part of the commentary's text. In this passage, the commentator has explained the issue of the basmalah. One basmalah is part of the verse in Surah an-Naml; it is by consensus part of the Quran because it is transmitted by tawatur. As for the basmalah mentioned at the beginnings of surahs, is it part of the Quran or not? According to all except Imam Abu Hanifa, it is part of the Quran. And Imam Sahib has two sayings: (1) the well-known saying is that it is not part, and that is what the early Hanafis say. (2) The lesser-known but correct saying is that it is part of the Quran, and that is what the later scholars say. And for this correct saying, there are two proofs: First proof: The basmalah is written in the script of the Quran, and the Salaf did not object to this, even though the Salaf made an effort to completely separate non-Quran from the Quran, to the extent that they would write the names of surahs on the margins. Second proof: The later scholars' second proof is that the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم said about the basmalah that it is 'munazzal min Allah', so it is revealed to the Messenger, hence it is Quran.

Objections to the later scholars' saying and their answers:
There are several objections to what the later scholars say, that Imam Sahib's correct school is that the basmalah is part of the Quran. First objection: When according to Imam Abu Hanifa the basmalah is part of the Book, then reciting it should suffice for prayer, but if a person recites only the basmalah in prayer, then according to Imam Sahib his prayer is not valid, whereas reciting one verse makes the prayer valid. So this is also one verse; the prayer should be valid with it.
Answer: What Imam Sahib said that the prayer is not valid is due to doubt: whether it is a complete verse or a part of a verse, i.e., incomplete.
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage is a detailed inter-madhhab and intra-madhhab dispute regarding the status of the basmalah ('Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim') at the beginning of Quranic surahs. The discussion centers on whether this basmalah is a verse of the Quran itself or merely a phrase for separation and blessing. The author first presents the position of the early Hanafis (mutaqaddimin), associated with Imam Abu Hanifa's well-known view, that the basmalah at the start of surahs is not part of the Quran; only the basmalah within Surah an-Naml is a Quranic verse by tawatur. Then he presents the later Hanafi view (muta'akhkhirin) that it is indeed a Quranic verse, revealed for separation between surahs, and he offers two proofs: (1) it is written in the Quranic script in the mushaf without any objection from the Salaf, and (2) the Prophet (peace be upon him) said it is 'sent down from Allah' (munazzal min Allah), implying it is part of revelation. The author then addresses practical consequences: why prayer with only the basmalah is not valid (due to doubt whether it is a complete verse), why it is permissible for a junub or menstruating woman to recite it with the intention of blessing, and why one who denies it being Quran outside Surah an-Naml is not declared a disbeliever (due to the strength of the doubt). He then clarifies that even with the later Hanafi view, disagreement remains with the Shafi'is because the Shafi'is consider each occurrence of the basmalah at the beginning of a surah (113 occurrences) as a separate verse, while the Hanafis consider it one verse repeated for separation. The passage also rejects the analogy of writing 'Alhamdu lillahi rabbil 'alamin' at the start of every surah, which would be innovation, because the basmalah is specifically revealed for that purpose. The Urdu commentary further explains the two sayings of Imam Abu Hanifa, presents the two proofs, and then raises the objection about prayer validity with the basmalah, giving the answer that the doubt is whether it is a complete verse or a part of a verse, so it does not qualify as the required recitation in prayer.

Key Terms
تسمیہ (tasmiah): The phrase 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' at the beginning of surahs, whose Quranic status is disputed.
مشہور (mashhur): The well-known (but not necessarily correct) view within the Hanafi school, attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa by the early scholars, that basmalah is not part of the Quran.
شُبْهَة (shubha): Doubt that prevents a ruling from being applied with certainty, used here to avoid takfir and to explain prayer invalidity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later Hanafis (muta'akhkhirin), how many Quranic verses does the basmalah constitute?
A) It is not a Quranic verse at all.
B) It is one Quranic verse repeated for separation and blessing.
C) It is 113 separate verses, one for each surah.
D) It is a complete verse in each surah except Surah an-Naml.

Key Takeaway
The basmalah's Quranic status involves an intra-Hanafi dispute (early vs later) and an inter-madhhab difference (Hanafi vs Shafi'i), with practical consequences for prayer validity, takfir, and Quranic verse count.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
8 min
Circularity in Defining the Quran: A Hanafi Usul Analysis
Commentator refutes attempts to avoid circularity in defining the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the circularity in the definition of the Quran and evaluate the Hanafi position that the circle is broken only by treating the definition as non-real (ghayr haqiqi) for distinction.

Core Idea
The definition of the Quran as 'transmitted to us' creates circularity unless it is intended for identification only, not essence.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, definitions must avoid logical circularity (dawr). The standard definition of the Quran — 'that which has been transmitted to us in tawatur, written in the mashaf, beginning with al-Fatiha and ending with al-Nas' — seems to depend on the term 'mushaf', whose definition in turn depends on 'Quran'. This lesson walks through the commentator's rigorous analysis of why several attempts to break this circle fail, and the only solution: recognizing the definition as non-essential (for tamyiz only).

Guided Path
1
Recognize the circularity problem
Understand that if we define the Quran by reference to the mushaf, and the mushaf by reference to the Quran, we have a logical circle. The commentator calls this 'dawr' and considers it a defect if the definition is meant to capture the essence (mahiyya).
The key is the concept of dependency (tawaquf): A depends on B, and B depends on A.
2
Distinguish real (haqiqi) vs. non-real (ghayr haqiqi) definitions
A real definition requires knowledge of all parts; a non-real definition (for distinction only) does not. The commentator argues that the definition in question is intended as real, hence the circle is problematic.
Hanafi usul distinguishes between ta'rif haqiqi (essential) and ta'rif ghayr haqiqi (non-essential, e.g., tamyizi).
3
Analyze the attempts to break the circle
The passage presents three attempts: (a) distinguishing 'Quran' from 'Book' (identical), (b) defining mushaf as 'collection of pages', (c) defining mushaf as 'that which contains recited revelation'. The commentator refutes each.
Each attempt fails because it either changes the subject (to metaphorical) or the proposed alternative is synonymous with the Quran.
4
Apply the commentator's reasoning to reject each attempt
For (a): Quran and Book are identical in essence. For (b): literal wad' is not the intended usage; it turns from apparent to hidden. For (c): recited revelation (wahy matlu) is identical to Quran. Thus the circle remains.
The commentator insists that unless the definition is explicitly for distinction, the circle is inevitable.
5
Conclude that only a non-essential definition avoids circularity
If the definition is taken as non-real (for tamyiz), then knowledge of all parts is not required; understanding 'mushaf' via custom or indication suffices, breaking the dependency. This is the commentator's final resolution.
This shows the importance of intention in usul definitions: whether one aims to define essence or merely identify.

لازم آئیگا دور نہ اعتراض کیا جائے کہ دور جزی نیست کہ لازم آتا ہے جب بنایا جائے تعریف ماہیت قرآن کی نہ کہ ماہیت کتاب کی کیونکہ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ ماہیت کتاب وہی بعینہ ماہیت قرآن ہے بوجہ اس کے جو گذرا ہے کہ وہ دونوں نام ہیں ایک ہی شئی کے۔ پس موقوف ہونا مصحف کا ماہیت قرآن پر وہ بعینہ اس کا موقوف ہوتا ہے ماہیت کتاب پر ۔ اور اس کے ساتھ تو ظاہر ہو گیا کہ بیشک مصحف کی تفسیر ما جمع فی الوحی المحملو کے ساتھ نہیں دفع کرتی دور کو کیونکہ وہ بھی مترادف ہے کتاب اور قرآن کے پس مصنف نے تصریح کی ہے اس بات کی کہ وہ نہیں ہے تعریف ماہیت کی برابر ہے کہ تعریف کی ہو کتاب کی یا قرآن کی یہ اشارہ ہے اس بات کی طرف کہ بیشک نہیں ہے فرق دور کے لازم آنے میں دونوں صورتوں میں ۔ پھر کہا کہ جز این نیست کہ لازم آتا ہے دور اگر مرا دلیا جائے ماہیت قرآن کی تعریف یہ اشارہ ہے اس بات کی طرف کہ ماہیت کتاب ہی وہ ماہیت قرآن ہے پس ذکر ان دونوں میں سے ایک کا بے پرواہ کرنے والا ہے دوسرے سے پس اگر اعتراض کیا جائے کہ (دفع دور کیلئے ) تفسیر کر دی جائے مصحف کی ماجمع فیہ الصحائف کے ساتھ ہے ( مصحف وہ ہے جس میں صحائف کو جمع کیا جائے مطلقا ) بناء کرتے ہوئے اس پر کہ یہ موضوع لغوی ہے اور نکل جائیگا منسوخ استلاوۃ تعریف سے تواتر کی قید کے ساتھ پس کوئی دور لازم نہیں آتا ۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ عدول کرنا ہے ظاہر سے مخفی کی طرف اور حقیقت سے مجاز عرفی کی طرف پس نہیں ہے حسن تعریفات میں ۔ پس اگر اعتراض کیا جائے کہ اصولی کی تعریف جز این نیست کہ وہ اس مفہوم کلی کی ہے جو صادق آتا ہے مجموعہ پر اور ہر بعض پر اور مصحف کی معرفت جز این نیست کہ وہ موقوف ہے قرآن بمعنی مجموع شخصی پر اور وہ معلوم محفوظ ہے لوگوں کے درمیان وہ اس کو یاد کرتے ہیں اور اس کو پڑھتے ہیں اور نہیں ہے وہ ( قرآن ) لوگوں پر مشتبہ پس کوئی دور نہیں ہے۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ اگر تسلیم کر لیا جائے مجموع شخصی کی معرفت کو اپنی حقیقت کے ساتھ مفہوم کلی کی معرفت کے بغیر پس بنیاد مصنف کے کلام کی اس پر ہے کہ بیشک تعریف مجموع شخصی کی ہے نہ کہ مفہوم کلی کی۔
اگر قرآن کی یہ تعریف ماعدا سے امتیاز کے لئے ہو تو دور لازم نہیں آئے گا تشریح : قوله فان اتمام الجواب:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے اس میں شارع نے متن کی وضاحت کی ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ مانقل الینا الخ یہ تعریف قرآن کی اگر غیر حقیقی ہو یعنی ماہیت قرآن کی نہ ہو بلکہ قرآن کو صرف ماعدا سے جدا کرنے کیلئے تعریف کی گئی ہو تو پھر دور لازم نہیں آئیگا کیونکہ تعریف حقیقی کے تمام اجزاء کی معرفت ضروری ہوتی ہے اور تعریف غیر حقیقی کے تمام اجزاء کی معرفت ضروری نہیں ہوتی لہذا جب یہ تعریف غیر حقیقی ہے تو اس کے اجزاء میں مصحف کے لفظ کی معرفت ضروری نہیں ہے مصحف کی معرفت کیلئے عرف یا اشارہ بھی کافی ہے تعریف حقیقی ضروری نہیں ہے یعنی مصحف کی تعریف

اشارہ سے حاصل ہو جائے گی یا عرف پر ہی اکتفاء کیا جائیگا کہ مصحف عرف میں مشہور ہے سب لوگ پہچانتے ہیں کہ مصحف کیا چیز ہے لہذا قرآن کا سمجھنا تو مصحف پر موقوف ہے لیکن مصحف کا سمجھنا قرآن پر موقوف نہیں ہے ہاں اگر تعریف حقیقی ہوتی تو پھر دور بھی لازم آتا کیونکہ تعریف حقیقی میں تمام اجزاء کی تعریف کو جاننا ضروری ہوتا ہے تو لا محالہ مصحف کی تعریف ہوگی تو کہا جائیگا ما کتب فیہ القرآن اب قرآن کی معرفت مصحف پر موقوف ہوگی اور مصحف کی معرفت قرآن پر موقوف ہوگی اور یہ تو قف اشتی علی نفسہ ہے اس کا نام دور ہے جو باطل ہے۔
دور سے بچنے کے لئے بعض حضرات کی تاویلات اور شاریخ کی طرف سے تردید را یقال :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے غرض شاریخ بعض حضرات کا رد کرتا ہے کہ انہوں نے دور والے اعتراض سے بچنے کیلئے کہا تھا کہ دور لازم نہیں آتا وہ اس طرح کہ ما نقل الینا الخ یہ تعریف کتاب کی ہو اور مصحف کے بارے میں پوچھیں تو کہا جائے کہ ما کتب فیہ القرآن یا ما جمع فیہ القرآن اب مصحف کا سمجھنا قرآن پر موقوف ہے اور قرآن کا سمجھنا مصحف پر موقوف نہیں ہے بلکہ کتاب کا سمجھنا مصحف پر موقوف ہے اب جہت توقف تبدیل ہو گئی کہ کتاب کا سمجھنا تو مصحف پر موقوف ہے اور مصحف کا سمجھنا کتاب پر موقوف نہیں ہے یعنی ہالفاظ دیگر مصحف کا موقوف علیہ قرآن ہے اور کتاب کا موقوف علیہ مصحف ہے جہت توقف کے تبدیل ہونے سے دور لازم نہیں آئیگا۔
رد الشارع: شارع فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ جو کتاب ہے وہی قرآن ہے کیونکہ دونوں کی ماہیت ایک ہے پس مصحف کی معرفت کا قرآن کی معرفت پر موقوف ہونا یہ بعینہ کتاب کی معرفت پر موقوف ہوتا ہے لہند اپھر بھی دور لازم آئیگا
وبهذا يظهر
یہ شرح کی عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے فرض شاریے بعض حضرات کی تردید بیان کرنا ہے بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ النقل الیتا الخ یہ ماہیت قرآن ہے لیکن دور لازم نہیں آتا کیونکہ بالنقل الینا الخ یہ تو قرآن کی تعریف ہے تو اب قرآن کا سمجھنا مصروف پر موقوف ہے لیکن مصعوف کے بارے میں پوچھیں تو کہا جائیگا ما جمع فیہ الحی العلویہ مصحف ہے اب مصحوف کا سمجھنا قرآن پر موقوف نہیں ہو گا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ قرآن کا موقوف علیہ مصحف ہے اور مصحف کا موقوف علیہ وحی متلو ہے تو اب جہت توقف تبدیل ہو گئی اور جب جہت توقف تبدیل ہو تو دور لازم نہیں آتا۔
رد الشارع: شارع نے کہا کہ قرآن اور وحی متلو میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے دونوں کی ماہیت اور حقیقت ایک ہے ما جمع القرآن ہو یا ما جمع فیہ الوحی المعتلو کہو ایک ہی بات ہے تو دور لازم آئیگا۔
Circularity will necessarily occur. One should not object that circularity is not necessary because it arises only if the definition is of the essence of the Quran, not of the essence of the Book. For we say: the essence of the Book is exactly the essence of the Quran, due to what has passed, that both are names for the same thing. Thus, the dependency of the Mushaf on the essence of the Quran is exactly the same as its dependency on the essence of the Book. And with this it becomes clear that interpreting the Mushaf as 'what is collected in the recited revelation' does not remove the circularity, because that is also synonymous with Book and Quran. So the author has clarified that it is not a definition of the essence, whether the definition is of the Book or of the Quran; this indicates that there is no difference in the occurrence of circularity in both cases. Then he said: It is inevitable that circularity occurs if the definition of the essence of the Quran is intended; this indicates that the essence of the Book is the same as the essence of the Quran, so mentioning one of the two suffices for the other. Then if it is objected (to avoid circularity) that the Mushaf is interpreted as 'that which contains the pages' (i.e., the Mushaf is that in which pages are collected, absolutely), building upon the fact that this is the literal meaning (wad' lughawi), and it will exit from the definition of the abrogated recitation (mansukh al-tilawah) with the condition of tawatur, so no circularity occurs. We say: this is turning away from the apparent to the hidden, and from the real to the customary metaphorical, and that is not good in definitions. Then if it is objected that the definition of an usuli is nothing but that it is a universal concept that applies to the whole and to every part, and the knowledge of the Mushaf is nothing but that it depends on the Quran in the sense of the particular whole, and that is known and preserved among people; they memorize it and recite it, and it is not ambiguous to them, so no circularity exists. We say: If the knowledge of the particular whole is conceded as to its own reality without the knowledge of the universal concept, then the basis of the author's statement is that the definition is of the particular whole, not of the universal concept. If this definition of the Quran is for distinguishing from other things, then circularity will not occur. Elaboration: His statement 'then the completion of the answer' is the first part of the commentary. In it the commentator explains the text, the gist of which is: 'ma nuqila ilayna...' this definition of the Quran, if it is non-real (i.e., not of the essence of the Quran) but rather the definition is made only to separate the Quran from other things, then circularity will not occur, because in a real definition the knowledge of all parts is necessary, whereas in a non-real definition the knowledge of all parts is not necessary. Hence, when this definition is non-real, the knowledge of the word 'Mushaf' among its parts is not necessary; for the knowledge of the Mushaf, custom or indication is sufficient; a real definition is not necessary. That is, the definition of the Mushaf can be obtained through indication, or reliance on custom is enough, because the Mushaf is well-known in custom; everyone recognizes what the Mushaf is. Thus, understanding the Quran is dependent on the Mushaf, but understanding the Mushaf is not dependent on the Quran. However, if it were a real definition, then circularity would necessarily occur, because in a real definition knowing the definitions of all parts is necessary. Then inevitably the definition of the Mushaf will be given, and it will be said: 'that which contains the Quran'. Then the knowledge of the Quran would be dependent on the Mushaf, and the knowledge of the Mushaf would be dependent on the Quran, and that is something standing on itself; it is called circularity, which is invalid. That which is said: 'the explanation of the statement: fa'in atamma al-jawab...' The second part of the commentary is the refutation by the commentator of some people's interpretations to avoid circularity. These people said that circularity does not occur in that 'ma nuqila ilayna...' is a definition of the Book, and if you ask about the Mushaf, it is said: 'that which contains the Quran' or 'that in which the Quran is collected'. Now the understanding of the Mushaf is dependent on the Quran, while the understanding of the Quran is not dependent on the Mushaf, but rather the understanding of the Book is dependent on the Mushaf. Thus the direction of dependency changed: the understanding of the Book is dependent on the Mushaf, and the understanding of the Mushaf is not dependent on the Book. In other words, that upon which the Mushaf depends is the Quran, and that upon which the Book depends is the Mushaf. With the change in the direction of dependency, circularity does not occur. Refutation by the commentator: The commentator says this is incorrect, because the Book is the same as the Quran—both have the same essence. Therefore, the dependency of the knowledge of the Mushaf on the knowledge of the Quran is exactly the same as its dependency on the knowledge of the Book; hence circularity still occurs. And with this it becomes clear: The third part of the commentary is the refutation by the commentator of some other people. Some people said that 'al-naql ilayna...' is the essence of the Quran, but circularity does not occur because 'al-naql ilayna...' is a definition of the Quran. Now the understanding of the Quran is dependent on the Mushaf, but if you ask about the Mushaf, it is said: 'that in which the recited revelation (al-wahy al-mutlu) is collected'. Thus the Mushaf is that in which the recited revelation is collected. Now the understanding of the Mushaf is not dependent on the Quran; in summary, that upon which the Quran depends is the Mushaf, and that upon which the Mushaf depends is the recited revelation. Thus the direction of dependency changed, and when the direction changes, circularity does not occur. Refutation by the commentator: The commentator said that there is no difference between the Quran and the recited revelation; both have the same essence and reality. Whether you say 'that in which the Quran is collected' or 'that in which the recited revelation is collected', it is the same thing, so circularity will occur.
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage is an usul dispute about whether a certain definition of the Quran leads to circularity (دور). The commentator (al-Muhaqqiq) refutes several attempts to avoid circularity. The core issue: if we define the Quran as 'that which has been transmitted to us (manqul ilayna)' etc., then to understand 'Mushaf' we might say 'that in which the Quran is written'. This creates a circle: understanding the Quran depends on Mushaf, and understanding Mushaf depends on Quran. Some scholars try to avoid this by claiming the definition is non-essential (ghayr haqiqi) or by redefining Mushaf differently (e.g., as 'that which contains pages' or 'that which contains the recited revelation'). The commentator rejects each: (1) The definition is real (haqiqi) because it aims to define the essence. (2) 'Quran' and 'Book' are synonymous, so changing terms doesn't break the circle. (3) 'Recited revelation' (al-wahy al-mutlu) is identical to the Quran, so the circle remains. The commentator insists that the only way to avoid circularity is if the definition is purely for distinction (tamyiz), not real. Then understanding Mushaf via custom or indication suffices, breaking the dependency. The passage demonstrates rigorous logical analysis in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
دور (dawr): A logical fallacy where the definition of A depends on B and definition of B depends on A, causing circularity.
تعریف حقیقی (ta'rif haqiqi): An essential definition that captures the essence (mahiyya) of a thing, requiring knowledge of all constituent parts.
مصحف (mushaf): The physical codex in which the Quran is written.
وحی متلو (wahy matlu): Recited revelation, i.e., the Quran as it is recited, synonymous with the Quran itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why does redefining Mushaf as 'that which contains the recited revelation' not avoid circularity?
A) Because 'recited revelation' is broader than the Quran.
B) Because 'recited revelation' is identical to the Quran in essence.
C) Because the definition of Mushaf is still dependent on the definition of the Quran.
D) Because the direction of dependency is reversed.

Key Takeaway
A definition intended to capture the essence of the Quran leads to circularity; only a non-essential (tamyizi) definition breaks the dependency.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Deriving the Ruling on Persian Recitation: Quranic Dalil and Imam Abu Hanifa's Retraction
Explains the ruling on Persian recitation, the retraction of Imam Abu Hanifa, and the evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to derive the Hanafi ruling on reciting Quran in Persian translation from the Quranic verses describing the Quran as Arabic, and evaluate the impact of Imam Abu Hanifa's retraction on the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Imam Abu Hanifa retracted his initial permissibility because the Quran's description as 'Arabic' is a qat'i dalil that defines its essence.

This lesson examines the internal Hanafi dispute over reciting the Quran in a Persian translation. Using the Quranic verses that describe the Quran as Arabic, we will trace the derivation of the ruling that translation is not Quran. The lesson also explores the retraction (ruju') of Imam Abu Hanifa from his earlier view—a key moment in Hanafi usul that illustrates how the school resolves ikhtilaf when faced with a strong dalil.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic Dalil
Locate the two Quranic verses cited in the passage: 'Indeed, We have sent it down as an Arabic Quran' (12:2) and 'in a clear Arabic language' (26:195). These are the primary textual evidence for the ruling.
The verses are qat'i al-thubut (certain transmission) but zanni al-dalala (ambiguous meaning) due to possible interpretations.
2
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah (Indicative Aspect)
Determine how these verses prove that the Quranic recitation must be in Arabic. The key is that the attribute 'Arabic' is attached to the word 'Quran' or 'language', implying that the Quran itself is Arabic—a translation loses this attribute and thus cannot be considered Quran.
Imam Fakhr al-Islam argued that the apparent meaning (zahir) of the verses contradicts permissibility.
3
Apply the Hanafi Principle of Amr and Qat'i Dalala
In Hanafi usul, a command or description that is qat'i in meaning (nass) cannot be overridden by istihsan alone. Here, the description of the Quran as Arabic is treated as a nass that defines its essence, so recitation in another language is invalid.
This is why Imam Abu Hanifa's initial istihsan (based on meaning being the pillar) was later abandoned.
4
Consider the Retraction (Ruju') as Tarjih
The passage states that Imam Abu Hanifa retracted to the view of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). In Hanafi usul, the Imam's retraction is a valid form of tarjih—it indicates that the later, corrected view is the mufta bihi.
The retraction is narrated by reliable transmitters (Nuh ibn Abi Maryam, Ali ibn Ja'far).
5
Derive the Mufta Bihi Ruling
Based on the Quranic evidence and the retraction, the operative ruling is that recitation of Quran in Persian (or any non-Arabic translation) is not permissible in or out of prayer, and an impure person may not touch a mushaf in any language that contains Quranic verses.
The later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) extended this to prohibit touching Persian translations due to caution (ihtiyat).

تلاوت فارسی میں قراءت پر اور حرام ہے بے وضو کے لئے اس مصحف کو چھونا جسے فارسی میں لکھا گیا ہو پس بنایا گیا ہے نظم کو غیر لازم اس میں بھی پس نہیں ہے صحیح اس کا قول خاصتہ ۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ بنیاد رکھی گئی ہے اس کے کلام کی متقدمین کی رائے پر کیونکہ نہیں ہے صراحت ان سے اس بارہ میں اور متاخرین بنیا در رکھتے ہیں امر کی احتیاط پر بوجہ قائم ہونے رکن مقصود یعنی معنی کے۔ قول لکن الا صبح لیکن صحیح یہ ہے کہ بیشک رجوع کر لیا انہوں نے صاحبین کے قول کی طرف بناء کرتے ہوئے اس پر جسے روایت کیا ہے نوح بن ابی مریم نے ان سے کہا ہے فخر الاسلام نے بیشک وہ جس کا قول کیا ہے اس نے مخالفت کی ہے کتاب اللہ کی ظاہر ا اس حیثیت سے کہ وصف بیان کیا ہے منزل (قرآن) کی عربی کیسا تھے اور کہا ہے ابوالینسر نے کہ بیشک یہ مسئلہ مشکل ہے نہیں واضح ہوتا ہر ایک کے لئے جس کا قول کیا ہے امام ابو حنیفہ نے اور تحقیق تصنیف کی ہے امام کرخی نے اس میں لیبی تصنیف اور نہیں لائے کوئی دلیل شافی ۔
اختلاف صرف فارسی میں ہے یا دوسری زبانوں میں
تشریح: قولہ بغیر العربية : ۔ مائن نے کہا تھا کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک غیر عربی میں قراءت جائز ہے تو شارخ فرماتے ہیں کہ بغیر العربیة کے لفظ سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ عربی کے علاوہ تمام لغات میں قراءت قرآن جائز ہو اور یہ اختلاف جمہور اور امام صاحب کا تمام زبانوں میں ہو۔ لیکن بعض دوسرے حضرات نے فرمایا کہ غیر عربی سے مراد صرف فارسی ہے یہ اختلاف صرف فارسی ترجمہ میں ہے وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ فارسی چونکہ عربی کے ساتھ فصاحت و بلاغت میں شریک اور عربی کے قریب ہے اور حدیث شریف میں ہے کہ فارسی زبان بھی جنت کی زبان ہوگی جیسے عربی زبان ہوگی (اوکما قال) قولہ لوقرو: ماتن نے کہا تھا کہ ایک آیت غیر عربی میں پڑھ لے تو جائز ہے اس میں اشارہ کر دیا کہ جنبی اور حائضہ اس فارسی کے ترجمہ پڑھنے کی عادت نہ بنائے اور اس پر مداومت نہ کرے بلکہ مطہر کو بھی اس کی عادت نہیں بنانا چاہیے ہاں کبھی ایسا ہو جائے تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ اور یہ اشارہ اس طرح سے ہوا کہ مائن نے ماضی کا صیغہ کا استعمال کیا اسی طرح آیتہ کو نکر و لائے اس کی تکثیر تقلیل پر دال ہے مطلب ہوگا کہ اگر اس نے ایک دو آیت تلاوت کر لیں تو جائز ہے لیکن بہتر یہ ہے کہ نہ کرے۔ فان قیل: یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے غرض شارخ خاصہ کے لفظ پر اعتراض ہے کہ ماتن نے کہا تھا کہ نماز میں خاص طور پر فارسی میں قراءت جائز ہے اور خاصتہ کا فائدہ بیان کیا تھا کہ امام صاحب نے نظم کو صرف جواز صلوۃ کے حق میں رکن غیر لازم قرار دیا ہے اور غیر صلوۃ میں امام صاحب بھی نظم کو رکن لازم قرار دیتے ہیں یعنی غیر نماز میں الفاظ کو ہی قرآن قرار دیتے ہیں فلہذا جنبی اور حائضہ اگر فارسی میں ترجمہ پڑھے تو یہ جائز ہے یعنی غیر نماز میں نظم رکن لازم ہے تو گویا حائضہ نے فارسی کا ترجمہ پڑھنے کی صورت میں تلاوت ہی نہیں کی کیونکہ رکن لازم یعنی الفاظ کی تلاوت نہیں ہوئی اس پر اعتراض ہے، اعتراض:۔ یہ ہے کہ متاخرین کہتے ہیں کہ فارسی میں تلاوت کرنے سے سجدہ تلاوت واجب ہوگا اور غیر مطہر کے لئے اس مصحف کو چھونا جائز نہیں جس میں فارسی میں قرآن کا ترجمہ لکھا ہوا ہو نیز جنبی کے لئے قرآن کے ترجمہ کا مس جائز نہیں ہے ایسے ہی حائضہ کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ فارسی ترجمہ کو چھوئے اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ غیر صلوۃ میں بھی قرآن معانی کا نام ہے۔ اور اس صورت میں بھی نظم رکن غیر لازم ہے۔
جواب:- خاصہ متقدمین کے مسلک پر محمول ہے یعنی ماتن نے متقدمین کے مسلک کے مطابق اس کو نماز کے ساتھ خاص کیا ہے کیونکہ ان سے غیر صلاۃ کے بارے میں کوئی صریح حکم ثابت نہیں ہے اور معترض نے جو احکام غیر صلاۃ میں ثابت کئے ہیں یہ متاخرین کے نزدیک ہیں کیونکہ ان کا مذہب احتیاط پر مبنی ہے کیونکہ قرآن کا رکن مقصودی ( معنی ) وہ فارسی کے ترجمہ میں بھی موجود ہے اس لئے انہوں نے اس کی تلاوت کی اجازت نہیں دی۔
قول لکن اصح : امام صاحب سے رجوع ثابت ہے : امام ابو حنیفہ نے فارسی میں قراءت کو جائز قرار دیا تھا اصح قول یہ ہے کہ امام صاحب نے رجوع کر لیا تھا امام صاحب کے نزدیک الفاظ دال علی معنی کا نام قرآن ہے اور اس رجوع والی روایت کو ابو عصمہ نوح بن ابی مریم قاضی مرد اور علی بن جعفر (استاذ بخاری و مسلم واحمد بن حنبل) نے نقل کی ہے علامہ فخر الاسلام اس کی وجہ یہ بیان کرتے ہیں کہ اکثر آیات میں قرآن کی صفت عربی بیان کی گئی ہے کما قال اللہ تعالی انا انزلناه قرآنا عربیا اور دوسری جگہ ارشاد فرماتے ہیں وانہ لنتنزیل رب العالمین نزل به روح الامین علی قلبک تلسکون من المندرين بلسان عربی مبین تو ان دونوں آیات میں عربی یا لسان عربی کو قرآن کا وصف قرار دیا گیا ہے اور معنی عربی کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہوتا معنی عربی و غیر عربی میں کر سکتے ہیں اس لئے امام صاحب کا مذہب بظا ہر قرآن کے خلاف تھا اس لئے رجوع کر لیا۔ اور ظاہرا اس لئے کہا کہ مذکورہ آیات میں تاویل ہو سکتی ہے کہ پہلی آیت میں ضمیر کا مرجع سورۃ ہو اور ضمیر کو نہ کر اس لئے ذکر کیا کہ ما بعد مذکر تھا یعنی قرآن عربیا تو اس سے قرآنا کا عربی میں نازل ہونا ثابت نہیں ہوگا اسی دوسری آیت میں بلسان عربی مبین میں یہ احتمال موجود ہے کہ یہ منذرین کے متعلق ہو یعنی قرآن و حفظ و نصیحت عربی میں کرنا ہے اس سے قرآن کا عربی ہونا معلوم نہیں ہوگا اور جبکہ دوسری آیت وانہ فی زیر الاولین موجود ہے تو حقیقت میں ایک دو کلمات کا غیر عربی میں تکلم اس کے منافی نہ ہونا چاہیے لیکن کیونکہ بظاہر یہ آیات کے خلاف تھا
Recitation in Persian and it is forbidden for one without ablution to touch this mushaf which is written in Persian. Then the structure (nazm) is made non-essential also in this. Then his statement 'specifically' is not correct. We say that the foundation of his speech is based on the opinion of the early scholars because there is no clear statement from them regarding this. And the later scholars base upon caution due to the establishment of the intended pillar, meaning the meaning. Statement: 'But the correct is that they indeed retracted to the saying of the two companions (sahibayn), building upon what was narrated by Nuh ibn Abi Maryam from them. Fakhr al-Islam said: Indeed, he whose saying is stated opposed the apparent meaning of the Book of Allah in that he described the revealed (Quran) as Arabic. And Abul Yusr said: Indeed, this issue is difficult; it is not clear to everyone what Imam Abu Hanifa said. And Imam al-Karkhi wrote a treatise on it, but he did not bring any sufficient proof.
Difference: whether it is only in Persian or other languages.
Commentary: His statement 'other than Arabic': The matn said that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, recitation in non-Arabic is permissible. So the commentator says that from the word 'other than Arabic' it appears that recitation of Quran is permissible in all languages besides Arabic, and this is the disagreement between the majority and Imam Abu Hanifa regarding all languages. But some other scholars said that 'non-Arabic' refers only to Persian; this difference is only in Persian translation. The reason is that because Persian shares eloquence with Arabic and is close to Arabic, and in the noble hadith it says that Persian will also be a language of Paradise like Arabic (or as he said). Statement 'even if he recites': The matn said that if one recites a verse in non-Arabic, it is permissible. In it, there is an indication that a junubi and ha'ida should not make a habit of reading the Persian translation and should not persist in it; rather, a pure person should not make it a habit either. However, if it happens sometimes, there is no harm. And this indication occurred in that the matn used the past tense, and similarly he brought 'verse' as indefinite, indicating multiplicity or paucity. The meaning would be that if he recites one or two verses, it is permissible, but it is better not to. If it is said: This is the second part of the commentary's text. The purpose of the commentator's word 'specifically' is an objection. The matn said that in prayer, specifically recitation in Persian is permissible, and the benefit of 'specifically' was explained: that Imam Abu Hanifa considered the structure as non-essential only for the validity of prayer, but outside prayer, he also considers the structure as essential, i.e., outside prayer he considers the words as Quran. Therefore, if a junubi or ha'ida recites the Persian translation, it is not permissible, i.e., outside prayer, the structure is an essential pillar, so the ha'ida did not recite because the essential pillar, i.e., the recitation of words, did not occur. Upon this is an objection: The objection is that later scholars say that reciting in Persian makes sajda tilawat wajib, and it is not permissible for an impure person to touch a mushaf in which the Quran's Persian translation is written, and similarly it is not permissible for a junubi to touch the Quran's translation, and likewise for a ha'ida to touch the Persian translation. This indicates that outside prayer, the Quran is a name for the meaning. And in this case, the structure is also non-essential.
Answer: It is carried on the school of the early scholars, meaning the matn specifically tied it to prayer according to the school of the early scholars because no explicit ruling from them regarding outside prayer is established. And what the objector established regarding rulings outside prayer is according to the later scholars because their school is based on caution, because the intended pillar of the Quran (the meaning) is present in the Persian translation, so they did not permit its recitation.
Statement 'but the correct': The retraction from Imam Abu Hanifa is established. Imam Abu Hanifa had permitted recitation in Persian. The correct view is that he retracted. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the name 'Quran' applies to words indicative of meaning. And this report of retraction is narrated by Abu 'Isma Nuh ibn Abi Maryam the judge and Ali ibn Ja'far (teacher of Bukhari, Muslim, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal). 'Allama Fakhr al-Islam explains the reason: In most verses, the attribute of the Quran is described as Arabic, as Allah says: 'Indeed, We have sent it down as an Arabic Quran' and elsewhere: 'And indeed, it is the revelation of the Lord of the worlds; the Trustworthy Spirit has brought it down upon your heart that you may be among the warners, in a clear Arabic language.' In these two verses, 'Arabic' or 'Arabic language' is made an attribute of the Quran, and meaning is not specific to Arabic; meaning can be expressed in both Arabic and non-Arabic. Therefore, Imam Abu Hanifa's school apparently contradicted the Quran, so he retracted. And apparently this was said because there is a possibility of interpretation: in the first verse, the pronoun could refer to 'surah', and because the following word is masculine, i.e., 'Quran Arabic', so it does not prove that 'Quran' was revealed in Arabic. In the second verse, 'in a clear Arabic language' could relate to the warners, i.e., the warning and advice is in Arabic; this does not indicate that the Quran is Arabic. And when the other verse 'And indeed it is in the scriptures of the former peoples' exists, actually speaking one or two words in non-Arabic should not contradict it. But because it apparently opposed these verses.
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the Hanafi ruling regarding reciting the Quran in a Persian translation. It begins by stating the prohibition for an impure person to touch a mushaf written in Persian, and then explains the underlying principle: whether the structure (nazm) is an essential pillar (rukn lazim) or non-essential (ghayr lazim). The matn specifically said that recitation in Persian is permissible in prayer, implying that outside prayer, the structure is essential. The commentator clarifies that the early scholars (mutqaddimin) had no explicit statement on outside prayer, so the ruling was tied to prayer. Later scholars (muta'akhkhirin), out of caution since the meaning is present, ruled that touching the translation is forbidden for the impure and that sajda tilawat becomes wajib. The passage then addresses the retraction of Imam Abu Hanifa from his initial permissibility. The correct view is that he retracted to the opinion of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The evidence is from Quranic verses describing the Quran as Arabic. Fakhr al-Islam argues that since the Quran's attributes emphasize Arabic, and meaning can be expressed in any language, Abu Hanifa's initial view contradicted the apparent meaning, so he retracted. However, the commentator notes that there is room for interpretation (ta'wil): the verses might not explicitly require the Quranic text to be Arabic in all respects. The passage thus covers the fiqh ruling, the internal madhhab dispute, the evidence, and the resolution through retraction.

Key Terms
نظم (nazm): The structural wording of the Quran; in this context, whether it is an essential pillar (rukn lazim) or not.
خاصتہ (khāssatan): The word used in the matn meaning 'specifically' to limit the permissibility to prayer only.
رکن لازم (rukn lāzim): Essential pillar that constitutes the reality of the act; here, the specific Arabic wording of the Quran.
رجوع (rujūʿ): The retraction of Imam Abu Hanifa from his earlier opinion to the view of the two companions.
تلاوت (tilāwat): Recitation of the Quran; the act of reading the revealed words.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did Imam Abu Hanifa retract his permission to recite Quran in Persian translation?
A) Because the two companions convinced him using a hadith from the Prophet.
B) Because the Quranic verses describe the Quran as Arabic, and his initial view apparently contradicted this.
C) Because he realized Persian is grammatically inferior to Arabic.
D) Because the majority of scholars opposed him.

Key Takeaway
The Quran is defined by its Arabic wording; a translation lacks this essential attribute, so recitation in translation is not valid Quranic recitation, and Imam Abu Hanifa's retraction confirms the dominance of the nass over istihsan.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
10 min
The Hanafi Dispute on Reciting Quran Translation: Words or Meaning?
Dispute over reciting Persian Quran translation in non-prayer context

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the early and later Hanafi positions on reciting Persian Quran translation and evaluate the textual proof from Quranic verses used to justify Imam Abu Hanifa's ruju'.

Core Idea
The Quran is both words and meaning; early scholars required Arabic words, later scholars extended rulings to meaning.

Scholars debated whether reciting a translation of the Quran in a language like Persian counts as tilawa, especially for those in a state of impurity. This lesson explores the intra-Hanafi dispute between the early (mutaqaddimin) and later (muta'akhkhirin) schools, and how they relied on different interpretations of Quranic verses to support their views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
State the specific fiqh scenario: a junubi or ha'idah reciting a Persian translation of the Quran outside of prayer.
2
State the early school's view
The mutaqaddimin hold that it is not tilawa because the required pillar (words) is absent. Persian words are not the Quran.
3
State the later school's view
The muta'akhkhirin hold that it is tilawa because the intended pillar (meaning) is present in translation.
4
Analyze the dalil from Quran
Examine Surah Yusuf 12:2 and Surah al-Shu'ara 26:192-195. How do these verses describe the Quran as Arabic? What does this imply for translations?
5
Evaluate the ruju' report
Consider the narration that Imam Abu Hanifa retracted his earlier permission. What evidence supports or weakens this report?
