الترويج لحل التوضيح والتنويع قرار دیتے ہیں فلہذا جنبی اور حائضہ اگر فارسی میں ترجمہ پڑھے تو یہ جائز ہے یعنی غیر نماز میں نظم رکن لازم ہے تو گویا حائضہ نے فارسی کا ترجمہ پڑھنے کی صورت میں تلاوت ہی نہیں کی کیونکہ رکن لازم یعنی الفاظ کی تلاوت نہیں ہوئی اس پر اعتراض ہے، اعتراض:۔ یہ ہے کہ متاخرین کہتے ہیں کہ فارسی میں تلاوت کرنے سے سجدہ تلاوت واجب ہوگا اور غیر مطہر کے لئے اس مصحف کو چھونا جائز نہیں جس میں فارسی میں قرآن کا ترجمہ لکھا ہوا ہو نیز جنبی کے لئے قرآن کے ترجمہ کا مس جائز نہیں ہے ایسے ہی حائضہ کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ فارسی ترجمہ کو چھوئے اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ غیر صلوۃ میں بھی قرآن معانی کا نام ہے۔ اور اس صورت میں بھی نظم رکن غیر لازم ہے۔
جواب:- خاصہ متقدمین کے مسلک پر محمول ہے یعنی ماتن نے متقدمین کے مسلک کے مطابق اس کو نماز کے ساتھ خاص کیا ہے کیونکہ ان سے غیر صلاۃ کے بارے میں کوئی صریح حکم ثابت نہیں ہے اور معترض نے جو احکام غیر صلاۃ میں ثابت کئے ہیں یہ متاخرین کے نزدیک ہیں کیونکہ ان کا مذہب احتیاط پر مبنی ہے کیونکہ قرآن کا رکن مقصودی ( معنی ) وہ فارسی کے ترجمہ میں بھی موجود ہے اس لئے انہوں نے اس کی تلاوت کی اجازت نہیں دی۔
قول لکن اصح :
امام صاحب سے رجوع ثابت ہے
: امام ابو حنیفہ نے فارسی میں قراءت کو جائز قرار دیا تھا اصح قول یہ ہے کہ امام صاحب نے رجوع کر لیا تھا امام صاحب کے نزدیک الفاظ دال علی معنی کا نام قرآن ہے اور اس رجوع والی روایت کو ابو عصمہ نوح بن ابی مریم قاضی مرد اور علی بن جعفر (استاذ بخاری و مسلم واحمد بن حنبل) نے نقل کی ہے علامہ فخر الاسلام اس کی وجہ یہ بیان کرتے ہیں کہ اکثر آیات میں قرآن کی صفت عربی بیان کی گئی ہے کما قال اللہ تعالی انا انزلناه قرآنا عربیا اور دوسری جگہ ارشاد فرماتے ہیں وانہ لنتنزیل رب العالمین نزل به روح الامین علی قلبک تلسکون من المندرين بلسان عربی مبین تو ان دونوں آیات میں عربی یا لسان عربی کو قرآن کا وصف قرار دیا گیا ہے اور معنی عربی کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہوتا معنی عربی و غیر عربی میں کر سکتے ہیں اس لئے امام صاحب کا مذہب بظا ہر قرآن کے خلاف تھا اس لئے رجوع کر لیا۔ اور ظاہرا اس لئے کہا کہ مذکورہ آیات میں تاویل ہو سکتی ہے کہ پہلی آیت میں ضمیر کا مرجع سورۃ ہو اور ضمیر کو نہ کر اس لئے ذکر کیا کہ ما بعد مذکر تھا یعنی قرآن عربیا تو اس سے قرآنا کا عربی میں نازل ہونا ثابت نہیں ہوگا اسی دوسری آیت میں بلسان عربی مبین میں یہ احتمال موجود ہے کہ یہ منذرین کے متعلق ہو یعنی قرآن و حفظ و نصیحت عربی میں کرنا ہے اس سے قرآن کا عربی ہونا معلوم نہیں ہوگا اور جبکہ دوسری آیت وانہ فی زیر الاولین موجود ہے تو حقیقت میں ایک دو کلمات کا غیر عربی میں تکلم اس کے منافی نہ ہونا چاہیے لیکن کیونکہ بظاہر یہ آیات کے خلاف تھا اس لئے رجوع کر لیا۔ لیکن فقیہ ابو الیسر کہتے ہیں کہ امام صاحب نے جو یہ قول کیا ہے یہ بات فقہاء کو صراحتا سمجھ میں نہیں آئی اس لئے اس قول کا اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا امام کرختی نے اس مسئلہ میں لمبی چوڑی کتاب لکھی لیکن واضح بات وہ بھی نہ کر سکے۔
They decide that a junubi and a ha'idah, if they read the translation in Persian, then it is permissible, meaning in non-prayer the required pillar (nazm rukn) is necessary. So it is as if the ha'idah did not recite at all because the required pillar, i.e., the recitation of the words, did not occur. There is an objection: The later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) say that reciting in Persian makes the prostration of recitation (sajda tilawa) obligatory, and it is not permissible for an impure person to touch a mushaf in which the Persian translation of the Quran is written, and likewise the junubi is not allowed to touch the translation, and similarly the ha'idah is not allowed to touch the Persian translation. This indicates that outside of prayer, the Quran is also called meanings. And in this case also, the pillar of arrangement (nazm rukn) is not necessary. Response: It is carried according to the madhhab of the early scholars (mutaqaddimin), i.e., the matn author specified this for prayer according to the madhhab of the early scholars because from them no explicit ruling about non-prayer is established. As for the rulings that the objector established for non-prayer, these are according to the later scholars because their madhhab is based on caution, because the intended pillar (rukn maqsudi) of the Quran, i.e., meaning, is present in the Persian translation; therefore they did not permit its recitation. The sounder saying (qawl la'innah asahh? Actually 'qawl lakin asahh') It is established that Imam Abu Hanifa returned (ruju') from his position. Imam Abu Hanifa had declared recitation in Persian permissible. The sounder saying is that the Imam had returned. According to the Imam, the name Quran is for words that indicate meanings. This narration of return is transmitted by Abu 'Asma Nuh ibn Abi Maryam al-Qadi and 'Ali ibn Ja'far (teacher of Bukhari and Muslim and Ahmad ibn Hanbal). 'Allama Fakhr al-Islam explains the reason: In most verses, the Quran is described as Arabic, as Allah said, 'Indeed, We have sent it down as an Arabic Quran' (12:2) and elsewhere, 'And indeed it is a revelation of the Lord of the worlds. The Trustworthy Spirit has brought it down upon your heart, [O Muhammad], that you may be of the warners, in a clear Arabic tongue.' (26:192-195). So in these two verses, Arabic or Arabic tongue is made a description of the Quran, and meaning is not specific to Arabic; meaning can be in Arabic and non-Arabic. Therefore the Imam's madhhab was apparently against the Quran, so he returned. And he said 'apparently' because these verses can be interpreted: in the first verse, the pronoun could refer to the sura, and since the word after is masculine ('Quranan Arabiyyan'), it would not prove that the Quran was revealed in Arabic. Similarly, in the second verse, 'with a clear Arabic tongue' could be about the warners, meaning that warning and advice is in Arabic, so it does not imply the Quran is Arabic. And since the other verse 'and indeed it is in the scriptures of the former peoples' exists, then actually speaking one or two words in non-Arabic should not contradict it. But because apparently it was against the verses, he returned. However, Faqih Abu al-Yusr says that the meaning of this statement of the Imam was not clearly understood by the jurists, so this statement was not considered. Imam al-Karkhi wrote a lengthy book on this issue but could not clarify the matter.
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage discusses a usul dispute regarding the definition of Quran-whether it consists of words and meaning, or just meaning. The early school (mutaqaddimin) held that recitation of the Quran in non-prayer requires the actual Arabic words; thus a Persian translation is not recitation. The later school (muta'akhkhirin) took a precautionary approach, treating the Persian translation as Quran in terms of rulings like sajda tilawa and prohibition of touching by impure persons. The passage then narrates Imam Abu Hanifa's ruju' from his initial position allowing Persian recitation, citing verses that describe the Quran as Arabic. It also presents an alternative interpretation of those verses, showing the subtleties of textual analysis (ta'wil). The passage ends by noting that some jurists doubted the ruju' report.

Key Terms
متقدمین (mutaqaddimin): Early Hanafi scholars who held that recitation of Quran in non-prayer requires the Arabic wording.
متاخرین (muta'akhkhirin): Later Hanafi scholars who extended Quranic rulings to translations due to caution.
رجوع (ruju'): Imam Abu Hanifa's retraction of his earlier opinion allowing Persian recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the sounder saying (qawl asahh) regarding Imam Abu Hanifa's position on reciting Persian translation?
A) He always permitted it.
B) He retracted his permission.
C) He left the issue unresolved.
D) He forbade it only in prayer.

Key Takeaway
The definition of the Quran—whether it consists of words or meaning—affects multiple rulings, including permissibility of reciting translations by impure persons.

The Objection and Answers Regarding Tuhr in 'Iddah Calculation
Refuting an objection about partial tuhr counting as complete tuhr in iddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi argument against counting a partial tuhr as a complete tuhr for 'iddah and evaluate the Shafi'i objection based on usul principles.

Core Idea
A partial tuhr cannot count as a complete tuhr for 'iddah because it would lead to absurd results impossible in Shari'ah.

In this passage, the Hanafi school responds to an objection that a partial period of purity (tuhr) should count as a complete tuhr for the purpose of the waiting period ('iddah) after divorce. The objector argues that if any moment of purity is called tuhr, then the tuhr in which divorce occurs should be counted, and three such moments would complete the 'iddah. The Hanafi response, given by the majority and uniquely by the matn author, demonstrates why this interpretation is untenable using the usul principles of linguistic consistency and avoidance of legal absurdity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
What is the Shafi'i-like claim about tuhr? The objector says that a minimal moment of purity can be called tuhr, so the tuhr in which divorce occurs is a complete tuhr for 'iddah.
This objection relies on a broad linguistic definition of tuhr.
2
Analyze the majority response
The majority (jumhur) show that if every moment is a separate tuhr, then three moments would complete the 'iddah, which is absurd and against the intended meaning of three complete cycles.
This refutation uses reductio ad absurdum.
3
Examine the matn author's unique response
The matn author argues that if part of the first tuhr counts, then part of the third tuhr would also count, ending the 'iddah before the third menstrual cycle, contrary to consensus.
This response is considered more powerful because it avoids the counter-objection that could be raised against the majority.
4
Distinguish the two answers
The passage points out that the majority's answer can be countered by arguing that only the beginning or end of a tuhr is considered complete, not every moment. But the matn author's answer is irrefutable.
This shows the depth of Hanafi analysis in defending their position.
5
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
The Hanafi position that 'iddah requires three complete tuhrs between menses is upheld by ensuring linguistic terms are understood in their Shari'ah context, not merely linguistically.
This illustrates the Hanafi method of interpreting general terms with specific legal intent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعتراض: طہر مراد لینے کی صورت میں آپ نے جو خرابی بیان کی ہے ہم کہتے ہیں کہ وہ خرابی لازم نہیں آتی کیونکہ طہر اس گھڑی کا نام ہے جس میں عورت حیض سے پاک ہو یعنی کم از کم وہ وقت جس پر طہر کا اطلاق ہو سکے وہ طہر ہے اور وہ ایک گھڑی ہے یہ ضروری نہیں کہ مکمل ایام جو دو حیفوں کے درمیان ہوں وہ ایک مکمل طہر ہے اور اگر کچھ ایام گزرجائیں تو بقیہ ایام بعض طہر ہوں گے تو اب ہم کہتے ہیں کہ جس طہر میں طلاق دی جائے گی اس کو عدت میں شمار کیا جائے گا چونکہ بعض طہر کو بھی طہر ہی کہا جاتا ہے اس لیے یہاں یہ نہیں کہا جائے گا کہ یہ بعض طہر ہے بلکہ یہ مکمل طہر ہے اور مکمل طہر ہی عدت شمار ہوگا جب مکمل طہر عدت شمار ہورہا ہے تو عدت مکمل تین طہر ہوئی کم نہ ہوئی تو ثلثہ کے موجب پر عمل ہو گیا۔
جواب (۱):۔ اس عتراض کے دو جواب دیئے ہیں۔ ایک جمہور نے دیا ہے اور ایک مائن نے جمہور نے یہ جواب دیا ہے کہ آپ کے اعتراض سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ہر وہ گھڑی جس میں عورت حیض سے پاک رہے گی وہ مکمل طہر شمار ہو گی تو مطلب یہ ہو گا کہ دو حیضوں کے درمیان وقفہ آپ کے نزدیک ایک طہر نہیں ہے بلکہ کئی طہر ہیں یعنی جتنی گھڑیاں ہیں اتنے طہر ہیں اور اس سے یہ لازم آئے گا کہ خاوند جب بیوی کو طہر میں طلاق دے گا اس کے بعد متصل ہر گھڑی ایک طہر شمار ہوگا تو جتنی گھڑیاں متحقق ہونگی اتنے طہر متحقق ہونگے تو اس سے یہ لازم آئے گا کہ خاوند جب بیوی کو طہر میں طلاق دے گا اس کے بعد متصل ہر گھڑی ایک طہر شمار ہوگا تو تین گھڑیاں گزرنے سے تین طہر گزر جائیں گے تو گویا تین گھڑیاں گزرنے سے آپ کے نزدیک عورت کی عدت گزر جائے گی پھر تو یہ کہنا چاہیے کہ عورت کی عدت طلاق کے بعد تین گھڑیاں ہیں نہ یہ کہ اس مکمل طہر کے بعد جب حیض آئے گا اور اس کے بعد دو ہر اور گزریں گے تو پھر عدت مکمل ہو گی لیکن آپ اس بات کے قائل نہیں ہیں لہذا آپ کا یہ کہنا کہ بعض طہر بھی مکمل طہر ہی ہوتا ہے درست نہیں ہے۔
جواب (۲):۔ مائن نے جواب دیا کہ بعض طہر مکمل طہر نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ اگر ایسا ہو تو چونکہ پہلے اور تیسرے طہر میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے اس لیے اگر پہلے طہر کا بعض حصہ مکمل طہر شمار ہو سکتا ہے تو تیسرے طہر کا بعض حصہ بھی مکمل طہر شمار ہوسکتا ہے تو اب ہم یہ کہیں گے کہ اس پہلے طہر (طلاق والے ظہر اور اس کے بعد دوسرے طہر کو گزارنے کے بعد جب تیسر اطہر آئے گا تو اس تیسرے طہر کا کچھ حصہ گزرنے کے بعد عورت کی عدت پوری ہو جانی چاہیے حالانکہ یہ اجتماع کے خلاف ہے لہذا یہ کہنا کہ بعض ہر مکمل طہر ہی ہوتا ہے درست نہ ہوا۔
جمہور و مائن کے جوابات میں فرق
فرق بین الجوابین:۔ جمہور اور مائن کے جواب میں فرق یہ ہے کہ جمہور کو یہ جواب دیا جاسکتا ہے کہ جناب ہمارا مطلب یہ نہیں کہ مطلقا ہر ایسی گھڑی جس میں عورت حیض سے پاک ہو وہ طہر ہوتا ہے بلکہ ہمارا مطلب یہ ہے کہ طہر کے آخر میں اگر کچھ حصہ بچ جائے یا طہر کے شروع والا کچھ حصہ مکمل طہر کے حکم میں ہوتا ہے نہ یہ کہ ہر گھڑی ہی مکمل طہر شمار ہوگی لہذا آپ کا جواب درست نہیں ہے۔ تو جمہور کو یہ جواب دیا جا سکتا ہے لیکن ماتن کا جواب لا جواب ہے اس لیے تو فرمایا که هذا الجواب قاطع بشبهة الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى وقد تفردت بهذا ۔ اس لیے میرے اس جواب کی قدر کرو۔
Objection: In the case of taking tuhr (period of purity) as intended, the flaw you mentioned we say that flaw is not necessary because tuhr is the name of that moment in which a woman is pure from menses, i.e., the minimum time on which the term tuhr can apply, that is tuhr, and it is one moment. It is not necessary that the complete days between two menses be one complete tuhr. If some days pass, the remaining days will be part of tuhr. So we say that the tuhr in which divorce is given will be counted in the iddah. Since a part of tuhr is also called tuhr, therefore it will not be said here that this is a partial tuhr; rather it is a complete tuhr, and the complete tuhr will be counted as iddah. When the complete tuhr is being counted as iddah, then the iddah is complete three tuhrs, not less, so the rule of three has been applied. Answer (1): Two answers have been given to this objection. One is given by the majority (jumhur) and one by the matn author. The majority gave this answer: Your objection indicates that every moment in which a woman is pure from menses would be counted as a complete tuhr. So the meaning would be that the interval between two menses, in your view, is not one tuhr but many tuhrs, i.e., as many moments as there are, that many tuhrs. And from this it would necessarily follow that when the husband divorces his wife in a tuhr, then immediately every moment will be counted as a tuhr. So as many moments occur, that many tuhrs occur. Then this would necessitate that when the husband divorces his wife in a tuhr, immediately after that every moment is a tuhr, so three moments passing would mean three tuhrs have passed. Thus in your view, the woman's iddah would expire after three moments. Then you should say that the woman's iddah after divorce is three moments, not that after this complete tuhr, when menses comes and then two more menses pass, then the iddah is complete. But you do not believe that. Therefore your saying that a partial tuhr is also a complete tuhr is incorrect. Answer (2): The matn author answered that a partial tuhr is not a complete tuhr because if it were so, then since there is no difference between the first and third tuhr, if part of the first tuhr can be counted as a complete tuhr, then part of the third tuhr can also be counted as a complete tuhr. Then we would say that after this first tuhr (the tuhr of divorce) and after passing the second tuhr, when the third tuhr comes, after some part of that third tuhr passes, the woman's iddah should be completed, whereas this is contrary to consensus. Therefore saying that a partial tuhr is a complete tuhr is incorrect. Distinction between the answers of the majority and the matn: The difference between the answer of the majority and the matn author is that the majority can be answered by saying: Sir, we do not mean that absolutely every moment in which a woman is pure from menses is a tuhr. Rather, we mean that if some part remains at the end of the tuhr or some part at the beginning of the tuhr, it is considered as a complete tuhr, not that every moment is a complete tuhr. Therefore your answer is incorrect. So the majority can be answered like this, but the matn author's answer is unanswerable. Therefore he said: This answer cuts off the doubt of Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him), and I have been uniquely granted this. So appreciate my answer.
Source pages p. 539

Commentary
This passage presents an objection to a previous ruling regarding the calculation of the 'iddah (waiting period) based on tuhr (periods of purity between menses). The objector argues that if the minimum moment of purity is considered a tuhr, then when divorce occurs in a tuhr, that tuhr should be counted as a complete tuhr for 'iddah purposes, thus fulfilling the required three tuhrs without needing full menstrual cycles. The Hanafi response (from the majority, jumhur) refutes this by showing that it would lead to absurd consequences: if every moment is a complete tuhr, then the 'iddah would end after three moments, which contradicts the understanding that 'iddah requires three complete tuhrs between menses. The matn author provides a second, more precise answer: a partial tuhr cannot be considered a complete tuhr because if part of the first tuhr counts, then part of the third tuhr would also count, prematurely ending the 'iddah before the third menstrual cycle, which is against consensus. The passage then distinguishes the two answers, noting that the majority's answer can be countered, but the matn author's answer is decisive against Imam al-Shafi'i's position. The discussion highlights the Hanafi legal methodology of applying literal and conceptual consistency to prevent undermining the established rules of 'iddah.

Key Terms
طهر (tuhr): The period of purity between two menstrual periods; here debated as to whether it must be a complete period or a minimal moment.
عدة (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce before remarriage; for a woman who menstruates, it is three tuhrs (periods of purity) or three menstrual cycles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn author's answer, what would be the consequence if a partial tuhr were counted as a complete tuhr for the first tuhr?
A) The 'iddah would be completed after three moments.
B) The 'iddah would be completed after the first menstrual cycle.
C) The third tuhr would also be completed by a partial tuhr, ending the 'iddah prematurely.
D) The divorce would be considered invalid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school maintains that 'iddah requires three complete tuhrs (full periods of purity between menses), and no partial period can be substituted, as it would lead to legal absurdity and violate consensus.

The Qur'anic Proof for Khul' as Divorce: The Letter 'Fa' in Verse 2:230
Arguing that the Qur'anic 'fa' in 'fa in tallaqaha' shows khul' is divorce, not annulment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi argument that the Qur'anic particle 'fa' in verse 2:230 indicates that khul' is a type of divorce, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The Arabic 'fa' binds khul' to divorce — disconnecting them corrupts the Qur'anic structure.

In this passage, the Hanafi school defends a crucial principle: the literal and sequential reading of the Qur'an. The dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i over the nature of khul' (divorce by redemption) turns on the single letter 'fa' in verse 2:230. How we read this particle determines whether khul' counts as a divorce or as an annulment, with significant practical consequences for the number of divorces available to a husband after reconciliation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
The core disagreement: Is khul' talaq (divorce) or faskh (annulment)? The Hanafi position is that khul' is a type of divorce with compensation; the Shafi'i holds it is annulment.
2
State the Hanafi position and its dalil
The Hanafis argue that the particle 'fa' in 'fa in tallaqaha' indicates immediate sequence (ta'qib) and connects to the immediately preceding mention of khul' in verse 2:229, proving khul' is a divorce.
The dalil is the Qur'anic text itself, with the 'fa' as the key linguistic indicator.
3
State the Shafi'i position and its dalil
Imam al-Shafi'i connects the 'fa' back to 'al-talaqu marratan' (divorce is twice) from earlier in the passage, treating the khul' verses as an interpolation. Thus khul' is faskh.
The Shafi'i argument relies on avoiding a fourth divorce if khul' were counted as a third.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis claim the Shafi'i interpretation adds to the Book (ziyada 'ala al-kitab) by assuming an interpolation, and that the natural reading is the most direct one.
The matn author asserts this response is decisive.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Hanafi says khul' uses up one of three divorces; Shafi'i says it does not count, so the husband retains all three after remarriage.
This affects the number of divorces before permanent prohibition.

Source Text

وَقَوْله تَعَالَى ) فَإِنْ طَلَّقَهَا فَلاَ تَحِلُّ لَهُ الْفَاءِ لَفُظْ خَاصٌ لِلتَّعْقِيبِ ، وَقَدْ عَقَّبَ الطلاق بِالِافْتِدَاء فَإِنْ لَمْ يَقَعُ الطَّلَاقُ بَعْدَ الْخُلْعِ كَمَا هُوَ مَذْهَبُ الشَّافِعِيِّ رَحِمَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى يَبْطُلُ مُوجِبُ الْخَاصٌ تَحْقِيقُهُ أَنَّهُ تَعَالَى ذَكَرَ الطَّلَاقِ الْمُعَقِّبَ لِلرَّجُعَةِ مَرَّتَيْنِ ثُمَّ ذَكَرَ افْتِدَاء الْمَرْأَةِ ، وَفِي تَخْصِيصِ فِعْلِهَا هُنَا تَقْرِيرُ فِعْلِ الزَّوْجِ عَلَى مَا سَبَقَ وَهُوَ الطَّلَاقُ فَقَدْ بَيَّنَ نَوْعَيْهُ بِغَيْرِ مَالٍ وَبِمَالٍ لَا كَمَا يَقُولُ الشَّافِعِيُّ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى أن الالْتِدَاء فَسُخْ فَإِنْ ذَلِكَ زِيَادَةٌ عَلَى الْكِتَابِ ثُمَّ قَالَ فَإِنْ طَلَّقَهَا أَى : بَعْدَ الْمَرَّتَيْنِ سَوَاءٌ كَانَتَا بِمَالٍ أَوْ بِغَيْرِهِ ، فَفِى اتِّصَالِ الْفَاء بِأَوَّلِ الْكَلَامِ وَانْفِصَالِهِ عَنْ الْأَقْرَبِ . فَسَادُ التَّرْكِيبِ ( اعْلَمُ أَنَّ الشَّافِعِيُّ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى يَضِلُ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى ( فَإِنْ طَلْقَهَا ) بِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى ) الطَّلَاقُ مَرَّتَانِ) وَيَجْعَلُ ذِكْرَ الْخُلْعِ وَهُوَ قَوْله تَعَالَى ( وَلَا يَحِلُّ لَكُمْ أَنْ تَأْخُذُوا ) إلَى قَوْله تَعَالَى ) فَأُولَئِكَ هُمُ الظَّالِمُونَ ) مُعْتَرِضًا وَلَمُ يَجْعَلُ الخُلُعَ طَلَاقَا ، بَلْ فَسُخًا وَإِلَّا يَصِيرُ الْأَوَّلَانِ مَعَ الْخُلُعِ ثَلَاثَةٌ فَيَصِيرُ قَوْلُهُ (فَإِنْ طَلَّقَهَا ) رَابِعًا وَقَالَ : الْمُخْتَلِعَةُ لَا يَلْحَقُهَا صَرِيحُ الطَّلَاقِ فَإِنَّ قَوْلَهُ ( فَإِنْ طَلَّقَهَا ) مُتَصِلٌ بِأَوَّلِ الكَلامِ وَوَجُهُ تَمَسُّكِنَا مَذْكُورٌ فِي الْمَتْنِ مَشْرُوحًا ترجمہ: اور اللہ تعالیٰ کا قول فان طلقها فلا تحل له " ( پس اگر طلاق دے دے وہ اسکو پس نہیں ہے وہ حلال اس کے لیے ) فا ایسا لفظ ہے جو خاص ہے تعقیب کے لیے اور تحقیق پیچھے ذکر کیا طلاق کو فدیہ کے پس اگر نہ واقع ہو طلاق خلع کے بعد جیسا کہ وہ امام شافعی کا مذہب ہے تو باطل ہو جائے گا خاص کا موجب تحقیق اس کی یہ ہے کہ بے شک اللہ تعالیٰ نے ذکر کیا
And the saying of Allah Most High: 'fa in tallaqaha fala tahillu lahu' (then if he divorces her, she is not lawful for him). The letter 'fa' is a specific word for sequential ordering, and He has made divorce follow redemption (khul'). If divorce does not occur after khul', as is the school of Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him), then the implication of the specific (letter) is invalidated. Its verification is that He Most High mentioned divorce followed by revocation twice, then mentioned the woman's redemption. And in specifying her action here, there is an affirmation of the husband's action as previously, which is divorce. So He has explained its two types: without compensation and with compensation. Not as Imam al-Shafi'i says that khul' is annulment (faskh), for that is an addition to the Book. Then He said 'fa in tallaqaha', i.e., after the two (divorces), whether they were with compensation or without. So in connecting the 'fa' to the beginning of the speech and disconnecting it from the nearest [context], there is corruption of structure. Know that Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) connects His saying 'fa in tallaqaha' with His saying 'al-talaqu marratan' (divorce is twice) and considers the mention of khul', which is His saying 'wa la yahillu lakum an takhudhu' up to His saying 'fa ula'ika hum al-zalimun', as an interpolation, and does not consider khul' as divorce but as annulment. Otherwise the first two with khul' would become three, and His saying 'fa in tallaqaha' would become the fourth. And he said: The woman who makes khul' is not affected by explicit divorce, for His saying 'fa in tallaqaha' is connected to the beginning of the speech. And the aspect of our reliance is mentioned in the matn, explained. Translation: And the saying of Allah Most High 'fa in tallaqaha fala tahillu lahu' (Then if he divorces her, she is not lawful for him). 'Fa' is a word specific for sequential ordering, and He has indeed mentioned divorce after redemption. So if divorce does not occur after khul', as is the school of Imam al-Shafi'i, then the implication of the specific is invalidated. Its verification is that Allah Most High indeed mentioned... (the text cuts off).
Source pages p. 540

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the nature of khul' (divorce by redemption). The Hanafi argument is based on the Qur'anic verse 2:230, 'fa in tallaqaha fala tahillu lahu' (Then if he divorces her, she is not lawful for him). The Hanafis observe that the verse uses the particle 'fa', which indicates immediate sequence (ta'qib). This 'fa' connects to the preceding context where khul' is mentioned (verse 2:229). Thus, the 'fa' shows that the divorce mentioned after khul' is a continuation and that khul' itself is a type of divorce (talaq), not an annulment (faskh). Imam al-Shafi'i, however, argues that the 'fa' connects back to the beginning of the passage about divorce (2:228-229), considering the mention of khul' as an interpolation ('mu'tarid'). For him, khul' is an annulment, not a divorce, so the subsequent 'fa in tallaqaha' would then refer to a divorce after the two divorces mentioned earlier, making it a third divorce. The Hanafis reject this as an addition to the Book and argue that the natural reading is that khul' is included as a type of divorce with compensation. The passage also mentions that the Shafi'i position would lead to a fourth divorce if khul' were separate, which is impossible. The Hanafi claim is that the matn author's argument is decisive.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation (usually the return of the mahr or some property).
فسخ (faskh): Annulment of marriage without counting as a divorce; the marriage is dissolved as if it never occurred in terms of divorce counts.
فاء (fa): The Arabic particle 'fa' indicating immediate sequence or consequence; here argued to connect khul' to the subsequent divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the Hanafi argument in this passage use to prove that khul' is a type of divorce?
A) The word 'talaq' appears in the khul' verse.
B) The letter 'fa' in 'fa in tallaqaha' indicates immediate sequence after khul'.
C) The consensus of the companions.
D) The hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi reading of the Qur'anic 'fa' in verse 2:230 demonstrates that khul' is a type of divorce, and this interpretation is based on the grammatical rule of immediate sequence (ta'qib).

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
12 min
Khul' as Talaq: Hanafi Response to Shafi'i on the Particle 'Fa'
Hanafi response to Shafi'i on khul' as talaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi and Shafi'i arguments on the legal nature of khul' and apply the Hanafi critique of the parenthetical reading to the Quranic structure.

Core Idea
The particle 'fa' binds khul' to the divorce sequence; breaking it creates corruption of composition (fasad al-tarkib).

This passage addresses a key usul dispute: whether khul' (wife-initiated divorce with compensation) constitutes a divorce (talaq) or an annulment (faskh). The Hanafi school holds that khul' is a valid talaq, citing the immediate sequence indicated by the particle 'fa' in Quran 2:230. The Shafi'i school reads the khul' verses as parenthetical, preserving the total count of three divorces. The author refutes the Shafi'i position by arguing that their reading causes structural incoherence (fasad al-tarkib).

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested ruling
What is the legal nature of khul'? Is it a valid divorce (talaq) or an annulment (faskh)? State the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions.
Hanafi: talaq (specifically talaq ba'in). Shafi'i: faskh.
2
Analyze the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i argue that if khul' were talaq, the two revocable divorces (al-talaq marratan) plus khul' plus the third divorce in 'فإن طلقها' would total four divorces, contradicting the Quranic limit of three. Therefore khul' must be faskh.
They treat the khul' verses as a parenthetical (jumlat mu'tarida).
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi response focuses on the particle 'fa' in 'فإن طلقها'. The 'fa' indicates immediate sequence (ta'qib). The previous mention of khul' (fidya) is part of the same sequence, making khul' a type of talaq. The two initial divorces are without compensation; khul' is the third type (with compensation).
Thus 'فإن طلقها' would refer to a fourth divorce, which is prohibited, reinforcing that khul' is the third.
4
Critique the Shafi'i position
The author argues that disconnecting the 'fa' from the nearest preceding clause (the khul' verses) and connecting it to a distant clause ('الطلاق مرتان') causes fasad al-tarkib (corruption of composition). The 'fa' must attach to what immediately precedes it.
This is a structural/grammatical argument based on usul al-tarkib.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference? Under Hanafi law, a woman who obtains khul' is divorced (talaq ba'in) and must observe 'iddah; she can remarry. Under Shafi'i law, khul' is an annulment that does not count as a divorce, and the couple must contract a new marriage if they wish to reunite.
This affects the counting of divorces and the possibility of remarriage between the same spouses.

شافعی یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر ضلع کو بھی طلاق شمار کیا جائے تو طلاقیں چار ہو جائیں گی دو طلاقیں الطلاق مرتان والی ایک یہی ضلع اور ایک فان طلقہا والی حالانکہ طلاقیں جو مشروع ہیں وہ تین ہیں اس لیے خلع طلاق نہیں ہے بلکہ فسخ نکاح ہے جب خلع طلاق نہیں ہے تو اس کے بعد طلاق بھی نہیں ہو سکتی اس لیے آگے فان طلقہا کا تعلق اس کے ساتھ نہیں ہے بلکہ الطلاق مرتان کے ساتھ ہے کہ دو طلاقوں کے بعد اگر تیسری طلاق دے دی جائے خواہ مال کے ساتھ ہو یا بغیر مال کے عورت خاوند پر حرمت غلیظہ کے تحت حرام ہو جائے گی۔
Not that absolutely every moment in which a woman is pure from menstruation is considered purity; rather our meaning is that at the end of purity if some part remains or the beginning part of purity is considered complete purity in ruling, not that every moment counts as complete purity. Therefore your answer is not correct. So this answer can be given to the majority, but the author's answer is unanswerable; therefore he said: 'This answer is decisive against the doubt of al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, and I have attained this uniquely. So appreciate my answer.' And the saying of Allah Most High: 'فَإِن طَلَّقَهَا فَلَا تَحِلُّ لَهُ' – the 'fa' is a specific word for sequence, and He has followed the divorce with redemption. So if the divorce does not occur after khul', as is the school of al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, the effect of the specific becomes void. Its verification: Indeed Allah Most High mentioned divorce that follows two revocable divorces, then mentioned the wife's redemption. And in specifying her action here is confirmation of the husband's action as earlier, which is divorce. So He has explained its two types: without compensation and with compensation. Not as al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, says that redemption is annulment, for that is an addition to the Book. Then He said: 'فَإِن طَلَّقَهَا' i.e., after the two [divorces], whether they were with compensation or without. So connecting the 'fa' to the beginning of the speech and disconnecting it from the nearer [clause] causes corruption of composition. Know that al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, connects His saying 'فَإِن طَلَّقَهَا' with His saying 'الطَّلَاقُ مَرَّتَانِ' and considers the mention of khul', which is His saying 'وَلَا يَحِلُّ لَكُمْ أَن تَأْخُذُوا' up to His saying 'فَأُولَئِكَ هُمُ الظَّالِمُونَ', as a parenthetical. And he does not consider khul' as divorce, but as annulment. Otherwise the first two together with khul' would become three, so His saying 'فَإِن طَلَّقَهَا' would become a fourth. And he said: The woman who makes khul' is not subject to explicit divorce, because His saying 'فَإِن طَلَّقَهَا' is connected to the beginning of the speech. And the way of our argument is mentioned in the matn with explanation. Translation: And Allah's saying 'فان طلقها فلا تحل له' (Then if he divorces her, she is not permissible for him) – 'fa' is a word specific for sequence. And indeed He mentioned divorce after redemption. If divorce does not occur after khul', as is the school of Imam Shafi'i, then the effect of the specific becomes void. Its verification: Indeed Allah mentioned divorce that follows revocable divorce twice, then mentioned the woman's redemption. And in specifying her action here is confirmation of the husband's action as earlier, which is divorce. So He explained its two types: without compensation and with compensation. Not as Imam Shafi'i says that redemption is annulment, because that is an addition to the Book of Allah, because redemption does not indicate the count, unlike being interpreted as divorce, because divorce is mentioned at the beginning of the speech. Then He said 'فان طلقها', i.e., after the two divorces, whether they were with compensation or without. So connecting the 'fa' to the beginning of the speech and disconnecting it from the nearer [clause] is corruption of composition. Know that Imam Shafi'i connects Allah's saying 'فان طلقها' to Allah's saying 'الطلاق مرتان' and considers the mention of khul', which is Allah's saying 'لا تحل لكم ان تاخذوا' up to 'فاولئك هم الظالمون', as a parenthetical, and does not make khul' a divorce but an annulment. Otherwise the first two together with khul' become three, so Allah's saying 'فان طلقها' becomes a fourth divorce. And he said: The woman who makes khul' is not subject to explicit divorce, because Allah's saying 'فان طلقها' is connected to the beginning of the speech. And our method of argument is mentioned in the text with explanation. Khul': is it divorce or annulment of marriage? Commentary: Here the author branches off on the ruling of the specific with a second branch. First understand this difference: there is a difference regarding whether khul' is divorce or not. According to Imam Shafi'i, khul' is not divorce but annulment of marriage. For that reason he says that after khul', the wife cannot be divorced. As evidence, he presents these verses: Allah's command 'الطلاق مرتان' mentions two revocable divorces. The mention of the third divorce is in the later verse 'فان طلقها فلا تحل له من بعد...'. In between there is mention of khul': 'لا يحل لكم ان تاخذوا... فلا جناح عليكم فيما افتدت به... فاولئك هم الظالمون' – this mention of khul' is a parenthetical sentence. And the connection of 'فان طلقها فلا تحل له' is with 'الطلاق مرتان'. So Imam Shafi'i says: If khul' is also counted as divorce, then divorces become four: two from 'الطلاق مرتان' one from this khul', and one from 'فان طلقها', while divorces that are prescribed are only three. Therefore khul' is not divorce but annulment of marriage. Since khul' is not divorce, divorce cannot occur after it. Hence 'فان طلقها' is not connected with it but with 'الطلاق مرتان': that after two divorces, if a third divorce is given, whether with compensation or without, the woman becomes prohibited to the husband under severe prohibition.
Source pages p. 540

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute on whether khul' (divorce by redemption) constitutes a valid divorce (talaq) or an annulment (faskh). The Hanafi position, defended by the matn, holds that khul' is a type of talaq (specifically talaq ba'in), while al-Shafi'i maintains it is a faskh. The author begins by dismissing a previous objection, then focuses on the Quranic proof: the verse 'فَإِن طَلَّقَهَا فَلَا تَحِلُّ لَهُ' uses the particle 'fa' indicating immediate sequence. Al-Shafi'i reads this verse as directly following 'الطلاق مرتان' (two divorces), making the intervening mention of khul' a parenthetical (جملة معترضة). The Hanafi response is that this disconnection corrupts the composition (فساد التركيب), because the 'fa' would then attach to a distant clause rather than the immediate preceding mention of khul'. The author argues that the verse explicitly presents two types of divorce: without compensation (the first two) and with compensation (khul'), and both are forms of talaq. If khul' were not talaq, then the 'fa' would lose its effect of sequence. The Urdu explanation (تشریح) clarifies the Shafi'i argument: counting khul' as a divorce would make the divorces four (two revocable, plus khul', plus the third) while the maximum is three. The Hanafi counter argues that the two revocable divorces are those without compensation, and khul' is the third (with compensation), so the verse 'فَإِن طَلَّقَهَا' refers to a fourth which is impossible; hence the correct interpretation is that khul' is a form of talaq that counts as the third (or a separate type). The passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of textual analysis using grammatical and structural arguments. Authority weight: This is from Al-Tarwih li Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih, a later Hanafi commentary (Fatawa/Mutakhkhirin level), not from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
الخلع (al-khulʿ): Divorce initiated by the wife by paying compensation (fidya) to the husband, resulting in the dissolution of marriage.
الفاء (al-faʾ): The Arabic letter 'fa' used as a particle of sequence (taʿqīb) meaning 'then' or 'so', indicating immediate succession.
جملة معترضة (jumlat muʿtariḍa): A parenthetical sentence or clause inserted in the middle of speech without breaking the flow of the main clause.

According to the Hanafi position defended in this passage, what is the legal nature of khul'?
A) It is an annulment (faskh) of the marriage.
B) It is a valid form of divorce (talaq).
C) It is a suspended divorce that becomes effective only upon payment.
D) It is a prohibited form of separation.

Key Takeaway
The classification of khul' as talaq or faskh hinges on the grammatical and structural analysis of the Quranic verses, specifically the role of the particle 'fa' in establishing sequence.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
The Hanafi Proof that Khul' is Divorce: The 'Fa' Connection
Explaining and defending Hanafi view that khul' is talaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the particle 'fa' in the Quranic khul' verses and apply the Hanafi usul principle of immediate sequence (taʿqīb maʿa al-waṣl) to derive the ruling that khul' is a type of divorce.

Core Idea
The particle 'fa' requires the third divorce to follow khul', making khul' itself a divorce.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute over whether khul' (divorce initiated by the wife with compensation) is a valid divorce or an annulment. The debate hinges on the grammatical role of the Arabic particle 'fa' in the verse 'fa in ṭallaqahā' (فإن طلقها). The Hanafi school argues that 'fa' requires immediate connection to the nearest preceding clause, which is the khul' verse, thus necessitating that khul' itself be a divorce. The Shafi'i school, however, treats the entire khul' section as a parenthetical interpolation, connecting 'fa in ṭallaqahā' to the earlier clause 'aṭ-ṭalāqu marratān'. Understanding this linguistic analysis is key to grasping the Hanafi usul of textual interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the verses and their structure
First, locate the relevant Quranic verses: Surah al-Baqarah 2:229-230. Note that 2:229 mentions two divorces (aṭ-ṭalāqu marratān) and then discusses khul' (fīmā iftadat bihī). Verse 2:230 begins with 'fa in ṭallaqahā' stating that after a third divorce the wife becomes impermissible until she marries another. The structure is: two divorces → khul' → third divorce.
2
Locate the particle 'fa' and its function
Identify the particle 'fa' at the beginning of verse 2:230: 'fa in ṭallaqahā'. In Arabic grammar, 'fa' can indicate sequence, cause, or immediate succession. The Hanafi usul holds that 'fa' implies immediate connection (taʿqīb maʿa al-waṣl) between the following clause and the immediately preceding clause.
The Shafi'i school does not assign this strict immediate connection; they allow separation via a parenthetical.
3
Apply the Hanafi principle of immediate sequence
According to the Hanafi principle, 'fa in ṭallaqahā' must be directly connected to the nearest preceding clause. That clause is the khul' verse (fīmā iftadat bihī), not the distant 'aṭ-ṭalāqu marratān'. Therefore, the third divorce mentioned in 'fa in ṭallaqahā' is contingent upon the occurrence of khul'. Hence, khul' itself must be a type of divorce for this contingency to make sense.
If khul' were an annulment, the third divorce could not be built upon it, violating the 'fa' connection.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i counter-argument
Imam al-Shafi'i treats the entire khul' section (from 'lā yaḥillu' to 'fa ulā'ika hum aẓ-ẓālimūn') as a parenthetical (muʿtariḍa). Thus, 'fa in ṭallaqahā' connects back to 'aṭ-ṭalāqu marratān', meaning after two divorces, if a third is given (whether with compensation or not), the marriage ends. This avoids counting khul' as a separate divorce, keeping the total at three.
The practical difference: after khul', a Hanafi allows another divorce, while a Shafi'i does not, since the marriage is annulled.
5
Derive the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The thamarah al-khilaf is the legal consequence of the dispute. If khul' is talaq (Hanafi), then after khul' the husband may still pronounce up to two more divorces (since khul' counts as one of the three). If khul' is faskh (Shafi'i), the marriage is dissolved from that point, and no future divorce can occur; the woman must remarry another if she wishes to return.
This shows how a seemingly minor grammatical point produces a significant difference in family law.

دوسری تفریح اور احناف کی دلیل:۔ احناف کی دلیل جو خاص کے حکم پر تفریح بھی ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ یہاں فان طلقہا کا تعلق فیما افتقدت بہ ۔۔۔ الا یہ ضلع کے ساتھ ہے نہ کہ الطلاق مرتان کے ساتھ کیونکہ فان طلقہا“ میں ”ف لفظ خاص ہے اور اس کا موجب ہے تعقیب مع الوصل اس کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ مابعد اس کے ماقبل پر مرتب ہو یہان اس کا ماقبل ضلع ہے اور مابعد تیسری طلاق ہے تو یہ طلاق اسی ضلع پر مرتب ہے اب اگر ضلع کو طلاق نہ مانا جائے اور فان طلقہا کو الطلاق مرتان پر مرتب کیا جائے تو خاص کا موجب باطل ہو جائے گا کیونکہ ”ف“ کا مابعد اپنے متصل ماقبل پر مرتب نہیں ہوگا بلکہ جس پر مرتب ہوگا اس کے اور اس کے درمیان فصل لازم آئے گا۔ تو خاص کے موجب پر عمل کرنے کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ اس کا ترتب ضلع پر ہو اور اس صورت میں خلع کا طلاق ہونا ضروری ہے۔ لہذا اطلع طلاق ہے اور اس کے بعد طلاق ہو سکتی ہے۔ باقی امام شافعی نے یہ بات کہی تھی ۔ کہ خلع کو طلاق بنا ئیں تو طلاقوں کا چار ہونا لازم آئے گا تو ہم کہتے ہیں کہ چار طلاقوں کا ہونا لازم نہیں آتا۔ کیونکہ خلع میں کوئی مستقل طلاق کا ذکر نہیں ہے بلکہ الطلاق مرتان میں جس طلاق کا بیان تھا یہاں اسی کی ایک نوع کو بیان کیا ہے گویا کہ اس بات کی طرف اشارہ ہے کہ طلاق کی دو نوع ہیں ایک بغیر مال کے اور اس کا ذکر الطلاق مرتان میں ہے اور دوسری نوع مال کے ساتھ اور اس کا ذکر ضلع میں ہے۔ تو یہ کوئی مستقل طلاق کا بیان نہیں ہے۔ لہذا چار طلاقوں کا ہونالازم نہیں آتا۔ وفی تخصیص فعلہا :۔ یہاں سے ماتن نے ایک اعتراض کا جواب دیا ہے۔ اعتراض: خلع کے ذکر میں فیما افتقدت بہ " ہے یہاں افتقدت کی نسبت عورت کی طرف ہے یعنی ضلع میں عورت کے فعل کو ذکر کیا ہے حالانکہ طلاق تو مرد کا فعل ہوتا ہے تو اگر خلع طلاق ہوتی تو یہاں مرد کا فعل مذکور ہوتا۔ جواب:۔ عورت کا فعل مستقل فعل نہیں ہے بلکہ مرد کے طلاق والے فعل کو پختہ کرنے کے لیے ہے اصل فعل مرد کا ہی ہے لیکن یہاں پر چونکہ مال کا ذکر کرنا تھا اور مال عورت کی جانب سے ہوتا ہے اس لیے یہاں عورت کا فعل ذکر کر دیا ہے۔ خلع کو فسخ قرار دینے میں کتاب اللہ پر زیادتی لازم آتی ہے

لا کما یقول الشافعی :۔ یہاں سے امام شافعی کے مذہب کا رد کیا جارہا ہے کہ اگر امام شافعی کی بات کو مانا جائے اور ضلع کو نسخ نکاح قرار دیا جائے تو کتاب اللہ پر زیادتی لازم آئے گی کیونکہ آیت میں فتح کا ذکر نہیں ہے آیت میں افتداء ( فدیہ دینے ) کا ذکر ہے اور اس سے فتح والا معنی سمجھ میں نہیں آتا ہاں اگر طلاق مراد لیں تو کتاب اللہ پر زیادتی لازم نہیں آتی ہے کیونکہ اس سے پہلے طلاق کا ذکر ہے اس لیے اگر افتداء سے مراد طلاق لیں گے تو یہ قرینے کے موافق ہو گا۔ اور اس صورت میں فان طلقہا کا
At-Tarwīḥ li-Ḥall at-Tawḍīḥ wa t-Talwīḥ. Divorce which comes after two revocable divorces, then mentioned the woman's ransom, and in the specification of her action here is to confirm the husband's action as passed, and that is divorce. So he explained its two types: without wealth and with wealth. Not as Imam al-Shafi'i says that indeed giving ransom is annulment, because it is an addition to the Book of Allah, because paying ransom does not indicate the count, unlike interpreting it as divorce, because divorce is mentioned at the beginning of the speech. Then He said: 'fa in ṭallaqahā' meaning after two divorces, it is the same whether they are with wealth or without wealth. So connecting 'fa' to the beginning of the speech and separating from the nearest would corrupt the construction. Know that indeed Imam al-Shafi'i connected Allah's saying 'fa in ṭallaqahā' to Allah's saying 'aṭ-ṭalāqu marratān' and made the mention of khul' (the saying of Allah 'lā taḥillu lakum an ta'khudhū...' up to 'fa ulā'ika hum aẓ-ẓālimūn') as an interpolated sentence, and did not make khul' as divorce but annulment; otherwise the first two [divorces] added to the khul' together would become three, then Allah's saying 'fa in ṭallaqahā' would be a fourth divorce. And he said that the woman who performs khul' is not affected by explicit divorce because Allah's saying 'fa in ṭallaqahā' is connected to the beginning of the speech. And our method of argument is mentioned in the text with clarity. Khul': is it divorce or annulment of marriage? Explanation: From here the author makes a second subsidiary point on the ruling of the specific. First understand this dispute about whether khul' is divorce or not. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, khul' is not divorce but annulment of marriage, and for that reason he says that after khul' the woman cannot be divorced. His evidence is that the verse 'aṭ-ṭalāqu marratān' mentions two revocable divorces, and the third divorce is mentioned in the later verse 'fa in ṭallaqahā fa lā taḥillu lahu min baʿdu...'. In between comes the mention of khul': 'lā yaḥillu lakum an ta'khudhū... fa lā junāḥa ʿalaykum fīmā iftadat bihī... fa ulā'ika hum aẓ-ẓālimūn'. This entire sentence is parenthetical, and the connection of 'fa in ṭallaqahā fa lā taḥillu lahu' is to 'aṭ-ṭalāqu marratān'. So Imam al-Shafi'i says that if khul' were also counted as divorce, the divorces would become four: two from 'aṭ-ṭalāqu marratān', one being this khul', and one from 'fa in ṭallaqahā', whereas the legally prescribed divorces are three. Therefore khul' is not divorce but annulment of marriage. Since khul' is not divorce, it cannot be followed by divorce, so the subsequent 'fa in ṭallaqahā' is not connected to it but to 'aṭ-ṭalāqu marratān', meaning that after two divorces, if a third divorce is given, whether with wealth or without, the woman becomes impermissible to the husband under severe prohibition. Second subsidiary point and the Hanafi evidence: The Hanafi evidence, which also is a subsidiary point on the ruling of the specific, is that here 'fa in ṭallaqahā' is connected to 'fīmā iftadat bihī...' i.e., to khul' and not to 'aṭ-ṭalāqu marratān'. Because the letter 'fa' in 'fa in ṭallaqahā' is a particle of sequence, requiring immediate succession with connection. Its requirement is that the later follows the immediately preceding. Here the preceding is khul', and the later is the third divorce. So this divorce is built upon that khul'. Now if khul' is not recognized as divorce, and 'fa in ṭallaqahā' is built upon 'aṭ-ṭalāqu marratān', then the requirement of 'fa' would be violated, because the later would not follow its immediate predecessor but would have an intervening separation. So to give effect to the requirement of 'fa', it is necessary that its sequence be upon khul', and in that case khul' must be divorce. Thus khul' is divorce and divorce can occur after it. As for what Imam al-Shafi'i said – that if we make khul' divorce, divorces would become four – we say that four divorces are not necessary. Because in khul' there is no mention of an independent divorce; rather, the divorce mentioned in 'aṭ-ṭalāqu marratān' is here specifying its type. It is as if it indicates that there are two types of divorce: one without wealth, mentioned in 'aṭ-ṭalāqu marratān', and the other with wealth, mentioned in the khul' verse. So this is not an independent statement of divorce. Hence four divorces do not become necessary. 'Wa fī takhṣīṣi fiʿlihā': From here the author answers an objection. Objection: In the mention of khul', it is 'fīmā iftadat bihī' – here 'iftadat' is attributed to the woman, meaning that the woman's action is mentioned in khul', whereas divorce is the husband's action. So if khul' were divorce, the husband's action would be mentioned here. Answer: The woman's action is not independent; rather, it is to confirm the husband's divorce action. The original action is the husband's, but since wealth was to be mentioned and wealth comes from the woman's side, the woman's action is mentioned here. Making khul' annulment would entail an addition to the Book of Allah. 'Lā kamā yaqūlu ash-Shāfiʿī': From here the refutation of Imam al-Shafi'i's school is made, that if his statement is accepted and khul' is declared annulment, then an addition to the Book of Allah would be necessary. Because the verse does not mention 'faskh'; it mentions 'iftidā' (ransom), and from it the meaning of annulment is not understood. Yes, if divorce is intended, then no addition to the Book of Allah is necessary, because divorce was mentioned previously. So if by 'iftidā' we mean divorce, it would be in accordance with the context. And in that case 'fa in ṭallaqahā'...
Source pages p. 541

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi exposition and defense of the position that khul' (divorce initiated by the wife with compensation) is a type of divorce (talaq), not an annulment (faskh) as held by Imam al-Shafi'i. The author begins by stating that the previous verse (aṭ-ṭalāqu marratān) mentions two revocable divorces, and then the verse discusses the wife's ransom (fidyah). The specification of the wife's action here is actually to confirm the husband's action (i.e., divorce). The author clarifies that the verse explains two types of divorce: without wealth and with wealth. This refutes Imam al-Shafi'i's claim that khul' is an annulment and that considering it as divorce would be an addition to the Qur'an. The Hanafi argument relies on the particle 'fa' (ف) in the phrase 'fa in ṭallaqahā' (فإن طلقها). According to the Hanafi interpretation, the 'fa' indicates immediate sequence with connection (taʿqīb maʿa al-waṣl), meaning the latter clause must directly follow and be connected to the immediately preceding clause. In the Qur'anic structure, the preceding clause is the khul' verse (fīmā iftadat bihī), not 'aṭ-ṭalāqu marratān'. Therefore, the third divorce mentioned in 'fa in ṭallaqahā' is contingent upon the khul' having occurred. If khul' were not considered a valid divorce, then the 'fa' would lose its proper grammatical effect, as the later clause would be disconnected from its immediate predecessor. Thus, to preserve the grammatical and legal coherence, khul' must be a type of divorce. The passage then addresses an objection: in the khul' verse, the action is attributed to the wife ('iftadat'), whereas divorce is the husband's action. The Hanafi response is that the wife's action is not independent; it serves to confirm the husband's divorce action. The wife's ransom is the means by which the husband's divorce is finalized. The mention of the wife's action is because the wealth comes from her side. Finally, the author refutes the Shafi'i argument that considering khul' as divorce would result in four divorces (two from 'aṭ-ṭalāqu marratān', one from khul', and one from 'fa in ṭallaqahā'). The Hanafi response is that khul' is not an independent divorce; it is merely a specification of one of the two types of divorce already mentioned in 'aṭ-ṭalāqu marratān'. Therefore, the total number of divorces remains three.

Key Terms
خلع (khalʿ / khulʿ): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation (fidya) paid to the husband.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment of a marriage contract, dissolving the marriage without counting as a divorce.
ف (fa): The Arabic particle 'fa' (ف) indicating sequence with immediate connection (taʿqīb maʿa al-waṣl). The Hanafis argue that this particle requires the following clause to be directly connected to the immediately preceding clause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the third divorce (fa in ṭallaqahā) connected to the khul' verse rather than to 'aṭ-ṭalāqu marratān'?
A) Because the particle 'fa' requires immediate connection to the nearest preceding clause, which is the khul' verse.
B) Because 'aṭ-ṭalāqu marratān' mentions two divorces, so the third must be based on the khul' verse to make three.
C) Because the Shafi'i school accepts this connection.
D) Because the khul' verse explicitly says it is a divorce.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that khul' is a type of divorce by relying on the grammatical rule that the particle 'fa' requires immediate connection to the nearest preceding clause.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Applying Analogies of Naskh and Istithna to Khiyar in Sales
Analyzing analogies for khiyar in a two-slave sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of tarjih between competing analogies (qiyas) in khiyar sales, specifically by selecting the analogy of naskh or istithna based on the presence of ignorance (jahl).

Core Idea
When analogies conflict, prefer the one that eliminates ignorance.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, analogical reasoning (qiyas) extends rulings to new cases. However, sometimes two different analogies can be applied to the same scenario, leading to conflicting conclusions. This passage from *Sharh al-Taozeeh wal-Talweeh* presents such a case: a sale of two slaves with khiyar (option). The author examines whether the proper analogy is with *naskh* (abrogation) or *istithna* (exception). The resolution depends on the presence of uncertainty (*jahl*). By studying this case, you will learn how the Hanafi school resolves competing analogies to reach a valid ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four scenarios
List the four combinations of known/unknown subject of option (place of khiyar) and known/unknown price (thaman) per slave.
The first scenario: both known; second: both unknown; third: subject known, price unknown; fourth: subject unknown, price known.
2
Apply the naskh analogy
Assume the opted slave was originally included in the contract and then abrogated (removed). Conclude the sale is valid in all four scenarios because no defect arises.
Naskh analogy leads to bay' bil-hissa baqa (partial sale in continuity), which is valid.
3
Apply the istithna analogy
Assume the opted slave was never part of the contract; the option is an exception. Identify defects: jahl in subject or price, or an invalid condition (accepting sale of non-sold item as condition). In all four scenarios, the sale is invalid.
First scenario: no jahl, but accepting the option is a condition that invalidates (shart fasid). Other scenarios have additional jahl.
4
Perform tarjih
Prefer the naskh analogy only in the first scenario (both subject and price known) because it avoids jahl and the only defect is a condition that can be overlooked, but here the condition is integral. In the other three scenarios, prefer istithna due to jahl.
The final ruling: sale valid only when both subject of option and price per slave are known.

محل خیار بھی متعین ہو کہ مجھے اس غلام میں خیار ہے اور شن بھی متعین ہو اور اس کی صورت یہ ہوگی کہ میں ان دو غلاموں کو ہزار کے بدلے بیچتا ہوں ہر غلام کی قیمت پانچ سو ہے اور مجھے اس غلام میں خیار ہے۔
(ii) اس کے برعکس کہ نہ محل خیار متعین ہو اور نہ ہی ثمن معلوم ہو۔ یعنی یوں کہے کہ میں یہ دو غلام ہزار کے بدلے بیچتا ہوں اور مجھے کسی ایک غلام میں خیار ہے۔
(iii) محل خیار متعین ہو لیکن شمن متعین نہ ہو ۔ مثلا یوں کہے کہ میں یہ دو غلام ایک ہزار کے بدلے میں بیچتا ہوں اور اس (خاص) غلام میں مجھے اختیار ہے۔ (۱۷) مثمن متعین ہو لیکن محل خیار متعین نہ ہو۔ مثلا یوں کہتا ہے کہ میں نے یہ دو غلام ایک ہزار کے بدلے بیچ دیے ہر ایک کی قیمت پانچ سوروپیہ ہے لیکن مجھے کسی ایک غلام میں اختیار ہے۔ حکم:۔ اگر ان چار صورتوں میں نسخ کی مشابہت کا اعتبار کیا جائے یعنی اس بات کا اعتبار کیا جائے کہ یہ غلام ( جس میں خیار ہے) ایجاب میں داخل تھا اب اس کو خارج کیا جا رہا ہے یعنی حکم میں تبدیلی کی جارہی ہے تو چاروں صورتوں میں بیج درست ہونی چاہیے کیونکہ کوئی خرابی لازم نہیں آتی ۔ ہاں انتقالا زم آئے گا کہ یہ بیع بالحصہ بن جائے گی ۔ اور اس میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ بیع بالحصہ بقاء ہوگی ابتداء نہیں ہوگی اور بیع بالحصہ بقاء بیع کو فاسد نہیں کرتی ۔
اور اگر دیکھا جائے کہ اس کو استثناء کے ساتھ مشابہت ہے یعنی کہ یہ غلام حکم میں داخل نہیں تھا اور اب رد کے ذریعہ اسی کا بیان کیا جارہا ہے تو چاروں سورتوں میں بیع نا جائز ہونی چاہیے کیونکہ اس میں کچھ خرابیاں لازم آتی ہیں۔ مثلاً پہلی صورت کہ جہاں شمن بھی معلوم ہو اور محل خیار بھی متعین ہو جہالت ثمن یا جہات مبیع تو لازم نہیں آتی لیکن غیر مبیع ( جس غلام میں خیار ہے ) میں بیع کو قبول کرنا شرط بن رہا ہے جبیع میں بیچ کو قبول کرنے کیلئے اور یہ شرط فاسد ہے لھذا بیع درست نہیں ہونی چاہیے اور دوسری صورتوں میں یہ خرابی بھی لازم آتی ہے اس کے ساتھ ایک اور خرابی بھی لازم آتی ہے اور وہ ہے جہالت والی خرابی۔ کہ جہاں محل خیار متعین نہیں ہے وہاں مبیع میں جہالت ہے جہاں شمن معلوم نہیں وہاں شمن میں جہالت ہے اور جہاں دونوں معلوم نہیں وہاں دونوں میں جہالت ہے اور اس طرح کی جہالت بیع کو فاسد کر دیتی ہے۔ تو استثناء کی مشابہت کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ چاروں صورتوں میں بیع فاسد ہو۔
تو جب شیخ کی مشابہت چاروں صورتوں میں بیع کو جائز قرار دیتی ہے اور استثناء کی مشابہت چاروں صورتوں میں بیج کو نا جائز قرار دیتی ہے تو ہم دونوں کا اعتبار کریں گے۔
اول صورت کے علاوہ یعنی جہاں محل خیار یا من یا دونوں مجہول ہیں وہاں ہم استثناء کی مشابہت کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے ہے کہیں گے کہ بیچ درست نہیں ہے اور پہلی صورت کہ جہاں محل خیار و ثمن دونوں معلوم ہیں وہاں نسخ کی مشابہت کا اعتبار کریں گے اور بیع کو صحیح قرار دیں گے۔ استثناء کی مشابہت کا اعتبار نہیں کریں گے کہ پھر یہ کہیں کہ یہاں غیر بی کو مبیع کے قبول کرنے کیلئے شرط بنایا جارہا ہے اس لیے یہ بیچ فاسد ہے بلکہ ہم نسخ کی مشابہت کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے بیچ کو جائز کہیں گے۔ غلام اور آزاد کی بیچ میں ہر ایک کے علیحدہ ثمن بیان کرنے کو شیخ سے مشابہت نہیں ہے بخلاف ما اذ باع الحر والعبد : ۔ یہاں سے ماتن یہ بیان فرمارہے ہیں کہ اگر کوئی آدمی حر اور غلام ایک معاملہ میں ہزار کے بدلہ میں بیچتا ہے اور دونوں کا ثمن متعین کر دیتا ہے اور یوں کہتا ہے کہ میں نے یہ دو غلام ایک ہزار کے بدلے میں بیچے اور ہر ایک کی قیمت پانچ سوروپیہ ہے تو اس صورت میں حر کی طرح غلام میں بھی امام صاحب کے نزدیک بیچ صحیح نہیں ہوتی حالانکہ یہ صورت بھی مذکورہ بالا چار صورتوں میں سے پہلی صورت کی طرح ہے اس کو شیخ کے ساتھ بھی مشابہت ہے اور استثناء کے ساتھ بھی مشابہت حاصل ہے اور یہاں ثمن یا میچ میں جہالت بھی نہیں ہے تو اس میں بھی نسخ کی رعایت کرنی چاہیے اور استثناء کی رعایت نہیں کرنی چاہیے غلام کی بیع جائز ہونی چاہیے لیکن امام صاحب یہاں بیع کو نا جائز کہتے ہیں۔ تو ماتن فرما رہے ہیں کہ حر اور غلام کو بیچنے والی صورت کو شیخ کے ساتھ مشابہت ہے ہی نہیں کیونکہ نسخ کے ساتھ مشابہت تب ہو سکتی ہے جب حر شروع سے ایجاب میں داخل ہو حالانکہ یہ ایجاب میں داخل ہی نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ مبیع بننے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا ۔ جب یہ شروع سے بیچ میں داخل ہی نہیں ہے تو اس کو استثناء کے ساتھ ہی مشابہت ہے نسخ کے ساتھ کوئی مشابہت نہیں ہے لھذا یہاں بیچ درست نہیں ہوگی لیکن یہاں شرط خیار والی صورت میں غلام چونکہ مبیع بننے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے اس لیے وہ ایجاب میں داخل ہو جائے گا تو اس کو نسخ کے ساتھ مشابہت ہے۔
The place of option is specified: 'I have the option in this slave' and the price is also specified. Its form: I sell these two slaves for one thousand, each slave's price is five hundred, and I have the option in this slave. (ii) The opposite: neither the place of option is specified nor the price known. That is, he says: I sell these two slaves for one thousand, and I have the option in one of them. (iii) The place of option is specified but the price is not specified. For example, he says: I sell these two slaves for one thousand, and I have the choice in this (specific) slave. (17) The sold object is specified but the place of option is not specified. For example, he says: I sold these two slaves for one thousand, each price five hundred rupees, but I have the option in one of them. Ruling: If in these four scenarios we consider the analogy of abrogation (naskh), i.e., we consider that this slave (in which the option exists) was included in the offer and now is being excluded, i.e., the ruling is being changed, then in all four scenarios the sale should be valid because no defect arises. However, a transfer (intiqal) will occur: the sale becomes a partial sale (bay' bil-hissa). There is no harm in this because this partial sale is a remaining (baqa) sale, not an initial one, and a partial sale in continuity does not invalidate the sale. And if we look at it having similarity with exception (istithna), i.e., this slave was not included in the ruling, and now by rejection (rad) it is being expressed, then in all four scenarios the sale should be impermissible because some defects arise. For example, in the first scenario where both the price is known and the place of option is specified, ignorance of price or ignorance of the sold object does not occur, but accepting the sale in the non-sold (the slave in which there is option) becomes a condition for accepting the sale in the sale, and this condition is invalid (fasad), therefore the sale should not be valid. In the other scenarios, this defect also arises along with another defect: the defect of ignorance. Where the place of option is not specified, there is ignorance in the sold object; where the price is not known, there is ignorance in the price; and where both are not known, there is ignorance in both, and such ignorance invalidates the sale. So the requirement of the analogy of exception is that in all four scenarios the sale is invalid. So when the analogy of naskh renders the sale valid in all four scenarios and the analogy of istithna renders it invalid in all four, we will consider both. Except for the first scenario, i.e., where the place of option or the price or both are unknown, we will consider the analogy of istithna and say that the sale is not valid. And in the first scenario, where both the place of option and the price are known, we will consider the analogy of naskh and deem the sale valid. We will not consider the analogy of istithna, because it would say that here accepting the non-sold as sold is made a condition, so the sale is invalid. Rather, we consider the analogy of naskh and say the sale is permissible. In the sale of a slave and a free person, stating each one's price separately does not have resemblance to naskh, contrary to the case of selling a free person and a slave (ma idha ba'a al-hurr wa al-'abd). From here, the matn author is explaining that if a person sells a free person and a slave in one transaction for one thousand, and specifies the price of both, saying: 'I sold these two slaves for one thousand, each price five hundred rupees,' then in this case, according to Imam Sahib (Abu Hanifa), the sale of the slave, like the free person, is not valid, although this case is similar to the first of the four scenarios above; it has resemblance to both naskh and istithna, and there is no ignorance in price or sold object. So here too one should consider naskh and not istithna; the sale of the slave should be valid. But Imam Sahib says it is invalid. So the matn author says that the case of selling a free and a slave has no resemblance to naskh at all, because resemblance to naskh occurs only when the free person was included in the offer from the beginning, whereas it is not included in the offer because it lacks the capacity to be sold. Since it was never included in the sale, it only resembles istithna, not naskh. Therefore, the sale is not valid here. But in the case of a condition of option (khiyar), the slave has the capacity to be sold, so it enters the offer, and thus it has resemblance to naskh.
Source pages p. 594

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul analysis of khiyar in a sale involving two slaves. The author examines four scenarios: (i) both the slave subject to option and the total price are known, (ii) neither known, (iii) only the subject known, (iv) only the price known. He then considers two competing analogies: naskh (abrogation), where the option is seen as removing the slave from the original contract, and istithna (exception), where the slave was never part of the contract. If naskh analogy is used, all four sales are valid. If istithna is used, all are invalid due to ignorance or invalid conditions. The author resolves by applying istithna to the three cases with ignorance and naskh to the first case (both known), making it valid. He then contrasts this with a sale of a free person and a slave together. Here, Imam Abu Hanifa rules the sale invalid, even with specified prices, because the free person was never part of the contract (incapable of being sold), so only the istithna analogy applies. This illustrates how usul principles (qiyas, tarjih between analogies) determine fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
خیار (khiyar): An option or choice given to one party in a contract, allowing them to rescind or confirm the sale.
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation or removal of a previous ruling, here applied analogically to excluding an item from a sale contract.
استثناء (istithna): Exception, i.e., excluding something from a statement; analogically, considering the opted item as never having been part of the contract.
بیع بالحصہ (bay' bil-hissa): A partial sale where part of the subject is sold, and the rest is retained; here it is a consequence of applying naskh analogy.
ترجیح (tarjih): Preponderance; giving preference to one Quranic evidence, hadith, or analogy over another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the discussion of selling two slaves with khiyar, under which scenario is the sale considered valid according to the final ruling?
A) When neither the price nor the subject of option is known
B) When only the subject of option is known but the price is unknown
C) When both the subject of option and the price are known
D) When only the price is known but the subject of option is unknown

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, when two analogies conflict, prefer the one that avoids ignorance (jahl); naskh analogy only applies when both the subject of option and the price per unit are known.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Refuting Arguments That Two People Form a Jama'ah
Refutes proofs that two constitute a group

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze a Hanafi refutation of the claim that two people constitute a jama'ah, identifying the opposing proofs and the Hanafi responses, and apply the principle of takhsis to hadiths cited as evidence.

Core Idea
The plural requires three; apparent hadiths are context-specific, not general.

This lesson delves into a classical usul al-fiqh dispute about the minimum number required to form a jama'ah (group) for legal rulings. The Hanafi school, based on linguistic consensus, holds that jama'ah means three or more. Opponents cite several proofs, including hadiths and linguistic arguments, to claim that two suffice. The passage systematically refutes each proof, demonstrating how general texts are restricted by context (takhsis).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Positions
State the Hanafi position (minimum three) and the opposing claim (minimum two). Note the linguistic basis: Arabic plural (jama') is for three or more according to Hanafi usul.
2
List the Four Opposing Proofs
Extract from the source the four proofs: (1) Quranic dual 'qulubakuma', (2) hadith 'al-insanu fama fawqahuma jama'ah', (3) travel hadith, (4) first person plural pronoun 'na'.
The second proof is the most central.
3
Analyze Hanafi Response to Each Proof
For each proof, explain the Hanafi rebuttal: metaphor (majaz), specificity (takhsis) to inheritance/prayer/travel, and shared usage of the plural pronoun.
Focus on the principle that a general text can be specified by context.
4
Evaluate the Role of Takhsis
Understand that the Hanafi response relies on takhsis: the hadiths are not general but restricted to specific scenarios (inheritance, imam's positioning, travel). This preserves the linguistic consensus.
Takhsis prevents contradiction between the primary linguistic rule and revealed texts.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
State the thamarah al-khilaf: In Hanafi fiqh, congregational prayer requires at least three (imam + two followers); in the opposing view, two (imam + one) suffices.
This difference affects daily worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جواب دلیل ثانی: فقد صنعت قلوبکما پس قلوب سے مجاز آدو دل مراد لیے گئے ہیں اور یہ مجاز دو دل مراد لینے پر قرینہ یہ ہے کہ قلوب کی اضافت تثنیہ کی طرف کی گئی ہے تو دو افراد کے دل بھی دو ہوں گے تو معلوم ہوا یہاں مجازاً تثنیہ مراد ہے۔ اور مجاز ا تو جمع سے ایک فرد بھی مراد لیا جا سکتا ہے لھذا کوئی ذلیل نہیں ہے۔ جواب اول دلیل ثالث الانسان فما فوقهما جماعة، والی حدیث میراث اور وصیت کے بارے میں وارد ہوئی ہے اور میراث اور وصیت میں تو دو کے جمع میں داخل ہونے میں کوئی اختلاف نہیں ہے۔
جواب ثانی یا یہ جواب بھی دیا جاسکتا ہے کہ یہ حدیث اس بارے میں وارد ہوئی ہے کہ اگر امام کیساتھ نماز میں دو آدمی ہوں تو امام کے کھڑا ہونے کا طریقہ کیا ہے؟ تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ اس بارے میں دو آدمی جماعت کے حکم میں ہیں کہ جو طریقہ جماعت کیساتھ کھڑا ہونے کا ہے وہی دو آدمیوں کے ہوتے ہوئے بھی ہوگا۔ امام ایک صف مقتدیوں سے آگے کھڑا اسے آگے کی ہوگا نہ ایسے جیسے ایک آدمی کے ہوتے ہوئے کھڑا ہوتا ہے یعنی بائیں جانب ایک قدم آگے۔ تو یہ حدیث ایک خاص حالت کے بارے میں وارد ہوئی ہے نہ کہ مطلقاً اور ہم مطلقا کم از کم تین افراد مراد لینے کی بات کر رہے ہیں۔ جواب ثالث:۔ اور یہ جواب بھی دیا جا سکتا ہے کہ یہ حدیث سفر کے بارے میں وارد ہوتی ہے۔ کہ پہلے پہلے جب اسلام کو غلبہ نہیں ہوا تھا، ایک یا دو آدمیوں کو سفر کرنے کی اجازت نہیں تھی آپ کا فرمان ہے ' الواحد شيطان والاثنان شيطانان والثلاثة ركب ' لیکن جب اسلام کو غلبہ ہوا تو آپ نے دو کو بھی سفر کرنے کی اجازت دے دی۔ اور یہ فرمایا " الانسان فما فوقهما جماعة "، تو یہ حدیث خاص سفر کی حالت میں نازل ہوئی ہے نہ کہ مطلقا لھذا اس حدیث سے بھی استدلال کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ اور ہاں یہ تاویلیں ہم نے اس لیئے کی ہیں کہ اگر اس حدیث کو ظاہر پر محمول کریں تو اس میں اصل لغت کے اجماع کی مخالفت لازم آئے گی۔ جواب دلیل رابع : فعلنا جمع متکلم سے آپ کا دلیل پکڑنا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ نا ضمیر صرف جمع کیلئے وضع نہیں کی گئی بلکہ یہ مشترک ہے مفرد اور جمع دونوں کیلئے وضع کی گئی ہے اس لیئے اس سے جمع بھی مراد لیتے ہیں اور تثنیہ بھی مراد لیتے ہیں لھذا یہ دلیل بھی درست نہیں۔ یہ دلیل جب درست ہوتی جب نا ضمیر کی صرف جمع کیلئے وضع ہوتی اور اس سے مراد دو بھی لیے جاتے حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے۔
Answer to the second proof: 'Fasadana qulubakuma' – so from 'qulub' hearts are meant metaphorically, and the indication for taking it metaphorically as two hearts is that 'qulub' is added to a dual, so the hearts of two individuals are two. So it is known that here metaphorically the dual is meant. And metaphorically you can mean one individual from a plural, so that is not problematic. First answer to the third proof: 'al-insanu fama fawqahuma jama'ah' – this hadith came regarding inheritance and bequest, and in inheritance and bequest there is no disagreement that two enter into the plural. Second answer: Or it can be said that this hadith came regarding how the imam stands when two people are with him in prayer. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said that for this, two people are like a congregation in the manner of standing; the imam stands one row ahead of the followers, not like when there is one person (standing on the left side one step ahead). So this hadith is about a specific situation, not absolute, and we are speaking about absolute minimum of three. Third answer: Or it can be said that this hadith is about travel. Initially, when Islam had no dominance, one or two people were not allowed to travel. The Prophet said: 'al-wahidu shaytan, wal-ithnani shaytanan, wal-thalathatu rakb' but when Islam became dominant, he allowed two to travel and said: 'al-insanu fama fawqahuma jama'ah'. So this hadith was revealed specifically for travel, not absolutely. Therefore, using this hadith as proof is not correct. And we make these interpretations because if we take this hadith literally, it would contradict the consensus of the language regarding the original meaning. Answer to the fourth proof: Your argument from 'fa'alna' (first person plural) is not valid because the pronoun 'na' is not exclusively for plural; it is shared used for dual and plural. Therefore, from it we can mean plural and dual. So this proof is also not valid. It would be valid only if 'na' were exclusively for plural and only plural were meant, but that is not the case.
Source pages p. 600

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul al-fiqh dispute about the minimum number for a jama'ah (group). The author refutes four proofs that two people can form a jama'ah. First proof (from Qur'an 'fasadana qulubakuma'): The opponent argues the dual pronoun includes two hearts, implying two are a group. The author replies that 'qulub' (hearts) is a plural used metaphorically for dual, and metaphorically a plural can refer to one, so it's ambiguous. Second proof (hadith 'al-insanu fama fawqahuma jama'ah'): The author gives three answers: it's about inheritance/bequest where two being plural is undisputed; it's about prayer positioning of imam, a specific context; it's about travel, also specific. Third proof: another hadith about travel. Fourth proof: linguistic argument from the first person plural pronoun 'na'. The author says 'na' is shared between dual and plural, so it doesn't prove only plural. The author maintains the Hanafi position that the minimum for jama'ah is three, based on linguistic consensus.

Key Terms
جَمَاعَة (jama'ah): A group of people; in legal context, the minimum number for collective worship or rulings.
مَجَاز (majaz): Metaphorical usage of a word, where the literal meaning is not intended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi usul, what is the primary evidence that jama'ah requires at least three persons?
A) The hadith 'al-insanu fama fawqahuma jama'ah'
B) Linguistic consensus (ijma' of Arabs) that plural is for three or more
C) The Quranic verse 'fasadana qulubakuma'
D) Qiyas on the minimum for travel

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school maintains that jama'ah requires three individuals, and apparent hadiths to the contrary are restricted by context (takhsis) to specific situations.
